# CHANGELOG.md — QuantAgent v2

> All notable changes to this project.
> Format: date, what changed, test count.
> Updated by: Claude Code after each task.

---

## Week 3 — Conviction, Decision, Memory, Pipeline (April 6, 2026)

### 2026-04-12
- **CryptoFlowProvider PriceFeed integration — zero REST for funding/OI** — Wired [engine/data/flow/crypto.py](engine/data/flow/crypto.py) to read funding rate and open interest from PriceFeed WebSocket memory instead of making REST calls on every pipeline cycle. New optional ctor kwargs `price_feed` and `event_bus` (both default `None`, preserving back-compat with all 42 existing tests). New `set_price_feed(pf, bus)` public setter for late-binding — the shared `CryptoFlowProvider` is captured in `_make_bot_factory`'s closure before the PriceFeed exists, so main.py calls the setter after PriceFeed startup succeeds (`bot_factory.flow_provider.set_price_feed(price_feed, event_bus)` inside the PriceFeed startup block). **PriceFeed-first reads**: new `_read_funding(symbol, adapter)` and `_read_oi(symbol, adapter)` helpers try `price_feed.get_funding_rate(symbol)` / `price_feed.get_open_interest(symbol)` first; if the PriceFeed returns `None` (e.g. no WebSocket data for that symbol yet), the adapter's REST methods are called as an automatic fallback. Zero behavior change when `price_feed=None`. **OI history buffer from events**: new `_on_oi_update(event)` handler subscribes to `OpenInterestUpdated` events on the bus (when both `price_feed` and `event_bus` are wired). Each push appends to the per-symbol deque via the extracted `_record_oi_snapshot(symbol, oi_value, ts)` method, so the buffer fills continuously from WebSocket pushes (every few seconds from `activeAssetCtx` channel) rather than only from pipeline `fetch()` calls (once per Sentinel cycle). This eliminates the multi-hour cold-start warmup penalty after process restarts even without the OI snapshot table `warmup_from_repo()` path — the WebSocket fills the buffer in real-time from the first connection. `_record_oi_snapshot` was extracted from the inline OI block in the old `fetch()` — it handles both the in-memory deque append and the fire-and-forget `oi_repo.insert_snapshot()` persistence write. Both `fetch()` and `_on_oi_update` call it, so duplicate entries from both paths are expected — the deque is bounded by `maxlen` and `_compute_oi_delta` is time-based not count-based, so duplicates are harmless (the buffer just fills faster). **10 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_crypto_flow_price_feed.py](tests/unit/test_crypto_flow_price_feed.py) via `FakePriceFeed` (serves canned funding/OI per symbol) + `FakeAdapter` (records REST call counts): (1) funding from PriceFeed memory, adapter NOT called, (2) OI from PriceFeed memory, adapter NOT called, (3) `price_feed=None` falls back to REST (both adapter methods called), (4) mixed: funding from PriceFeed + OI from REST when PriceFeed has no OI for that symbol, (5) funding signal classification (`CROWDED_LONG`) works with PriceFeed source, (6) `OpenInterestUpdated` event populates the OI history buffer, (7) `oi_change_pct` computed correctly from pushed snapshots with three-entry buffer setup (old before cutoff + boundary entry after cutoff as `best_oi` + current observation), (8) buffer fills from events then `fetch()` uses it for delta (pre-seeded 2 entries at 1.0B, PriceFeed reads 1.05B → +5% BUILDING, zero REST calls), (9) `set_price_feed` wires OI event subscription post-construction, (10) `set_price_feed` idempotent (same feed twice is a no-op). Full `pytest -q` → **2035 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +10 net. **(2036 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 7 — Main.py wiring + shadow mode switchover** — Final integration task: wired `HyperliquidPriceFeed` + `RESTFallbackManager` + `SLTPMonitor` into [quantagent/main.py](quantagent/main.py) and [quantagent/runner.py](quantagent/runner.py) so shadow mode can run the entire PriceFeed stack via a single env var flip (`PRICE_FEED_ENABLED=true`). **Feature flag**: `PRICE_FEED_ENABLED` env var checked at `_run_server` startup; defaults to `"false"`. Also added `price_feed_enabled: false` to [config/features.yaml](config/features.yaml) (bumped the feature flag count test from 19 → 20 in [tests/unit/test_config.py](tests/unit/test_config.py)). The flag is double-gated: must be `"true"` AND the process must be in shadow mode (`--shadow` flag) — live and paper modes keep using the exchange's native SL/TP, so WebSocket PriceFeed is irrelevant for them. **Startup sequence**: PriceFeed is created BEFORE `BotRunner` so it can be passed via the new `price_feed=None` ctor kwarg on `BotRunner`. The runner threads it into every `SentinelMonitor(price_feed=...)` at construction time inside `_register_bot` and calls `sentinel.set_sl_tp_monitor_active(True)` when set. After `runner.start_with_bots(active_bots)`, main.py extracts the unique symbol set from the active bots, starts `fallback_manager.start(shadow_symbols)` (which calls `feed.connect()` + `feed.subscribe(symbols)` + REST bootstrap), registers every symbol on the `SLTPMonitor`, and starts it. The entire block is wrapped in try/except so a WebSocket connect failure is non-fatal — the sentinels still run and the scheduled fallback loops in BotRunner trigger analysis cycles at the configured interval regardless. **Bootstrap adapter**: `adapter_factory("hyperliquid", mode="live")` creates a live-mode adapter for the PriceFeed's REST history seeding. `fetch_ohlcv` on Hyperliquid is public data (no signing needed), so using `mode="live"` is correct even in a shadow process. The same adapter is passed to the `RESTFallbackManager` as the REST polling source. **Shutdown sequence**: SLTPMonitor → FallbackManager → OptionsEnrichment → EquityFlowProvider → BotRunner → uvicorn. SLTPMonitor stops first (unsubscribes from the bus), then the FallbackManager (cancels the REST poll task + disconnects the PriceFeed's WebSocket), then the existing flow provider cleanup, then the runner and server. **BotRunner** (`quantagent/runner.py`): gained `price_feed=None` ctor kwarg stored as `self._price_feed`. `_register_bot` passes it to `SentinelMonitor(price_feed=...)` and calls `set_sl_tp_monitor_active(True)` when set. All existing runner tests pass unchanged (they don't pass `price_feed`). **Deployment rollback**: flipping `PRICE_FEED_ENABLED=false` + restart instantly reverts to the legacy REST-poll path — the `price_feed_enabled` guard in `_run_server` skips the entire PriceFeed block. **Version bumped** MINOR `3.16.0 → 3.17.0` in [quantagent/version.py](quantagent/version.py) + [PROJECT_CONTEXT.md](PROJECT_CONTEXT.md) line 4. **5 new integration tests** in [tests/integration/test_price_feed_integration.py](tests/integration/test_price_feed_integration.py) via `FakePriceFeed` + `FakeAdapter` + `FakeRepos`: (1) runner with price_feed → sentinel receives it + sl_tp_monitor_active=True, (2) runner without price_feed → sentinel._price_feed is None + sl_tp_monitor_active=False, (3) SLTPMonitor starts with registered symbols, (4) CandleClosed on bus triggers Sentinel check (adapter.fetch_ohlcv NOT called), (5) graceful shutdown cleans up all components. Full `pytest -q` → **2025 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +5 net. **(2026 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 6 — Sentinel PriceFeed integration (event-driven mode)** — Wired [sentinel/monitor.py](sentinel/monitor.py) to optionally read from a PriceFeed instead of REST-polling the adapter. Three surgical edits, zero changes to readiness scoring / threshold logic / escalation / cooldown / SetupDetected emission. New `price_feed` ctor kwarg (default `None` preserves legacy path). When set, `run()` enters **event-driven mode**: subscribes to `CandleClosed` on the bus, and each candle close triggers `_on_candle_close(event)` which filters by symbol, reads candle history from `price_feed.get_candle_history(symbol, count=candle_window)`, and passes the pre-fetched candles to `_check_once(candles=...)` — ZERO `adapter.fetch_ohlcv()` calls. The run loop becomes a lightweight keepalive that handles day-boundary resets via `self._clock()`. **`_check_once(candles=None)`** gained a `candles` kwarg: when `None` (legacy) it fetches from adapter; when passed (event-driven) it skips the fetch entirely. All downstream logic (indicator computation, swing detection, funding read, readiness scoring, threshold gate, SetupDetected emission) is SHARED — the only thing that changes is WHERE candles come from. **Timestamp normalisation**: PriceFeed candles carry `datetime` objects while REST candles carry `int` ms. The candle-close-detection line that used `int(candles[-1]["timestamp"])` now does `isinstance(raw_ts, datetime) → int(ts.timestamp() * 1000)` so both formats produce the same int-ms comparison key. **`stop()`** now unsubscribes the `CandleClosed` handler when `price_feed` is set so a stopped Sentinel doesn't process stale events. **Back-compat is the hard constraint**: `price_feed=None` (default) preserves the existing `sleep(check_interval) → _check_once() → adapter.fetch_ohlcv()` REST-poll loop byte-for-byte. All 88 existing Sentinel tests pass unchanged. **7 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_sentinel_price_feed.py](tests/unit/test_sentinel_price_feed.py) via a `FakePriceFeed` (concrete subclass pre-populated with synthetic candles) + `StubAdapter` (records `fetch_ohlcv` calls to prove it's NOT called in event-driven mode): (1) CandleClosed triggers readiness computation + fires SetupDetected (threshold=0.0) + adapter NOT called, (2) wrong-symbol CandleClosed is silently ignored, (3) insufficient candles (10 < 35) skips check — no SetupDetected, (4) PriceFeed latest_price is readable from Sentinel's bound symbol, (5) price_feed=None uses REST (adapter.fetch_ohlcv_calls populated), (6) price_feed=None does NOT subscribe to CandleClosed (publishing one does nothing), (7) SetupDetected payload matches the REST-path format (source="sentinel", symbol, readiness as float, conditions as list). Full `pytest -q` → **2020 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +7 net. No version bump (per sprint plan — 3.17.0 at Task 7). **(2021 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 5 — SLTPMonitor (tick-level shadow SL/TP)** — New [engine/sl_tp_monitor.py](engine/sl_tp_monitor.py) houses `SLTPMonitor`, a `PriceUpdated` subscriber that resolves shadow SL/TP at the actual tick that breaches a level — replaces Sentinel's 30s candle-close `_check_shadow_sl_tp` poll which was missing intra-candle wicks. **Hot-path discipline** is the key invariant: `_on_price_update` does a single `_open_trades.get(symbol)` lookup; if there are no open trades for the symbol it returns immediately with zero DB calls, zero allocation, zero parse work. Only when at least one trade exists does it call the lazy `_maybe_refresh()` (default 10s interval — never per tick) and iterate the per-symbol list. Tests pin this contract — `test_no_trades_for_symbol_is_fast_path` baselines the `get_open_shadow_trades` call count and asserts a tick on an unrelated symbol adds zero. **Per-trade evaluation** mirrors Sentinel's `_resolve_shadow_trade` byte-for-byte for the directional gates (LONG: SL `price ≤ sl`, TP `price ≥ tp`; SHORT flipped) and the PnL formula (`(exit-entry)*size_usd/entry_price`) so the new tick path produces identical PnL to the legacy candle-close path on the same exit price. On a hit: closes via `repo.close_trade(...)`, flushes any improved `forward_max_r` via `repo.update_trade(trade_id, {"forward_max_r": ...})`, drops the trade from the in-memory map (so the next tick on the symbol short-circuits via the fast path), and emits `TradeClosed(source="sl_tp_monitor", trade_id, direction, entry_price, sl_price, ...)` on the bus with the full payload so downstream consumers like `ForwardMaxRStamper` can look the row back up. **forward_max_r tracking**: in-memory high-water mark per `trade_id` (updated on EVERY tick — cheap float arithmetic) and persisted ONLY at close. Seeds from the trade's persisted `forward_max_r` on first observation so a process restart picks up where the previous run left off; the final flush is skipped when the in-memory HWM didn't beat the prior persisted value (matches Sentinel's "strictly improves" semantics). **Refresh model**: per-symbol via `repo.get_open_shadow_trades(symbol)`, walking `_known_symbols` (union of every symbol the wiring has ever passed to `register_symbol(s)`). The repository contract is per-symbol only, so the monitor needs to be told which symbols to ask about — wiring point for `BotRunner` / `TradeOpened` handlers in Task 7. The very first `start()` refresh walks the empty set and the in-memory map only fills after the first `register_symbol` call. Transient DB errors during refresh PRESERVE the previous snapshot for the affected symbol so a single blip can't make the monitor forget open trades. **Sentinel integration**: new `set_sl_tp_monitor_active(active: bool)` on `SentinelMonitor` flips a `_sl_tp_monitor_active: bool = False` flag; when True, Sentinel skips its candle-close `_check_shadow_sl_tp` call so the two paths never resolve the same trade twice. The legacy path stays as LIVE code (not dead) because non-WebSocket deployments still need it — the flag is opt-in. The check is `self._trade_repo is not None and not self._sl_tp_monitor_active` so flipping the flag without unwiring the trade_repo cleanly disables the legacy path. **13 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_sl_tp_monitor.py](tests/unit/test_sl_tp_monitor.py) via a `FakeTradeRepo` that records every method call: 4 directional gates with PnL assertions (LONG SL `price=94.5 → exit=95 → pnl=-50`, LONG TP `price=110.5 → exit=110 → pnl=100`, SHORT SL `price=105.5 → exit=105 → pnl=-50`, SHORT TP `price=89.5 → exit=90 → pnl=100`), hot-path no-trades fast return (zero `get_open_shadow_trades` calls baselined), price-between-SL-and-TP no-action, `TradeClosed` event emission with full payload (`source="sl_tp_monitor"`, trade_id, direction, entry_price, sl_price), `forward_max_r` HWM tracking (4 ticks at 102/108/105/110 → in-memory HWM 0.4 → 1.6 → 1.6 → 2.0 with NO mid-trade `update_trade` calls then ONE flush at close), `forward_max_r` flush skipped when prior persisted (5.0) > new HWM (2.0), periodic refresh picks up freshly added trade after `refresh_interval=0.0` triggers every tick, refresh skipped within `refresh_interval=999.0` window (call count baselined), `start()` idempotency, `stop()` unsubscribes (post-stop ticks are no-ops). **Test bug worth flagging from review**: my first refresh test added a second trade with `entry=200` and tested with a tick at `105` — but `105 < 200` triggered the SL gate immediately (my fault, not the code). Fixed the fixture to use a wide `t1` (entry=100, sl=50, tp=150 — never hit) and a tight `t2` (entry=100, sl=98, tp=102) so the assertion is unambiguously about the refresh, not about a bonus SL hit. Full `pytest -q` → **2013 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +13 net. No version bump (per sprint plan — 3.17.0 at Task 7). **(2014 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 4 — RESTFallbackManager + PriceFeed disconnect callback** — New [engine/data/price_feed/fallback.py](engine/data/price_feed/fallback.py) houses `ConnectionState` (4-value enum: `CONNECTED` / `RECONNECTING` / `FALLBACK` / `DISCONNECTED`) and `RESTFallbackManager`, which wraps a `PriceFeed` + REST `ExchangeAdapter` so consumers downstream of the bus never see a data gap when the WebSocket dies. Also re-exported from [engine/data/price_feed/__init__.py](engine/data/price_feed/__init__.py). **Hooks added to the PriceFeed ABC** ([engine/data/price_feed/base.py](engine/data/price_feed/base.py)): `set_on_disconnect_callback(cb)`, `set_max_reconnect_attempts(n)`, plus an internal `_fire_on_disconnect()` helper that handles sync/async callbacks and swallows handler errors. Default `_max_reconnect_attempts=None` keeps the legacy retry-forever behaviour, so the existing 19 HL tests still pass byte-for-byte without changes. **HyperliquidPriceFeed `_inline_reconnect`** ([engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py](engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py)) now counts reconnect attempts within a single dropout cycle; once the count reaches `_max_reconnect_attempts` (set by the manager via `set_max_reconnect_attempts`), it fires the disconnect callback and returns, so the listen loop exits cleanly and the manager can take over. **State machine**: `start()` → tries `feed.connect()` + `feed.subscribe()`, on success records CONNECTED + freezes `_connect_time` for ws_uptime tracking; on initial failure jumps straight to FALLBACK. The disconnect callback handler records RECONNECTING in `_state_history`, increments `health["reconnect_count"]`, then immediately calls `_enter_fallback()` which records FALLBACK + spawns the REST poll task. **REST poll loop** runs at `rest_poll_interval=5.0` (intentionally tighter than the legacy 30s Sentinel poll because fallback is degraded mode); per-symbol calls `_poll_symbol(symbol)` which fetches OHLCV (limit=2), funding, and OI from the adapter, then routes them through `feed._update_price()` / `feed._complete_candle()` / `feed._update_funding()` / `feed._update_oi()` so the SAME `PriceUpdated` / `CandleClosed` / `FundingUpdated` / `OpenInterestUpdated` events fire on the bus that the WebSocket would have emitted — consumers can't tell where the data came from. Candle deduplication is per-manager via `_last_seen_candle_open_time[symbol]`, so REST polls emit exactly ONE `CandleClosed` per new candle even though the loop runs every 5s. Per-call failures are warning-logged-and-swallowed so a single rate limit doesn't kill the loop. **WS recovery**: every `ws_recovery_check_interval=30.0` seconds the REST loop calls `_try_ws_recovery()` which attempts a fresh `feed.connect()` + `feed.subscribe()`; on success the state moves to CONNECTED, `health["reconnect_count"]` increments, and the REST task exits cleanly. **`_stopped` flag vs state-based guards** (subtle bug worth flagging): the manager uses an explicit `_stopped: bool` (not `state == DISCONNECTED`) to gate `_enter_fallback` / `_on_ws_disconnect`. The first version used the state guard and broke the very first `start() → connect-fails → fallback` transition because the INITIAL state IS DISCONNECTED before `start()` runs — the guard early-returned. Tests caught this immediately. **`stop()`** flips `_stopped`, records DISCONNECTED, cancels the REST poll task, awaits its end, calls `feed.disconnect()`, and CLEARS the disconnect callback so a stray async fire from the feed after `stop()` can't reactivate the manager. Idempotent — second `stop()` is a no-op. **Spec deviation worth flagging**: spec said `_on_ws_disconnect` fires at the START of a disconnect (before retries) and the manager waits for the feed to retry; I fire it at the END (after retries are exhausted) so the manager doesn't need to poll `is_connected()` to detect retry success. The RECONNECTING state is recorded but transient — visible to tests via `state_history`, not a long-lived state. This matches the practical reality of the existing HyperliquidPriceFeed which already owns its own retry loop; refactoring to "manager-driven retries" would have meant rewriting `_inline_reconnect`. **8 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_rest_fallback.py](tests/unit/test_rest_fallback.py) via a `FakePriceFeed(PriceFeed)` (no WS plumbing — `connect_should_fail` toggles success/failure, `connect_calls` / `subscribe_calls` count invocations) + `FakeAdapter` (`ohlcv_responses` / `funding_responses` / `oi_responses` dicts, raises if mapped value is an Exception): (1) starts CONNECTED on connect success + wires callback + sets max_reconnect_attempts, (2) starts FALLBACK on initial connect failure, (3) RECONNECTING + FALLBACK both recorded in state_history when `_fire_on_disconnect()` is called, (4) REST poll emits Price/Funding/OI events via PriceFeed helpers + emits exactly 1 CandleClosed for the one new candle even though the poll loop runs multiple times, (5) WS recovery from FALLBACK → CONNECTED when next `feed.connect()` succeeds, (6) health metrics increment on each transition, (7) `stop()` cleanly cancels the poll task + disconnects the feed + clears the callback, (8) second `stop()` is idempotent. Full `pytest -q` → **2000 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test as Tasks 1-3). +8 net. No version bump (per sprint plan — 3.17.0 at Task 7). **(2001 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **HyperliquidPriceFeed — REST history bootstrap on subscribe** — Added `_bootstrap_history()` to [engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py](engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py) so the `completed_candles` deque is seeded with REST history before consumers start reading from it. Without this, Sentinel's 50-candle readiness window would block setup detection for ~50 hours after every restart on a 1h timeframe — the WebSocket only emits `CandleClosed` once per candle period. **Wiring**: new ctor kwargs `bootstrap_adapter: ExchangeAdapter | None = None` and `bootstrap_count: int = 100`. The adapter call goes through `subscribe()` for new symbols only (tracked via a `_bootstrapped_symbols: set[str]` so a re-`subscribe()` doesn't re-pull history). **Spec deviation worth flagging**: the task spec said to bootstrap "after WebSocket subscriptions are sent". I bootstrap **before** sending the WS subscribe frames instead — otherwise a fast WebSocket `CandleClosed` could append a fresh candle to the deque before the historical bars catch up, breaking the time ordering that Sentinel/Indicators depend on. The new `subscribe()` flow is: (1) register `SymbolState` + coin mapping for new symbols, (2) await `_bootstrap_history()` for those new symbols, (3) send the 3 WS subscribe frames per symbol. Inline comment in `subscribe()` explains the ordering. **Format normalisation**: `fetch_ohlcv` returns `{"timestamp": ms_int, "open", "high", "low", "close", "volume"}` while `_complete_candle` produces `{"timestamp": datetime, "timeframe": str, ...}`. New `_normalise_bootstrap_candle()` converts ms→datetime, adds the `timeframe` field, coerces all numerics to float, and returns `None` on unparseable rows so the bootstrap loop can skip-and-continue without crashing. **Side effect**: bootstrap also seeds `state.latest_price` from the most recent close if it's still `None`, so `get_latest_price()` returns a sane value before the first WS tick lands. **Failure handling**: per-symbol failures (`fetch_ohlcv` raises, returns empty, all rows malformed) are logged at WARNING and the loop continues with the next symbol — a single rate-limited 4xx for one symbol must not block the rest of the portfolio. The `WebSocket` is unaffected (`is_connected()` stays True). **Cleanup**: `unsubscribe()` now also drops the symbol from `_bootstrapped_symbols` so a fresh re-subscribe re-pulls history. **4 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_hyperliquid_price_feed.py](tests/unit/test_hyperliquid_price_feed.py) via a tiny `_StubAdapter` (responses dict + calls log): (1) bootstrap seeds the deque with the right count + format (datetime timestamp + timeframe field + ascending order + latest_price seeded), (2) BTC adapter raise + ETH adapter success → ETH still bootstrapped + feed stays connected, (3) `bootstrap_adapter=None` → no calls, deque empty, WS subscribe still fires, (4) WebSocket-flushed candle appends AFTER the 2 bootstrapped candles in time-order with exactly one `CandleClosed` event for the WS flush. Full `pytest -q` → **1992 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +4 net. No version bump. **(1993 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 3 — HyperliquidPriceFeed (real WebSocket implementation)** — Concrete `PriceFeed` subclass wrapping a single `wss://api.hyperliquid.xyz/ws` (or testnet) connection. New file [engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py](engine/data/price_feed/hyperliquid.py), re-exported from [engine/data/price_feed/__init__.py](engine/data/price_feed/__init__.py). `websockets>=12.0` was already in `pyproject.toml` from an earlier sprint — no dep change needed, version 16.0 installed. **Subscription model**: per symbol, sends 3 subscribe frames to the venue — `trades` (tick price), `candle` (OHLCV with a configurable `interval` defaulting to `1h`), `activeAssetCtx` (funding + open interest). Subscribe / unsubscribe go through a shared `_subscription_messages(coin, method=...)` helper so subscribe and unsubscribe use identical framing. **Symbol mapping** is the non-obvious bit: the sprint spec told us to do `coin = symbol.split("-")[0]` which breaks for aliased HIP-3 tokens — `WTIOIL-USDC` needs `xyz:CL`, not `xyz:WTIOIL`. I added a `resolve_coin` staticmethod that reads the public `exchanges.hyperliquid.SYMBOL_MAP`, splits the CCXT symbol's base part, and emits `xyz:{DEPLOYER_SUFFIX}` for HIP-3 tokens (`XYZ-GOLD → xyz:GOLD`, `XYZ-CL → xyz:CL`, `XYZ-SP500 → xyz:SP500`) or the raw base for native perps (`BTC`, `ETH`, `HYPE`). Unknown symbols still fall back to the split for forward compatibility. **Connection lifecycle**: ctor takes an optional `ws_connect` factory (defaults to `websockets.connect`) so tests inject a stub with zero monkey-patching. `connect()` opens via the factory, spawns `_listen()` as an `asyncio.Task`, flips `_connected=True`. `disconnect()` flips `_stop`, cancels the task, closes the ws, drops the reference. **Listen loop**: `async for raw in self._ws` routed to `_handle_message` which decodes bytes/str/dict, reads `channel`, dispatches to `_handle_trades` / `_handle_candle` / `_handle_active_asset_ctx`. Every handler wrapped in try/except so malformed frames (bad JSON, bad types, missing fields, non-numeric strings) log a warning and continue — never crashes the loop. Ack/heartbeat/error envelopes (`subscriptionResponse`, `pong`, `error`, None) are no-ops. **Candle close detection** is the subtle one: Hyperliquid pushes the SAME candle repeatedly with updated OHLC as ticks arrive — a candle is only "closed" when you receive a candle with a NEW open-time (`t`). The feed caches the building candle's open-time in `_building_candle_open_time[symbol]` and the full OHLCV snapshot in `SymbolState.building_candle`; when `t` advances, the PREVIOUS building candle gets flushed via `_complete_candle()` (which emits `CandleClosed` on the bus). `activeAssetCtx` computes `oi_change_pct` from the delta against the previous `SymbolState.open_interest` — None on the first observation. **Reconnection** is handled inline in `_listen` via `_inline_reconnect()` — exponential backoff (1s → 2s → ... capped at 60s), reopens ws, calls `_resubscribe_all()` to re-send every subscription frame for every symbol in `_subscribed_symbols`. Living inside the same listen task avoids the footgun of spawning a second listen task from inside the first on reconnect. Backoff reset happens only AFTER a successful reconnect + resubscribe, so tests overriding `_reconnect_delay` before calling `connect()` aren't stomped by `_open_ws`. **15 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_hyperliquid_price_feed.py](tests/unit/test_hyperliquid_price_feed.py) — all against a `FakeWebSocket` async iterator (supports `push(frame)` for inbound, `fail()` to raise `ConnectionClosed`, `close()`, and a `sent` list to inspect outbound frames). Coverage: 4 symbol-mapping tests (native / straight HIP-3 / WTIOIL regression / unknown fallback), 2 subscribe tests (3 frames per symbol with correct type/coin/interval + HIP-3 coin shape), 3 trades tests (PriceUpdated with ms→datetime conversion, unsubscribed-coin filter, malformed entries skipped), 1 candle close detection (first-observe = building, same open-time = refresh, new open-time = flush + emit + append to history deque), 1 activeAssetCtx test (both FundingUpdated + OpenInterestUpdated, oi_change_pct None on first then 0.01 on +1% OI), 1 malformed-message test (bad JSON + unknown channel + sub ack all no-op), 1 reconnect test (fail ws_a → reopens ws_b → resubscribes all 3 frames), 1 unsubscribe test (3 unsubscribe frames + state dropped), 1 disconnect test. Zero real network. Full `pytest -q` → **1988 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (same macro-regime test). +15 net. No version bump (per sprint plan). **(1989 total tests)**

### 2026-04-12
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 2 — PriceFeed ABC + SymbolState container** — Abstract base class for real-time exchange data feeds. New package [engine/data/price_feed/](engine/data/price_feed/) with `__init__.py` re-exporting `PriceFeed` + `SymbolState`, and [engine/data/price_feed/base.py](engine/data/price_feed/base.py) housing the two types. **SymbolState** is a `@dataclass` per subscribed symbol: `latest_price`, `latest_bid`, `latest_ask`, `building_candle`, `completed_candles: deque(maxlen=500)` (via `field(default_factory=...)` — deques can't be assigned by `=` in a dataclass body), `funding_rate`, `open_interest`, `last_update`. The 500-candle window comfortably covers Sentinel's 50-candle readiness scorer + any parent-TF lookbacks while staying cheap on memory. **PriceFeed(ABC)** owns the state container and event emission; subclasses own the WebSocket plumbing and venue-specific parsing. Abstract async methods: `connect`, `disconnect`, `_listen`, `subscribe`, `unsubscribe`. Concrete **reads** (sync, zero-network): `get_latest_price`, `get_latest_candle`, `get_candle_history(count)`, `get_funding_rate`, `get_open_interest`, `get_symbol_state`, `is_connected`, plus `exchange_name` / `subscribed_symbols` properties. Concrete **mutators** (async): `_update_price(symbol, price, bid, ask, size, timestamp)` updates state + emits `PriceUpdated`; `_complete_candle(symbol, timeframe, open, high, low, close, volume, timestamp)` appends a dict to the deque + emits `CandleClosed`; `_update_funding(symbol, rate, next_funding_time, timestamp)` emits `FundingUpdated`; `_update_oi(symbol, oi, change_pct, timestamp)` emits `OpenInterestUpdated`. All four route through a shared `_publish()` helper that wraps `bus.publish()` in try/except so a bus-level failure never crashes the WebSocket receive loop (matches the `TrackingModule._safe()` pattern). **Design nuances worth keeping**: (1) `_ensure_state()` lazy-inits a `SymbolState` on first tick even if the subclass forgot to call `subscribe()` first — WebSocket races where the first tick beats the subscription ack would otherwise silently drop data. (2) `_update_price` with no bid/ask keeps the previous bid/ask on the state (partial ticks are common on the trades channel). (3) `_complete_candle` only seeds `latest_price` from `close` when no live tick has arrived yet — a historical candle replay must not rewind a live tick. (4) `get_candle_history(count)` materialises `list(deque)` once and tail-slices because `deque` doesn't support slice syntax. (5) Source strings on emitted events are `"price_feed:{exchange_name}"` so downstream tracking can attribute a tick to its venue. **26 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_price_feed_base.py](tests/unit/test_price_feed_base.py) via a `StubPriceFeed` subclass: per-mutator state assertions + event emission, deque `maxlen=500` enforcement (pushes 600 candles, asserts oldest survivor is index 100), `_update_price` partial-tick preservation of bid/ask, lazy state-init on unsubscribed symbol, candle close vs live price ordering (seed if empty, never overwrite), every `get_*` method returns None / `[]` for unknown symbols, `get_candle_history` count semantics (exact/exceed/zero), unsubscribe drops state, `connect`/`disconnect` toggles `is_connected`, and a `pytest.raises(TypeError)` check confirming the bare `PriceFeed` ABC can't be instantiated. Zero existing file modifications. Full `pytest -q` → **1973 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (`test_mcp/test_macro_regime/test_runner.py::test_check_mode_trigger_escalates_to_deep`, unrelated). No version bump (per sprint plan — 3.17.0 at Task 7). **(1974 total tests)**

### 2026-04-11
- **Sprint Week 7 Task 1 — PriceFeed event types + payload dataclasses** — Foundation for the event-driven WebSocket PriceFeed refactor (Phase 1). Added 4 payload dataclasses in [engine/types.py](engine/types.py): `PriceUpdate` (symbol/price/bid/ask/size/exchange/timestamp — emitted per tick from the Hyperliquid `trades` channel), `CandleClose` (symbol/timeframe/OHLCV/exchange/timestamp — emitted when a candle finalises on the `candle` channel), `FundingUpdate` (symbol/funding_rate/next_funding_time/exchange/timestamp — from `activeAssetCtx`), `OIUpdate` (symbol/open_interest/oi_change_pct/exchange/timestamp — from `activeAssetCtx`). Each dataclass has a `to_dict()` method matching the existing pattern and defaults `timestamp` via `field(default_factory=lambda: datetime.now(timezone.utc))` (required because Python can't have a non-default positional field after defaulted fields). New `from datetime import datetime, timezone` import at the top of types.py. Added 4 `Event` subclasses in [engine/events.py](engine/events.py): `PriceUpdated` (wraps `PriceUpdate`), `CandleClosed` (wraps `CandleClose`), `FundingUpdated` (wraps `FundingUpdate`), `OpenInterestUpdated` (wraps `OIUpdate`). Each wraps its corresponding payload via the same `field(default_factory=lambda: None)  # type: ignore[arg-type]` trick `DataReady` / `ConvictionScored` already use. **Interpretation note**: the sprint spec said "add EventType enum values" but this codebase uses class-based dispatch (`bus.subscribe(DataReady, handler)`), not a string enum — followed existing architecture and skipped the enum so `SLTPMonitor.subscribe(PriceUpdated, …)` in Task 5 works out-of-the-box instead of dead code. **13 new tests** in [tests/unit/test_price_feed_types.py](tests/unit/test_price_feed_types.py): per-dataclass required-fields instantiation, all-fields populated, `to_dict()` round-trip with timestamp preservation, optional-field default verification, UTC timezone default assertion, and 4 event-wrapper tests verifying the Event subclass carries the payload by identity. Zero existing file modifications beyond the additive imports. Full `pytest -q` → **1947 passed, 1 pre-existing fail** (`test_mcp/test_macro_regime/test_runner.py::test_check_mode_trigger_escalates_to_deep` — unrelated to types/events, does not touch any file I edited). No version bump (per sprint spec — version bumps to 3.17.0 at Task 7). **(1948 total tests)**

### 2026-04-11
- **FINRA RegSHO EquityFlowProvider + 4 new FlowSignalAgent rules** — New `engine/data/flow/equity.py` houses `EquityFlowProvider(FlowProvider)` pulling daily pipe-delimited RegSHO short-volume files from `https://cdn.finra.org/equity/regsho/daily/CNMSshvol{YYYYMMDD}.txt`. **Scope**: `TSLA-USDC`, `NVDA-USDC`, `GOOGL-USDC` only — every other symbol returns `{}` immediately. Verified the CDN URL + format against live FINRA data before coding (FINRA deprecated the old `regsho.finra.org/CNMSshvol…` URL some time ago; the new cdn.finra.org path is the current one). **20-day rolling history**: per-symbol ascending list of `(trade_date, short_volume, total_volume, short_volume_ratio)` dicts; `_compute_metrics` runs Z-score (excluding the most recent entry to avoid self-reference) and 5-day-vs-20-day trend classification off the tail. **Refresh loop**: `_maybe_refresh()` pulls the newest trading-day file via injectable `httpx.AsyncClient` (tests stub with `MockTransport`, never hit the network), walking backwards up to 5 weekdays if today's 404s (handles weekends, holidays, pre-publish early fetches). Guarded by `asyncio.Lock` so the three equity bots concurrently scanning Sentinel cause ONE HTTP pull. Fetch failures are logged-and-swallowed — the provider keeps serving cached history. **Market hours helper**: stdlib `zoneinfo` (no pytz dep) — `_is_us_market_open(now)` returns True Mon-Fri 9:30–16:00 ET; `market_open` is populated for every equity fetch regardless of whether the FINRA file loaded, so the "outside market hours" rule can fire without any RegSHO data. **Persistence**: new `RegSHOCacheRepository` abstract interface + PG/SQLite implementations (`upsert` idempotent via `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`, `get_recent` ascending by `trade_date`, `cleanup_older_than_days`). New `regsho_cache` table (composite PK `(symbol, trade_date)` + `ix_regsho_cache_symbol_date` index). Alembic **007** migration. **FlowOutput**: 4 new optional fields — `short_volume_ratio`, `svr_zscore`, `svr_trend`, `market_open` — all default `None`/`None` so existing call sites keep working. `FlowAgent._fetch_and_merge` merges the new keys. **Wiring**: `quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory` creates the shared `EquityFlowProvider(regsho_repo=repos.regsho_cache)` alongside crypto + options + commodity providers; `_run_server` awaits `equity_provider.warmup_from_repo()` before bot spawns and `close()`s the httpx client on graceful shutdown. **FlowSignalAgent rules** (run AFTER options + COT blocks, BEFORE funding/OI block — 4 new rules): (1) `svr_zscore > 2.0` → BEARISH @ 0.55 (extreme short volume), (2) `svr_zscore > 2.0` AND price up > 1% over 12 candles AND `svr_trend == "RISING"` → BULLISH @ 0.60 (short squeeze setup — wins priority over rule 1 when both fire), (3) `svr_zscore < -1.5` → BULLISH @ 0.50 (short volume collapse), (4) `market_open is False` → NEUTRAL @ 0.40 (outside market hours caution). Non-equity symbols keep every `svr_*` / `market_open` field `None` so all four rules short-circuit cleanly and the crypto funding/OI block runs unchanged. Docstring rewritten to document the full 18-rule pipeline order. **49 new tests**: 6 `RegSHOCacheRepository` tests (upsert roundtrip, replace-on-conflict, ascending order, symbol filter, limit, cleanup), 34 `EquityFlowProvider` tests (symbol gating crypto/unknown/equity-gets-market-open, FINRA parser with valid rows / target tickers / noise / malformed / empty, metric computation Z-score edge cases including flat-history guard / nearly-flat measurable / trend RISING/FALLING/STABLE, 7 market-hours tests with deterministic ET datetimes, 5 trading-day-helper tests, 6 warmup/persistence tests including walks-backwards-on-404 + refresh-deduped-within-same-day + FINRA-failure-falls-back-to-cache), 8 FlowSignalAgent RegSHO rule tests (one per new rule + squeeze wins over plain extreme-short when both fire + squeeze requires price up + market_open=True doesn't trigger closed rule + non-equity fall-through), 1 Alembic 007 shape test, 1 schema-parity update. Engine version bumped MINOR `3.15.0 → 3.16.0`. Full `pytest -q --ignore=tests/test_mcp` → **1720 passed** (+49 net), zero regressions. **(1933 total tests)**

### 2026-04-11
- **CFTC COT CommodityFlowProvider + 4 new FlowSignalAgent rules** — New `engine/data/flow/commodity.py` houses `CommodityFlowProvider(FlowProvider)` pulling weekly Commitment of Traders data from the CFTC via the `cot_reports` library (added to `pyproject.toml`). **Scope**: `GOLD-USDC`, `SILVER-USDC`, `WTIOIL-USDC`, `BRENTOIL-USDC` only — every other symbol (crypto, FX, equity) returns `{}` immediately. Canonical CFTC contract names matched via ordered substring patterns so a CFTC rename doesn't break anything. **52-week rolling buffer**: in-memory `dict[symbol, list[dict]]` holds up to 52 weekly snapshots ascending by report_date; `_compute_metrics` runs percentile / divergence / weekly-change math off the tail. **Refresh loop**: `_maybe_refresh()` checks every commodity's newest row against a 7-day cutoff; if any is stale the provider spawns a single `asyncio.to_thread(cot_year, ..., "disaggregated_fut")` call, extracts the highest-OI row per target pattern, writes back to both in-memory history and `cot_cache` table. `cot_reports` is imported lazily inside the refresh so a missing dependency or a CFTC 503 is logged-and-swallowed — the provider falls back to whatever DB-cached history it already has. Concurrent refresh is guarded by `asyncio.Lock` so 4 commodity bots hitting Sentinel at the same second cause ONE CFTC pull, not four. **Persistence**: new `COTCacheRepository` abstract interface + PG/SQLite implementations with `upsert(symbol, report_date, ...)` (idempotent via `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE`), `get_recent(symbol, limit=52)` (ascending by date), `cleanup_older_than_weeks(weeks)`. New `cot_cache` table (composite PK on `(symbol, report_date)` + `ix_cot_cache_symbol_date` index). **Alembic 006**: new migration creates the table and index. **FlowOutput**: 6 new optional fields — `cot_speculator_percentile`, `cot_commercial_net`, `cot_managed_money_net`, `cot_weekly_change_pct`, `cot_divergence`, `cot_divergence_abs_percentile` — all default `None` so existing call sites keep working. `FlowAgent._fetch_and_merge` merges the new keys. **Wiring**: `quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory` creates the shared `CommodityFlowProvider(cot_repo=repos.cot_cache)` alongside the crypto + options providers and threads it into every `FlowAgent`; `_run_server` awaits `commodity_provider.warmup_from_repo()` before any bot spawns so the 52-week history is live on cycle #1. **FlowSignalAgent rules** (run AFTER options block, BEFORE funding/OI block — 4 new rules): (1) `cot_speculator_percentile > 90` → BEARISH @ 0.55 (extreme speculator long), (2) `cot_speculator_percentile < 10` → BULLISH @ 0.55 (extreme speculator short), (3) `cot_divergence > 0 AND cot_divergence_abs_percentile > 80 AND cot_speculator_percentile < 30` → BULLISH @ 0.60 (follow the hedgers), (4) `cot_divergence < 0 AND cot_divergence_abs_percentile > 80 AND cot_speculator_percentile > 70` → BEARISH @ 0.60 (smart money exiting). Non-commodity symbols keep every `cot_*` field `None` so all four rules short-circuit cleanly and the existing funding/OI block runs unchanged. Docstring rewritten to document the full 14-rule pipeline order. **39 new tests**: 6 COTCacheRepository tests (upsert roundtrip, replace-on-conflict, ascending order, symbol filter, limit, cleanup), 26 CommodityFlowProvider tests (symbol gating crypto/unknown/empty, metric computation with 10-point and 2-point histories, percentile helper edge cases, warmup from DB, warmup no-repo, fetch after warmup, library failure falls back to cache, refresh persists new rows, refresh skipped when history fresh, DataFrame parser with pattern match / no match / highest-OI tiebreaker), 8 FlowSignalAgent COT rule tests (extreme long BEARISH, extreme short BULLISH, commercial divergence BULLISH / BEARISH, BTC fall-through, middle percentile fall-through, divergence-not-extreme, extreme-long priority over divergence), 1 Alembic 006 shape test, 1 SQLite schema-parity update. Engine version bumped MINOR `3.14.0 → 3.15.0`. Full `pytest -q --ignore=tests/test_mcp` → **1671 passed** (+39 net), zero regressions. **(1884 total tests)**

### 2026-04-11
- **Deribit OptionsEnrichment provider + 6 new FlowSignalAgent rules** — New `engine/data/flow/options.py` houses `OptionsEnrichment(FlowProvider)` fetching `put_call_ratio`, `dvol`, `dvol_change_24h`, `skew_25d`, and `gex_regime` from Deribit's public API (`get_book_summary_by_currency` + `get_volatility_index_data`). **Scope**: BTC-USDC / ETH-USDC only — every other symbol short-circuits to an empty dict so altcoins never pay the network round-trip. **Caching**: 15-minute per-symbol TTL via a simple `{symbol: (expires_at, data)}` map; well under the 20 req/sec Deribit rate limit even with 22 Sentinel symbols scanning every 30s. **Robustness**: each sub-call (book summary, DVOL) is independently try/excepted so a partial outage still surfaces whatever data it can; total-outage returns an empty dict and the pipeline keeps running. **Parsers**: pure static methods (`_parse_book_summary`, `_parse_dvol`) so tests can hit them with hand-built fixture dicts without any HTTP plumbing. PCR from summed call/put OI; approximate 25-delta skew picks the strikes ~7% OTM from spot on each side of the nearest-monthly expiry (full BS interpolation is roadmap); GEX classification sums `oi * gamma * contract_size * underlying_price` across all instruments and reports `POSITIVE_GAMMA` / `NEGATIVE_GAMMA` by sign (returns `None` when no gamma is in the summary). **FlowOutput**: new optional fields `put_call_ratio`, `dvol`, `dvol_change_24h`, `skew_25d` (all default `None` so existing call sites keep working). **FlowAgent**: `_fetch_and_merge` merges the options fields alongside funding/OI. **Wiring**: `quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory` creates a single `OptionsEnrichment()` shared across all bot spawns (same pattern as `CryptoFlowProvider`), passes both to every `FlowAgent` via `[crypto, options]`, and stashes the instance on `factory.options_provider`. `_run_server` calls `options_provider.close()` on graceful shutdown to release the httpx client. **FlowSignalAgent**: 6 new rules run BEFORE the funding/OI block so options data (more informative than funding alone) wins when present: (1) bearish hedging — PCR > 1.2 → BEARISH @ 0.60, (2) complacent longs — PCR < 0.5 → BEARISH @ 0.55, (3) extreme skew — skew_25d > 10 → BEARISH @ 0.55, (4) vol spike — dvol_change_24h > 20% → NEUTRAL @ 0.55, (5) positive gamma pinning — `gex_regime == POSITIVE_GAMMA` → NEUTRAL @ 0.50, (6) negative gamma confidence boost — when `gex_regime == NEGATIVE_GAMMA`, the divergence / accumulation rules' confidence gets +0.10 (capped at 0.80). Rules for non-BTC/ETH symbols are unchanged (all options fields are `None` → every options rule short-circuits and the funding/OI block runs normally). Docstring at the top of `signal_agent.py` rewritten to document the new pipeline order (10 rules total: 5 options + 4 funding/OI + 1 default NEUTRAL). **32 new tests**: 24 OptionsEnrichment tests (symbol gating, book-summary parsing for PCR / GEX / skew / malformed rows, DVOL parsing, error handling across both endpoints, 15-minute cache hit / expiry / per-symbol isolation, identity) + 10 FlowSignalAgent options-rule tests (one per new rule + priority test + threshold-edge test + fall-through test for non-BTC/ETH symbols). Engine version bumped MINOR `3.13.0 → 3.14.0`. Full `pytest -q --ignore=tests/test_mcp` → **1632 passed** (+32 net), zero regressions. **(1845 total tests)**

- **Persistent OI snapshots + configurable lookback** — `CryptoFlowProvider` is now wired to a new `OISnapshotRepository` so the per-symbol rolling deque survives process restarts. **Persistence**: New abstract `OISnapshotRepository` (`insert_snapshot` ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, `get_recent_snapshots(lookback_seconds)` returning ascending rows, `cleanup_older_than(seconds)`). PostgreSQL + SQLite implementations land in [storage/repositories/postgres.py](storage/repositories/postgres.py) + [sqlite.py](storage/repositories/sqlite.py); both add the `oi_snapshots(symbol, timestamp, oi_value)` table with `(symbol, timestamp)` primary key and `ix_oi_snapshots_symbol_time` index. New Alembic migration `005_oi_snapshots.py`. The container exposes `repos.oi_snapshots`. The provider's `warmup_from_repo()` bulk-loads `1.5×lookback_seconds` of recent snapshots on startup (the over-fetch ensures the oldest entry is provably older than the cold-start cutoff so the very first post-warmup `fetch()` can compute deltas immediately). Each fetch fires an idempotent `insert_snapshot()` to mirror the in-memory append; DB blips are logged-and-swallowed so the data layer keeps working. **Configurable lookback**: New `lookback_seconds` constructor arg + `set_lookback_for_timeframe(tf)` helper mapping `15m→30min`, `30m→1h`, `1h→2h`, `4h→8h`, `1d→48h`. Default is 2h (down from the hardcoded 4h that left 1h-bot divergence signals two candles stale). Deque maxlen scales as `max(60, lookback_seconds // 30)`. The 2% trend threshold is unchanged on purpose — a 2% move in 2h is a stronger signal than 2% in 4h, which naturally raises the bar for shorter windows. The `oi_change_4h` field name is preserved for backward compatibility; the docstring clarifies it's now a generic delta over the configured window. **Wiring**: `quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory` constructs the shared `CryptoFlowProvider(oi_repo=repos.oi_snapshots)`, calls `set_lookback_for_timeframe("1h")`, and stashes the instance on `factory.flow_provider`. `_run_server` awaits `bot_factory.flow_provider.warmup_from_repo()` before any bot spawns and launches an hourly background task that calls `cleanup_older_than(86_400)` to keep the table small. The cleanup task is cancelled cleanly on graceful shutdown. 18 new tests: 5 OISnapshotRepository tests (insert/recent roundtrip, ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING, lookback filtering, cleanup, ordering), 5 CryptoFlowProvider lookback tests (default/explicit/per-timeframe/unknown-tf-fallback/reset-history-on-set), 6 persistence tests (warmup load, no-repo no-op, swallowed warmup errors, fetch persists, swallowed fetch errors, warmup-then-fetch yields immediate delta), 1 migration shape test, schema-parity test updated for `oi_snapshots`. Engine version bumped MINOR `3.12.2 → 3.13.0`. Full `pytest -q --ignore=tests/test_mcp` → **1600 passed** (+18 net), zero regressions. **(1813 total tests)**

- **Share CryptoFlowProvider across bot spawns** — `quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory` now constructs a single `CryptoFlowProvider()` once at the outer scope and the inner `factory(...)` closure passes it into every spawned bot's `FlowAgent`. Previously the inner closure built `FlowAgent([CryptoFlowProvider()])` on every spawn, so each hourly TraderBot started with an empty per-symbol OI history `deque(maxlen=480)` — the cold-start path never ended and FlowSignalAgent's BUILDING / DROPPING / divergence rules stayed permanently dormant in production. The provider's OI buffer is keyed per-symbol internally, so one shared instance correctly accumulates 4-hour windows across all 22 symbols. Engine version bumped PATCH `3.12.1 → 3.12.2`. **(1582 tests, no regressions)**

- **Shadow default balance 10k → 100k** — `exchanges/factory.py::_DEFAULT_SHADOW_BALANCE` raised so 22 symbols × $500 fixed shadow trades have headroom for many concurrent positions without artificial fill blocking from the simulated wallet running dry. - **Shadow data-collection: deterministic conviction + PRM bypass + DB-backed SL/TP monitoring** — Three-part change so shadow-mode signal-quality data collection actually produces measurable PnL. **Part 1 (deterministic conviction)**: `engine/conviction/agent.py` calls the LLM at `temperature=0.0` instead of `0.3` — ConvictionAgent is an evaluator, not a creative writer, and the previous sampling temperature was producing 0.25–0.65 spreads on identical signal patterns. 2 new tests pin the contract. **Part 2 (PRM bypass)**: `AnalysisPipeline` accepts a new `shadow_fixed_size_usd: float | None` constructor arg. When set AND the action is an entry, the pipeline stamps `position_size = shadow_fixed_size_usd` and skips PRM entirely so per-asset / portfolio exposure caps cannot starve the dataset (shadow positions accumulate until the new SL/TP monitor closes them). `_make_bot_factory` wires `500.0` only when `shadow_mode` is true — paper mode keeps PRM active because PRM validation is the whole point of paper. 4 new tests cover bypass + persistence + non-shadow no-op + failed-order skip. **Part 3 (Sentinel SL/TP monitor)**: New Alembic migration `004_trade_sl_tp_columns.py` adds `sl_price` + `tp_price` to the `trades` table, mirrored in the SQLite + Postgres CREATE TABLE DDLs. New `TradeRepository.get_open_shadow_trades(symbol)` and `close_trade(id, exit_price, exit_reason, exit_time, pnl)` interface methods land on both backends. New `AnalysisPipeline.record_trade_open(action, order_result)` persists a freshly opened shadow trade with full SL/TP/conviction/engine_version context — TraderBot calls it immediately after the executor returns a successful entry fill. `BotRunner` now passes `repos.trades` to `SentinelMonitor` in shadow mode; `SentinelMonitor._check_once()` invokes `_check_shadow_sl_tp(latest_candle)` which queries open shadow trades, closes any whose SL/TP falls inside [low, high] (SL takes precedence), computes per-direction PnL via `(exit-entry)*size_usd/entry_price`, and updates `forward_max_r` whenever the favourable extreme exceeds the prior best. Logs `Shadow trade OPENED:` and `Shadow trade CLOSED:` lines for the audit trail. Live + paper modes get `trade_repo=None` and the monitor is a no-op. 13 new tests across repo + sentinel cover LONG/SHORT × SL/TP, no-breach, SL-precedence, no-repo no-op, forward_max_r tracking, close-trade idempotency, shadow-row filtering, sl_price/tp_price persistence. Migration parity test updated for the two new columns; new test pins the 004 migration file shape. Engine version bumped MINOR `3.11.0 → 3.12.0`. Full `pytest -q --ignore=tests/test_mcp` → **1582 passed** (+19 net), zero regressions on changed surfaces. **(1795 total tests)**

### 2026-04-10
- **Shadow mode SL/TP triggering via shared adapter + Sentinel candle feed** — Three-part fix so virtual positions in shadow mode actually close when price hits stop-loss or take-profit levels. **Part 1 (shared adapter)**: `BotRunner._register_bot()` now stores the adapter it creates for Sentinel in `self._adapters[symbol]` and registers it with `BotManager.set_adapter_for_symbol()`. `BotManager._run_bot()` and `spawn_bot()` pass the override to the factory via `adapter_override` kwarg. `_make_bot_factory`'s inner closure accepts `adapter_override` — if provided, uses it instead of calling `adapter_factory()`. This ensures the pipeline and Sentinel operate on the same `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` instance (positions opened by the pipeline are visible to Sentinel's candle feed). No-op in live mode (real adapters don't need sharing). **Part 2 (Sentinel candle feed)**: `sentinel/monitor.py::_check_once()` now calls `adapter.set_current_candle(symbol, candles[-1])` after fetching candles if the adapter has the method (`hasattr` guard). This triggers SL/TP checks against the candle's high/low on the sim adapter. SL takes priority over TP when both are hit in the same candle (existing `_check_sl_tp_triggers` behavior). No-op on real adapters. **Part 3 (already verified)**: `SimulatedExchangeAdapter.set_current_candle()` already checks `low ≤ sl_price` and `high ≥ tp_price` (not just close) — confirmed from backtesting. 10 new tests: SL triggered by candle low, TP triggered by candle high, SL wins when both hit same candle, no trigger when within range, shared adapter end-to-end (pipeline opens → Sentinel triggers SL), real adapter has no set_current_candle, adapter override passed to factory, no override passes None, factory uses override identity, factory without override creates new. Version bumped MINOR `3.10.2 → 3.11.0`. Full `pytest -q` → **1776 passed** (1766 → 1776, +10 net), zero regressions. **(1776 total)**

- **Fix scheduled loop consuming Sentinel cooldown** — `BotManager.spawn_bot()` now accepts `source: str = "sentinel"` parameter. When `source="scheduled"` (set by `BotRunner._scheduled_loop`), `SetupResult` event emission is skipped so the hourly fallback loop doesn't ratchet Sentinel's escalation threshold or consume cooldown. Sentinel-triggered spawns (default `source="sentinel"`) still emit normally. Fixes the production issue where Sentinel logged "readiness above threshold but cooldown/budget prevents trigger" because scheduled SKIPs had consumed the cooldown. 4 new tests: scheduled spawn skips SetupResult, sentinel spawn still emits, scheduled TRADE also skips, default source is sentinel.
