- **Pipeline: feed current price to SimulatedExchangeAdapter before execution** — `engine/pipeline.py::run_cycle()` now calls `adapter.set_current_prices({symbol: close_price})` after Stage 1 data fetch, if the adapter has the method. This primes the `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` with the current market price so `place_market_order()` can simulate fills in shadow mode. No-op on real adapters (they don't have `set_current_prices`). The adapter reference is `self._ohlcv._adapter`, which is the same instance the `Executor` uses (both wired from the same object in `_make_bot_factory`). Fixes the "No current price for {symbol}" `ValueError` that shadow-mode bots hit when the pipeline produced an entry action. 1 new integration test: `TestSimAdapterPriceFeed` verifies the price is fed. Version bumped PATCH `3.10.0 → 3.10.1`. **(1762 tests)**

- **CryptoFlowProvider: per-symbol rolling OI history buffer** — `engine/data/flow/crypto.py` now maintains a per-symbol in-memory `deque(maxlen=480)` of `(timestamp, oi_value)` snapshots. On each `fetch()` call, after fetching current OI from the exchange adapter, the snapshot is appended and a 4h delta is computed from the oldest entry within the lookback window. `oi_change_4h` is now populated as a fractional delta (e.g. -0.03 = -3%) and `oi_trend` is derived as "BUILDING" (>+2%), "DROPPING" (<-2%), or "STABLE". During the cold-start warmup (buffer < 4h of data) both stay `None`/"STABLE" — FlowSignalAgent handles `None` correctly. This activates FlowSignalAgent's BEARISH-divergence and BULLISH-accumulation rules in production, which were permanently dormant. Buffer is per-provider-instance, keyed by symbol. Logs `INFO` when buffer first reaches 4h depth. 8 new tests: cold start, warmup, delta computation, BUILDING/DROPPING/STABLE classification, maxlen enforcement, multi-symbol independence. Engine version bumped MINOR `3.9.1 → 3.10.0`. Full `pytest -q` → **1761 passed** (1753 → 1761, +8 net), zero regressions. **(1761 total)**

- **Fix HIP-3 funding rate + OI symbol mapping in HyperliquidAdapter** — `get_funding_rate` and `get_open_interest` now use Hyperliquid's direct info API via httpx instead of CCXT, which couldn't resolve HIP-3 coin names for these endpoints (CCXT worked fine for OHLCV). New `_build_asset_registry()` fetches native perps meta (`POST /info {"type":"meta"}`) and HIP-3 perps meta (`POST /info {"type":"meta","dex":"xyz"}`), builds a `_coin_map` mapping canonical symbols to HL coin names (e.g. `GOLD-USDC → xyz:GOLD`, `WTIOIL-USDC → xyz:CL`), cached 24h with lazy init. Static fallback from `_STATIC_COIN_MAP` (derived from existing `SYMBOL_MAP`) ensures hardcoded aliases survive even if meta fetch fails. New `_resolve_coin()` async helper translates canonical symbol to coin name. `get_funding_rate` calls `fundingHistory` endpoint with the resolved coin; `get_open_interest` calls `metaAndAssetCtxs` (with `dex:"xyz"` for HIP-3) and matches the coin in the universe array. Testnet URL handled automatically. 20 new tests: `TestStaticCoinMap` (4), `TestAssetRegistry` (4), `TestResolveCoin` (4), `TestFundingRate` (4), `TestOpenInterest` (4). Engine version bumped PATCH `2026.04.3.9.0 → 2026.04.3.9.1`. Full `pytest -q` → **1753 passed** (1737 → 1753, +16 net), zero regressions. **(1753 total)**

- **Diagnose shadow-mode LLM agent None returns** — Added `DIAG` warning logs at every `return None` site in IndicatorAgent, PatternAgent, and TrendAgent `analyze()` methods. Each log line includes the exact code location, the reason for the None return, and the LLM provider state (type, presence, connection). Also logs pre-LLM-call confirmation ("about to call generate_text/generate_vision") and post-LLM-call confirmation ("LLM returned, content_len=...") so the next shadow-mode restart will reveal exactly which return path each agent hits. New `scripts/debug_shadow_agents.py` diagnostic script mirrors the production `_make_bot_factory` wiring exactly (unlike `debug_agents.py` which wires manually) to reproduce the scheduled-loop code path. Script inspects the registry contents, verifies `_llm` is not None on each producer, fetches MarketData through the pipeline's OHLCVFetcher, tests chart generation, calls each agent individually, and runs `registry.run_all()` to match production. 71 existing signal agent tests pass, zero regressions. **(1737 tests)**

- **Sprint Portfolio-Risk-Manager Task 4: Wire PRM into the analysis pipeline + production bot factory** — The capstone task that turns the PRM module from "tested in isolation" into "live in every bot the runner spawns". Tasks 1-3 built the pieces; Task 4 connects them. **`engine/pipeline.py` — `AnalysisPipeline` constructor changes**: new optional `portfolio_risk_manager: PortfolioRiskManager | None = None` ctor param. Default is None for back-compat with the existing 30+ test fixtures that build pipelines without one — the WARNING-at-construction log makes a misconfigured production path loud (`AnalysisPipeline[bot_id/symbol] constructed WITHOUT PortfolioRiskManager — entry actions will have position_size=None and the executor will refuse to place orders`). New `_peak_equity: float = 0.0` instance field tracks per-bot all-time-high equity for the Layer 6 drawdown throttle; in-memory only, resets on bot restart (the spec explicitly defers DB persistence as a future enhancement). **`run_cycle` integration**: after DecisionAgent returns and BEFORE the cycle record is built, the pipeline calls `await self._apply_prm(action, market_data)` ONLY IF the action is an entry (`LONG / SHORT / ADD_LONG / ADD_SHORT`) AND PRM is wired. Non-entry actions (`HOLD / SKIP / CLOSE_ALL`) bypass PRM entirely — there's nothing to size. **`_apply_prm` method (~120 lines)**: fetches `balance` and `positions` from `self._ohlcv._adapter` in two separate try/except blocks so a transient API hiccup converts to SKIP rather than crashing the cycle (CLAUDE.md Rule "SKIP is always safe"). Validates `balance > 0` (non-positive balance → SKIP), `current_price > 0` (bad candle data → SKIP), and that `action.sl_price` and `action.tp1_price` are populated (entry actions always have these from DecisionAgent's SL/TP computation, but defensive). Normalises the adapter's Position objects into the dict shape PRM expects: `{"symbol": p.symbol, "notional": abs(p.size * p.entry_price), "direction": p.direction}`. The `abs()` is direction-agnostic because PRM's Layer 2/3 caps treat long and short capacity equally (no netting). Malformed Position objects (missing fields, type errors) are logged + skipped per-row so a single bad row can't crash sizing for the whole bot. Computes `sl_distance_pct = abs(current_price - action.sl_price) / current_price` and `tp1_distance_pct = abs(action.tp1_price - current_price) / current_price` — both are positive fractions regardless of LONG/SHORT direction. Resolves `peak_for_prm = self._peak_equity if self._peak_equity > 0 else balance` so the very first cycle on a fresh bot feeds PRM `peak_equity == balance` (drawdown 0, multiplier 1.0) instead of `peak_equity == 0` which would also work via PRM's "no history" branch but is less clean. Falls back `risk_weight = action.risk_weight if action.risk_weight else 1.0` defensively — DecisionAgent should always set it for entry actions but a None slipping through shouldn't crash. Calls `self._prm.size_trade(equity, peak_equity, sl_distance_pct, tp1_distance_pct, risk_weight, symbol, open_positions)` with all the resolved arguments. **Peak equity update happens AFTER PRM runs** so this cycle uses the OLD peak — the order doesn't matter when balance ≥ peak (the result is identical) and when balance < peak the update branch doesn't fire (peak stays at the old high water mark, drawdown is computed against it correctly). **Result handling**: if `sizing.skipped`, the action is converted to SKIP via the new `_convert_to_skip` static helper; otherwise `action.position_size` is mutated in place with `sizing.position_size_usd` and the executor consumes that. Both branches log at INFO with the relevant numbers (`PRM SKIP: ...` or `PRM: size=$X, risk=$Y, weight=Z, DD_mult=W`) so operator logs are self-contained. **`_convert_to_skip` static helper**: builds a SKIP TradeAction that preserves `conviction_score` and `raw_output` (so cycle records still capture what DecisionAgent originally decided) but zeroes out every sizing field (`position_size`, `sl_price`, `tp1_price`, `tp2_price`, `rr_ratio`, `atr_multiplier`, `risk_weight`) so the executor can't act on stale levels. The PRM rejection reason is appended to the original reasoning as `[PRM override: <reason>]` so audit logs show BOTH the LLM's intent AND why PRM blocked it. **`quantagent/main.py` — `_make_bot_factory` changes**: imports `PortfolioRiskConfig` and `PortfolioRiskManager`. Inside the per-bot `factory(symbol, bot_id)` closure, builds one PRM per bot via `PortfolioRiskManager(PortfolioRiskConfig())` (spec defaults — 1% risk, 15% per-asset cap, 30% portfolio cap, 10/5/8% drawdown halt/reduce/resume). Each bot gets its OWN instance because PRM is stateful w.r.t. the `_halted` hysteresis flag and the per-bot peak-equity tracker lives on the AnalysisPipeline — sharing one PRM across bots would mix drawdown state between unrelated portfolios. Threads it into `AnalysisPipeline(..., portfolio_risk_manager=portfolio_risk_manager)`. Inline comment cross-references the per-bot scope rationale. **`scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` changes**: imports `PortfolioRiskConfig` and `PortfolioRiskManager`. Builds one PRM with the spec defaults and threads it into the `AnalysisPipeline` constructor (was previously absent so the script ran the pipeline with PRM=None and used a local fixed-fractional stand-in for sizing). Removed the entire PRM stand-in block from the order placement path — `action.position_size` is now populated by the pipeline's PRM call, so the script just reads it and applies the 50% testnet safety cap on top. The "PRM stand-in" inline comment was replaced with a "PortfolioRiskManager is wired into the pipeline above and has already stamped action.position_size" comment so a future reader doesn't get confused about where the size is coming from. The "Risk weight" diagnostic line is preserved; the "Suggested $" line is renamed to "PRM $" to match the new source of truth. **`tests/integration/test_pipeline.py`** — 32 tests, all pass: imported `PortfolioRiskConfig` and `PortfolioRiskManager`. New `_PortfolioStateAdapter` MockAdapter subclass with configurable balance + positions and per-call counters (`balance_calls`, `positions_calls`) for assertion. New `_build_pipeline_with_prm` helper that wires a pipeline with an explicit PRM, defaults to relaxed caps so individual cap-test scenarios opt back into the spec defaults. **NEW `TestPipelinePortfolioRiskManagerWiring` class** (9 tests): `test_prm_called_for_long_action_populates_position_size` pins the canonical `risk_dollars / sl_distance_pct` math directly against the action's actual SL price (rather than dollar bounds, because synthetic test candles have low ATR → tiny SL distance → huge leveraged notional that's a function of the test fixture, not a bug); `test_prm_skip_converts_action_to_skip` forces a Layer 5 cost-floor SKIP via `cost_floor_multiplier=10000.0` and asserts the action becomes SKIP with `[PRM override: ...]` in the reasoning, sizing fields cleared, conviction_score preserved; `test_prm_not_called_for_skip_action` and `test_prm_not_called_for_hold_action` use `_PortfolioStateAdapter`'s call counters to assert PRM doesn't fetch balance/positions for non-entry actions (the HOLD test patches `pipeline._decision.decide` with an async fake to return a HOLD TradeAction directly because DecisionAgent's safety-check path otherwise turns LONG into HOLD via a different route); `test_prm_balance_fetch_failure_skips` and `test_prm_positions_fetch_failure_skips` inject `RuntimeError` on the relevant adapter call and assert the SKIP reason includes the expected attribution text; `test_prm_zero_balance_skips` covers the non-positive balance branch; `test_pipeline_normalizes_positions_for_prm` is the load-bearing position-shape test — passes a real `Position(symbol="BTC-USDC", size=0.1, entry_price=50_000.0)` to the adapter, runs PRM with the spec defaults so `15% * $10k = $1500 cap < $5000 existing` triggers a Layer 2 SKIP, and asserts the SKIP reason says "Per-asset cap" + "BTC-USDC" — proving the abs(size * entry_price) → notional normalisation works end-to-end; `test_pipeline_short_action_uses_prm` patches `pipeline._decision.decide` to return a SHORT action with proper SL/TP and asserts PRM still fires (covers the `action.action in ("SHORT", ...)` gate). **NEW `TestPipelinePeakEquityTracking` class** (4 tests): `test_peak_equity_starts_at_zero` (fresh pipeline contract); `test_peak_equity_seeds_from_first_balance` (the first successful cycle sets `_peak_equity = balance`); `test_peak_equity_increases_when_balance_grows` (subsequent cycle with a larger balance bumps the peak); `test_peak_equity_does_not_decrease` (the load-bearing drawdown-depth pin — a smaller balance MUST keep the peak intact so the next cycle's drawdown is computed against the all-time high). **NEW `TestPipelinePrmOptional` class** (2 tests): `test_pipeline_runs_without_prm` (back-compat — existing fixtures that don't pass a PRM still complete, action.position_size stays None); `test_construction_without_prm_logs_warning` (the loud-by-default contract — a misconfigured production path emits a WARNING at construction so operators notice). **`tests/unit/test_main_bot_factory.py`** — 7 tests, all pass: 2 new tests added: `test_factory_wires_portfolio_risk_manager_into_pipeline` (asserts the constructed bot's pipeline has a `_prm` of type `PortfolioRiskManager` AND that the spec config defaults are present — risk_per_trade_pct=0.01, per_asset_cap_pct=0.15, portfolio_cap_pct=0.30); `test_factory_constructs_one_prm_per_bot_not_shared` (the load-bearing per-bot scoping test — `bot1._pipeline._prm is not bot2._pipeline._prm` so a future "optimization" that hoists PRM construction out of the closure can't accidentally cross-contaminate drawdown state between bots). **`quantagent/version.py`**: ENGINE_VERSION bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.8.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.9.0-alpha.1` (Sprint Portfolio-Risk-Manager COMPLETE — the four-task arc that strips DecisionAgent of dollar sizing AND builds a deterministic six-layer risk pipeline AND wires it into every production bot has now landed end-to-end). **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1737 passed in 15.12s** (1720 → 1737, +17 net), zero regressions across the existing 1720 tests. **Spec deviations**: (1) **PRM is OPTIONAL on the pipeline ctor**: spec implied required ("Construct PRM and pass it to the AnalysisPipeline constructor") but I made it `PortfolioRiskManager | None = None` so the existing 30+ test fixtures don't all need to thread one through. The WARNING-at-construction log makes a missing PRM loud, and `test_construction_without_prm_logs_warning` pins that contract. The Task 4 spec criterion "_make_bot_factory in main.py constructs PRM and passes it to the pipeline" is satisfied — `_make_bot_factory` builds one and threads it through; tests that explicitly want to exercise the no-PRM back-compat path opt out. (2) **Peak equity tracking is in-memory only**: spec said "store in memory (resets on restart). Future: persist to DB via bot config_json" — so the future-DB-persistence carve-out is in the spec itself. Implemented as an instance attribute on AnalysisPipeline (`_peak_equity: float`), exposed nowhere publicly so the storage shape can change without API churn when DB persistence lands. (3) **Pipeline uses `self._ohlcv._adapter` to access the exchange**: not a separate `_adapter` field on the pipeline. Rationale: the engine has zero direct exchange couplings (CLAUDE.md Rule 3) and the deleted `_resolve_account_balance` from Task 1 used this same pattern. Adding a parallel `_adapter` field would have meant updating every single test fixture's constructor call. The `_ohlcv._adapter` access is intentional indirection — OHLCVFetcher is the one place every adapter handle flows through. (4) **`_make_bot_factory` builds one PRM per closure invocation, NOT one shared instance hoisted out of the closure**: this is the right call because PRM holds the `_halted` hysteresis flag which MUST be per-bot to avoid cross-contaminating drawdown state across unrelated portfolios. Pinned by `test_factory_constructs_one_prm_per_bot_not_shared`. The "stateless except for peak_equity" comment in the spec was slightly misleading — `_halted` is also state, and that state matters per-bot. (5) **`_apply_prm` SKIPs on adapter failure rather than falling back**: the spec didn't specify the failure handling. I chose SKIP-on-error (rather than fall-back-to-cached or fall-back-to-fixed-balance) because PRM needs accurate state to make safe sizing decisions; running PRM on stale or missing portfolio state is materially worse than skipping the cycle. The operator still gets a clear WARNING log line so transient failures are visible. (6) **`_convert_to_skip` is a static helper on the pipeline class**, not a method on TradeAction. Rationale: TradeAction is a pure data dataclass and shouldn't grow imperative methods just for the pipeline's use case. The helper closes over no instance state (`@staticmethod`) but lives on the pipeline class for encapsulation. (7) **Position normalisation uses `abs(p.size * p.entry_price)`**: spec snippet used `p["size"] * p["entry_price"]` (no abs), but on a SHORT position `p.size` may be negative on some venues and the resulting notional would be negative. abs() is direction-agnostic and matches PRM's "no netting at the cap layer" contract. (8) **TESTNET RUN NOT EXECUTED**: the spec's last acceptance criterion ("Run testnet cycle and paste output showing PRM working") is intentionally deferred to the operator. The script wiring is complete and the unit/integration tests pin every observable behavior, but actually placing a real testnet order requires Hyperliquid testnet credentials, a funded testnet wallet, and operator-side `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET=true` environment setup that the test harness doesn't have. The script is ready to run; `tests/unit/test_main_bot_factory.py::test_factory_wires_portfolio_risk_manager_into_pipeline` proves the wiring at the closure level and `tests/integration/test_pipeline.py::TestPipelinePortfolioRiskManagerWiring` proves the end-to-end pipeline path. Marked in the SPRINT acceptance criteria as a documented deferral with the rationale.

- **Sprint Portfolio-Risk-Manager Task 3: PortfolioRiskManager — Layers 2, 3 (exposure caps)** — Replaced the inert Layer 2 / Layer 3 placeholders that Task 2 stubbed in with the real per-asset and portfolio-wide exposure caps so PRM can now genuinely defend against over-concentration. The Task 2 work locked the public `size_trade` signature and the placeholder method shapes, so this task is a body-only change — `_apply_per_asset_cap` and `_apply_portfolio_cap` now do real work; the `size_trade` orchestrator gained layer-attributed SKIP branches between the calls so operator logs say WHICH cap fired instead of a generic "exposure clamped". **`engine/execution/portfolio_risk_manager.py`**: replaced the two placeholder method bodies with the spec implementations. **`_apply_per_asset_cap`** sums the notional of every existing position in the SAME symbol via the new `_symbol_exposure(symbol, open_positions)` static helper, computes `cap = equity * per_asset_cap_pct`, and returns either `0.0` (existing ≥ cap → caller converts to SKIP), `min(position_size, remaining)` (clamping path — trade still goes through, just smaller), or `position_size` unchanged. Other symbols' positions don't count — Layer 2 is per-symbol by design; Layer 3 catches the portfolio-wide picture separately. **`_apply_portfolio_cap`** has the same shape but sums notional across EVERY open position regardless of symbol or direction, against `equity * portfolio_cap_pct`. The new `_symbol_exposure` and `_total_exposure` static helpers BOTH skip entries with malformed shape (missing `notional` field, non-numeric `notional` value) so a stale or partially populated position dict from `adapter.get_positions()` in Task 4 wiring can't crash sizing — defensive against the future production wiring path. **`size_trade` integration**: the previous catch-all `if position_size <= 0: return SKIP("Exposure caps clamped...")` block from Task 2 was replaced with TWO layer-attributed early-return blocks BETWEEN the layer calls. After Layer 2 returns, if the result is ≤ 0, build a SizingResult with `skip_reason=f"Per-asset cap: {symbol} existing exposure ${existing:,.2f} ≥ cap ${cap:,.2f} ({per_asset_cap_pct * 100:.0f}% of equity)"`. After Layer 3, similar but `skip_reason=f"Portfolio cap: total exposure ${total:,.2f} ≥ cap ${cap:,.2f} ..."`. Both branches log at INFO so operators get one line per skip. The layer-attribution is the load-bearing observability win — without it, an operator reading PRM logs would see "exposure clamped" and have to jump back to the code or recompute the math by hand. The layer ordering (Layer 2 first, then Layer 3) gives a tightest-cap-wins semantic automatically: if Layer 2 already clamped to $150 and Layer 3 would have allowed $200, the result is $150 (Layer 3 sees the $150 input and `min($150, $200) = $150`); if Layer 2 allowed $1000 but Layer 3 only has $200 of headroom, the result is $200 (Layer 3 clamps the $1000 down). **Module docstring**: updated the layer-summary table to reflect that Layers 2 and 3 are now "implemented" not "Task 3 placeholder", and added "Tasks 2 + 3" attribution to the "this module implements" sentence. **`tests/unit/test_portfolio_risk_manager.py`** — 49 tests, all pass (was 31 in Task 2, +18 net): **New `_capped_prm` helper** factory that returns a PRM with the spec-default 15% per-asset / 30% portfolio caps active; the existing `_prm` helper was updated to default both caps to `100.0` (10000% of equity → effectively disabled) so Layer 1 / 5 / 6 tests can test their layer in isolation without getting clobbered by Layer 2. The relax-by-default decision matters because the spec's natural Layer 1 baseline ($10k equity * 1% risk * 1.0 weight / 2% SL = $5000) is already 50% of equity, way over the 15% per-asset cap, so EVERY Layer 1 / 5 / 6 test that expects to compute a clean $5000 baseline would have started failing the moment Layer 2 went live. The relax-then-opt-in pattern keeps the Layer 1/5/6 tests focused on their own layer and forces Layer 2/3 tests to be explicit about which cap they're exercising. The `TestPortfolioRiskConfigDefaults` smoke tests still pin the spec defaults via `PortfolioRiskConfig()` directly so the dataclass contract has separate coverage. **New `TestLayer2PerAssetCap` class** (8 tests): no existing positions clamps to the cap (NOT to the unrelated Layer 1 baseline — pinning that the cap is a hard ceiling, not a "subtract from baseline" calculation), existing position clamps the proposed size with a precise math check ($1000 existing → $500 of the $1500 cap remaining → result $500), at-cap and above-cap both SKIP with `Per-asset cap` reasons, other symbol's exposure doesn't count toward this symbol's bucket (Layer 2 is per-symbol scoped), multiple positions in the same symbol sum into one bucket (regression test for a future bug where someone accidentally only counts the first match), skip-reason format includes dollar amounts AND the literal symbol name AND the word "cap", malformed position dicts (missing notional field, non-numeric notional) are SKIPPED safely without crashing — proves the defensive `try/except` in `_symbol_exposure` works under the same input shapes Task 4 will eventually pass from `adapter.get_positions()`. **New `TestLayer3PortfolioCap` class** (5 tests): no existing positions still clamps to Layer 2's per-asset cap first (since with both caps active, 15% is tighter than 30%), the spec scenario where 25% of equity is already exposed leaves only 5% remaining → clamp to $500 (the precise math check), at-portfolio-cap SKIP, above-portfolio-cap SKIP, skip-reason format includes dollar amounts and the word "exposure". **New `TestExposureCapsCombined` class** (5 tests): the load-bearing tightest-wins test from the spec — Layer 2 clamps to $150 (existing BTC $1350, BTC remaining $150) while Layer 3 would allow $200 (portfolio total $2800, remaining $200) → final result $150 because Layer 3 receives $150 as input and `min($150, $200) = $150`; the inverse where Layer 3 clamps tighter than Layer 2 (existing BTC $500 → BTC remaining $1000, existing ETH $2300 → portfolio remaining $200 → result $200); mixed-direction positions count without netting (long $1000 BTC + short $800 BTC → contribute $1800 to the per-asset cap, NOT $200 net — the SL/TP risk is symmetric across direction so capacity gets consumed equally); Layer 2 zero short-circuits BEFORE Layer 3's reason appears (operator must be able to attribute the skip to the right layer); skipped result preserves intermediate state (Layer 1's risk_dollars + Layer 6's multiplier still flow through to the SizingResult so logs are debuggable end to end). **Updated existing `test_layers_2_and_3_placeholders_dont_change_size`**: renamed to `test_small_existing_positions_below_caps_dont_clamp` and reworked to use $50 BTC + $50 ETH positions (well below both caps, so the result must equal the no-positions case). The original test asserted the placeholders were no-ops; with Task 3 the layers actually exist, so the test was rewritten as a NEGATIVE-CONTROL regression test for the no-op path — Layer 2/3 must NOT subtract unconditionally just because positions are passed in. **`quantagent/version.py`**: ENGINE_VERSION bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.7.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.8.0-alpha.1` (new public behavior — Layers 2 and 3 actually do something now; the public API surface is unchanged but the observable behavior of `size_trade` is materially different on every call with non-empty `open_positions`, and that crosses the MINOR-bump line). **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1720 passed in 14.60s** (1702 → 1720, +18 net), zero regressions across the existing 1702 tests. **Spec deviations**: (1) **`_prm()` test helper relaxed by default**: not in the spec but necessary because the spec's natural Layer 1 baseline ($5000 on $10k equity with 2% SL) is already 50% of equity, well over the 15% per-asset cap. Without relaxing the cap in Layer 1/5/6 tests, every existing Task 2 test would have started failing the moment Layer 2 went live. The opt-in `_capped_prm` helper for Layer 2/3 tests is the right inverse — explicit about which tests care about caps. (2) **Layer-attributed SKIP reasons**: spec said "If size is 0 after either, return SizingResult(skipped=True) with reason" but didn't specify the reason format. Implemented as `Per-asset cap: ...` vs `Portfolio cap: ...` so an operator reading PRM logs can attribute the skip to the right layer without checking the source. (3) **Defensive `_symbol_exposure` / `_total_exposure` helpers**: not in the spec but added because Task 4 will pass `adapter.get_positions()` results straight through, and venues that don't expose every field will give us partially populated dicts. The `try/except (TypeError, ValueError)` block silently skips malformed entries so a single bad row can't crash sizing for the whole bot. Pinned by `test_malformed_position_dict_is_skipped_safely`. (4) **No netting across direction**: long + short in the same symbol both consume the per-asset cap independently. The spec didn't address this; I chose no-netting because the SL risk is symmetric (a $1000 long with a 2% SL has the same loss potential as a $1000 short with a 2% SL — they're not naturally hedged unless someone explicitly sized them as a pair). Pinned by `test_mixed_directions_count_in_total_exposure`. (5) **Layer 2 / Layer 3 ordering**: Layer 2 runs first, Layer 3 second. The spec said "Apply Layer 2 (per-asset cap) — may reduce size" then "Apply Layer 3 (portfolio cap) — may reduce further", which matches. The tightest-wins semantic is automatic from this ordering.

- **Sprint Portfolio-Risk-Manager Task 2: PortfolioRiskManager — Layers 1, 5, 6** — Built the deterministic six-layer risk pipeline that owns ALL position-sizing math now that DecisionAgent only emits trade INTENT (Task 1). This task ships layers 1 (Fixed Fractional), 5 (LLM Cost Floor), and 6 (Drawdown Throttle); layers 2 and 3 (per-asset / portfolio caps) are wired in as inert placeholder methods so the public `size_trade` signature is locked NOW and Task 3 can replace the bodies without touching `size_trade` or any of its callers, and Task 4 (pipeline wiring) can be written against the final shape without churn. **New file `engine/execution/portfolio_risk_manager.py`** (~330 lines): three dataclasses + one stateful class. **`PortfolioRiskConfig`** carries every tunable parameter with the spec-mandated defaults: `risk_per_trade_pct=0.01`, `per_asset_cap_pct=0.15`, `portfolio_cap_pct=0.30`, `cost_floor_multiplier=20.0` (LLM cost ≤ 5% of TP1 profit), `drawdown_halt_pct=0.10`, `drawdown_reduce_pct=0.05`, `drawdown_resume_pct=0.08` (the 2-pp gap between halt and resume IS the hysteresis band), `llm_cycle_cost=0.025` (matches CONTEXT.md's per-cycle budget after prompt-cache hits). Inline docstring documents WHY each default was chosen so a future tuning pass has the rationale. **`SizingResult`** is the public output dataclass: `position_size_usd`, `risk_dollars`, `effective_risk_pct`, `drawdown_multiplier`, `skipped: bool = False`, `skip_reason: str = ""`, plus a `to_dict()` for tracking. The intermediate fields (`risk_dollars`, `effective_risk_pct`, `drawdown_multiplier`) are filled in as far as the pipeline got — if Layer 6 halts we have multiplier=0.0 but no risk dollars; if Layer 5 catches a too-small trade we have both multiplier and risk dollars but a zeroed-out final position. This makes operator logs self-documenting. **`PortfolioRiskManager`** is the orchestrator: stateful only with respect to a single `_halted: bool` flag; everything else is a pure function of the inputs to `size_trade(equity, peak_equity, sl_distance_pct, tp1_distance_pct, risk_weight, symbol, open_positions=None)`. Public `is_halted` property exposes the state machine for diagnostics + the eventual /health endpoint + tests (so we don't poke `_halted` directly). **Layer execution order is 6 → 1 → 5 → 2 → 3.** The spec acceptance criterion "Layer 5 runs FIRST — fail fast" was reconciled with the spec's own implementation note ("Layer 5 needs the position_size from Layer 1 to compute expected_profit") by running Layer 1 first; the math is identical to a fast-check on `equity * risk_pct * tp1_distance_pct / sl_distance_pct`, so doing Layer 1 first costs nothing but lets Layer 5 use the canonical size value. Inline docstring on `size_trade` documents this reconciliation explicitly. **Layer 1 (Fixed Fractional)** is the spec formula: `effective_risk_pct = config.risk_per_trade_pct * drawdown_multiplier`, `risk_dollars = equity * effective_risk_pct * risk_weight`, `position = risk_dollars / sl_distance_pct`. Final position is rounded to 2 decimal places to match the dollar-precision the executor expects. **Layer 5 (LLM Cost Floor)** computes `expected_profit = position_size * tp1_distance_pct` and `min_profit = config.llm_cycle_cost * config.cost_floor_multiplier`; if the trade can't clear `min_profit` it returns SKIP with a structured reason that includes BOTH dollar amounts and the floor multiplier so operators can debug without re-running. The boundary is `<` (strict) so a trade exactly AT the floor passes. **Layer 6 (Drawdown Throttle)** is the only stateful layer. The state machine: `not halted → halted` when `drawdown ≥ drawdown_halt_pct` (10%); `halted → not halted` when `drawdown < drawdown_resume_pct` (8%); `halted → halted` for any drawdown in the [resume, halt] band. The asymmetry IS the hysteresis — without it, equity bouncing between 9.99% and 10.01% drawdown would flip the manager on and off every cycle and the bot would uselessly stutter. The non-halted classifier returns 1.0 / 0.5 / 0.0 for the [0, reduce), [reduce, halt), [halt, ∞) bands. `peak_equity <= 0` is treated as "no history yet" and returns 1.0 (full risk) — also clears any stale halt flag — so a brand-new bot's first cycle isn't reflexively skipped before peak_equity has been seeded. The halt-trigger and halt-release transitions log at WARNING / INFO so the operator gets a single line per state change (not per cycle), and `Drawdown halt:` skip reasons surface BOTH equity AND peak AND the percentage so the log line is self-contained. **Layers 2 and 3 placeholders**: `_apply_per_asset_cap(position_size, equity, symbol, open_positions)` and `_apply_portfolio_cap(position_size, equity, open_positions)` return `position_size` unchanged. They're called by `size_trade` so the layer ordering is locked; the final-size sanity check (`if position_size <= 0: return SKIP("Exposure caps clamped position to zero")`) is also in place so Task 3 can flip to `return 0.0` without revisiting `size_trade`. **Defensive input validation**: `equity ≤ 0`, `sl_distance_pct ≤ 0`, `tp1_distance_pct ≤ 0`, and `risk_weight is None or ≤ 0` all return SKIP with structured reasons before any sizing math runs. PRM is invoked from the pipeline which has its own SKIP-on-error pattern, but the double-check protects misuse from scripts and tests too. **`tests/unit/test_portfolio_risk_manager.py`** — 31 tests, 100% pass: **`TestLayer1FixedFractional`** (8 tests): basic sizing math ($10k * 1% / 2% SL → $5000 position, $100 risk), wider SL gives smaller position, risk_dollars stays constant across SL distances (fixed-fractional invariant), risk_weight 1.3 scales the position by 30%, low-band weight 0.75 under-sizes by 25%, zero equity / zero SL / zero risk_weight all return SKIP. **`TestLayer5LLMCostFloor`** (5 tests): below-floor SKIP with correct reason format, above-floor PASS, AT-boundary edge case PASS (strict `<`), one-cent-below-boundary SKIP, skip reason format validation (must contain "$", "expected", "min"). **`TestLayer6DrawdownThrottle`** (9 tests): no drawdown → 1.0, 5% drawdown → 0.5 (with the position-math gotcha that drawdown shrinks BOTH the multiplier AND the equity, so position is NOT exactly half a no-drawdown trade), 10% drawdown → halt + SKIP, peak_equity=0 safe (no zero-div, full risk, clears stale halt), hysteresis halt persists at 9% drawdown after halting at 10% (the load-bearing thrash-prevention test), hysteresis releases at 7% drawdown (fall through to multiplier 0.5), full recovery returns to 1.0, drawdown exactly at resume threshold (8%) STAYS halted (strict `<` release), halt skip-reason format includes equity + peak + percentage. **`TestSizeTradeIntegration`** (5 tests): full happy path with realistic $10k account + 1.15 weight (asserts the exact $115 risk_dollars / $5750 position math), drawdown-then-Layer-5 interaction (5% drawdown halves the size, then a tight cost floor catches the smaller size — verifies the LATER layer fires with the EARLIER multiplier already applied, end-result is `LLM cost floor` SKIP NOT `Drawdown halt`), skipped result preserves intermediate state (Layer 5 SKIP still reports the risk_dollars and multiplier from Layer 1 / Layer 6), `open_positions=None` is treated identically to `[]`, Layers 2 and 3 placeholders DON'T mutate the size in Task 2 (a regression that wires Task 3 logic prematurely would be caught immediately). **`TestPortfolioRiskConfigDefaults`** (2 tests): pin every documented default value (catches typos in the dataclass), config overrides propagate through to the math (tested with `risk_per_trade_pct=0.02` doubling the risk_dollars). **`TestSizingResultDataclass`** (2 tests): `to_dict` round-trip on the happy path + the SKIP path. **Test helper gotcha**: the `_size` convenience wrapper defaults `peak_equity` to whatever `equity` is set to (rather than a fixed 10k constant) so overriding only `equity` doesn't accidentally trip Layer 6 by leaving a stale 10k peak in place. The bug surfaced on the second test run and the docstring on `_size` documents the trap so future contributors don't fall into it. **`quantagent/version.py`**: ENGINE_VERSION bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.6.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.7.0-alpha.1` (new public surface — `PortfolioRiskManager` class + `PortfolioRiskConfig` + `SizingResult` dataclasses + the entire `engine/execution/portfolio_risk_manager.py` module). **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1702 passed in 14.87s** (1671 → 1702, +31 net), zero regressions across the existing 1671 tests. **Spec deviations**: (1) **Layer execution order**: spec said "Layer 5 runs FIRST — fail fast" but the same spec's implementation note clarified that Layer 5 needs Layer 1's position_size, so the actual order is 6→1→5→2-3 with Layer 5 still functioning as a fail-fast gate (it returns SKIP immediately on hit, before Layers 2-3 mutate the size further). The fast-check optimisation the spec mentioned (`equity * risk_pct * tp1_distance_pct / sl_distance_pct < min_profit` without doing full sizing first) was NOT implemented because the math is identical and the micro-optimisation isn't worth the second code path. Inline docstring on `size_trade` documents the reconciliation. (2) **Hysteresis state**: the spec said "track a `_halted` state. Once halted at 10%, stay halted until drawdown improves below 8%." Implemented as a single instance attribute on `PortfolioRiskManager` with a public `is_halted` property — tests assert against the property rather than poking `_halted` directly so the encapsulation survives a future refactor. The state is per-PRM-instance, scoped per-bot, matching Task 4's "one PRM per bot" recommendation. (3) **`peak_equity ≤ 0` handling**: the spec didn't explicitly cover this edge case; I treat it as "no history yet → full risk" and ALSO clear any stale halt flag, because the first cycle of a brand-new bot would otherwise be unable to trade until peak_equity gets seeded. (4) **Final sanity check after Layers 2-3**: added a `if position_size <= 0: return SKIP("Exposure caps clamped position to zero")` block AFTER the placeholder layer calls. This is dead code in Task 2 (the placeholders never zero the size) but locks the contract so Task 3 can replace the placeholder bodies WITHOUT touching `size_trade`. (5) **Defensive input validation**: not in the spec but added for the tightness — `equity ≤ 0`, `sl_distance_pct ≤ 0`, `tp1_distance_pct ≤ 0`, `risk_weight ≤ 0` all return structured SKIP results before any math runs. The pipeline's SKIP-on-error pattern would catch these too, but a clean SizingResult with a debuggable reason is friendlier to operators reading PRM logs. (6) **31 tests vs spec's "at least 15"**: doubled the count because each of the four spec-mandated test categories (Layer 1, Layer 5, Layer 6, integration) deserved 5-9 tests to genuinely cover the boundary cases (specifically the hysteresis state transitions in Layer 6, which need 5 tests minimum to pin the four state-machine edges + the strict-`<` release boundary). (7) **`PortfolioRiskManager` is NOT exported from `engine/execution/__init__.py`** — Task 4 will wire it through the bot factory, and adding a re-export now without a consumer would just be churn.

- **Sprint Portfolio-Risk-Manager Task 1: Strip DecisionAgent of dollar sizing** — Stripped all position-sizing math out of the DecisionAgent path so the LLM only outputs trade INTENT (action + SL/TP + reasoning), and a deterministic conviction-band `risk_weight` (0.75 / 1.0 / 1.15 / 1.3) is attached in plain Python AFTER the LLM call. This is the load-bearing prerequisite for the PortfolioRiskManager work in Tasks 2-4: PRM will own dollar sizing end-to-end and consume `risk_weight` as its multiplier on top of the bot's base `risk_per_trade`. **`engine/types.py`**: added `risk_weight: float | None = None` to `TradeAction` as a default-None field at the end of the dataclass so every existing positional/keyword construction (most notably the executor unit tests that build TradeAction by hand) keeps working without changes. Inline docstring documents that `position_size` is now PRM-populated downstream — DecisionAgent always emits it as None. **`engine/execution/agent.py`**: removed the `account_balance` parameter from `DecisionAgent.decide()` (was previously threaded through to `compute_position_size`); deleted the LONG/SHORT/ADD_LONG/ADD_SHORT branch that called `compute_position_size`, multiplied by the conviction tier multiplier, and halved for pyramid adds; deleted the `_CONVICTION_SIZE_MULTIPLIER` dict and `_conviction_size_multiplier()` static method (the conviction-tier mapping moved into the new public helper); dropped the `compute_position_size` import. New module-level `risk_weight_from_conviction(score: float) -> float` is the ONLY place the conviction → weight mapping lives — pure Python, no async, no LLM, importable from anywhere PRM needs to grade a weight against the same source of truth. The mapping bands match the spec exactly: `[0.50, 0.60) → 0.75`, `[0.60, 0.70) → 1.0`, `[0.70, 0.85) → 1.15`, `[0.85, 1.0] → 1.30`. The agent attaches `risk_weight` only on entry actions (LONG / SHORT / ADD_LONG / ADD_SHORT); HOLD / SKIP / CLOSE_ALL leave it as None so PRM can't accidentally size a non-trade. The safety-override block was updated to clear `risk_weight` alongside SL/TP/RR when an entry action gets converted to HOLD/SKIP — this matches the existing "clear sizing fields" pattern and avoids leaking a stale weight into PRM. The `_safe_default()` helper and the conviction-below-threshold quick-exit path both pass `risk_weight=None` explicitly. **`engine/execution/prompts/decision_v1.py`**: removed the `Balance: ${{account_balance:.2f}}` line and the entire `## ACCOUNT` section from the USER_PROMPT (the LLM no longer sees account balance at all); rewrote the SYSTEM_PROMPT preamble to explicitly tell the LLM that "Position sizing is OUT OF SCOPE for this agent. PortfolioRiskManager owns all sizing math downstream — never output dollar amounts, position sizes, percentages of equity, or risk weights" so a future re-prompted run can't accidentally pollute the JSON with sizing fields; cut the size-related columns out of the conviction-tier table ("Base position size", "Full position size", "Enhanced size (1.3x)") since the LLM doesn't size anymore; cut the "ADD size = 50% of base position size" line from the pyramid rules section. The JSON output schema is byte-for-byte unchanged (`action`, `reasoning`, `suggested_rr`) — no risk weight, no size, no balance — because the spec says "compute risk_weight in Python code OUTSIDE the LLM call, not in the prompt". `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped from `"1.0"` to `"1.1"` since the SYSTEM_PROMPT and USER_PROMPT both changed structurally. **`engine/pipeline.py`**: removed the `_resolve_account_balance()` helper method (~50 lines), the `_FALLBACK_BALANCE_USD` class constant, and the `balance = await self._resolve_account_balance(...)` call from `run_cycle()`. The DecisionAgent invocation now reads `await self._decision.decide(conviction=..., market_data=..., current_position=..., memory_context=...)` — four args, no balance. The `_skip_action()` builder now passes `risk_weight=None` so the SKIP path is consistent with the new TradeAction shape. Inline comment cross-references PRM Task 4 ("PortfolioRiskManager will be wired into this same call site after DecisionAgent returns"). **`backtesting/evals/pipeline_adapter.py`**: removed the `account_balance: float = 10_000.0` constructor parameter from `PipelineAdapter.__init__` and the corresponding `self._account_balance` field; updated `_live_decision()` to call `decide()` without the `account_balance=` kwarg; updated `_trade_action_to_eval_output()` to set `position_size_pct=None` (no more `action.position_size / self._account_balance` math) and stamp `risk_weight=action.risk_weight` so eval reports surface DecisionAgent's intent; updated `_mock_decision()` to pass `risk_weight=None` (mock mode doesn't go through DecisionAgent so it has no weight to carry; the legacy 10% `position_size_pct` is preserved on entry directions for back-compat with the existing CI smoke assertion). **`backtesting/evals/output_contract.py`**: added `risk_weight: float | None = None` as a new optional field at the end of `EvalOutput` so historical eval recordings keep deserializing via `from_dict()` (the existing `from_dict` already drops unknown keys so old files load fine; new `risk_weight=None` default means new fields don't break old constructors). **`tests/unit/test_decision_agent.py`** — 34 tests, all pass: rewrote every `agent.decide(..., 10000.0)` call site to drop the trailing positional balance arg (15 call sites total); converted `test_below_threshold_no_position_size` → `test_below_threshold_no_sl_or_risk_weight` (asserts the new `risk_weight is None` contract on the SKIP path); replaced `test_account_balance_in_prompt` with `test_account_balance_not_in_prompt` (asserts `"Balance" not in prompt`, `"$" not in prompt`, `"account_balance" not in prompt` so a future regression that re-adds balance to the prompt is caught immediately); replaced the entire `TestDecisionAgentSizing` class (which tested dollar sizing, conviction multipliers, and pyramid 50% halving) with a new `TestDecisionAgentRiskWeight` class — 7 tests covering each conviction band (low/moderate/high/very-high), the contract that risk_weight is None for non-entry actions, the contract that `position_size` is ALWAYS None coming out of DecisionAgent (sized downstream by PRM), and a direct unit test of `risk_weight_from_conviction()` that exercises the band boundaries (0.50/0.59/0.60/0.69/0.70/0.84/0.85/1.00); upgraded `test_long_entry` to assert `position_size is None` AND `risk_weight == 1.15` (conviction 0.72 → high tier) so the new schema is pinned end-to-end on the happy path; renamed `test_safety_override_clears_sizing` → `test_safety_override_clears_sl_tp_and_risk_weight` and added `assert result.risk_weight is None` so the safety-override clear path is locked. **`tests/integration/test_pipeline.py`** — 17 tests, all pass: deleted the entire `TestPipelineAccountBalanceResolution` class (4 tests) and the `_BalanceCapturingDecision` shim that recorded `account_balance` kwargs — this contract is gone, the pipeline no longer fetches balance for DecisionAgent. Replaced with `TestPipelineDoesNotFetchBalanceForDecisionAgent` (1 test, `test_pipeline_does_not_call_adapter_get_balance`) which uses a `_BalanceTrackingAdapter` to assert `balance_call_count == 0` after a full cycle, AND asserts the resulting TradeAction has `position_size is None` and `risk_weight == 1.15`. Net is -3 tests in this file — Task 4 will reintroduce balance-fetch tests under the PRM contract. **`scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py`**: `_print_action()` now prints `Risk weight:` whenever DecisionAgent set one (with a "(PRM consumes this in Task 4)" note for the operator); the order-placement block was rewritten to use a local fixed-fractional sizer as a PRM stand-in (`risk_dollars = balance * 0.01 * risk_weight`, then `suggested_usd = risk_dollars / (sl_distance / current_price)`) so the testnet smoke test still places real orders against the testnet orderbook until Task 4 wires PRM into the production pipeline. The 50% safety cap is preserved untouched. Inline comment cross-references the PRM stand-in as a temporary bridge. **`quantagent/version.py`**: ENGINE_VERSION bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.5.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.6.0-alpha.1` (new public surface — `risk_weight_from_conviction()` helper, `TradeAction.risk_weight` field, signature change to `DecisionAgent.decide()`); PROMPT_VERSIONS["decision_agent"] bumped `2.0 → 2.1` to match the prompt-file PROMPT_VERSION bump from 1.0 → 1.1. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1671 passed in 15.13s** (1669 → 1671, +2 net: ~+10 new risk_weight / no-balance tests, ~−8 deleted dollar-sizing / balance-resolution tests). Zero regressions across the existing 1669 tests. **Spec deviations**: (1) Sprint spec said "remove `_resolve_account_balance` from pipeline" — done, but `TradingConfig.account_balance` field is preserved because the standalone `backtesting/engine.py` walker still uses it via `compute_position_size`. (2) `compute_position_size` itself is preserved in `engine/execution/risk_profiles.py` because `backtesting/engine.py` and the cost-model unit tests still consume it — Task 2's PRM will be a separate implementation; this helper survives as the legacy backtest sizer. (3) `TradingConfig.account_balance` field stays because removing it would cascade into the API schema, the bot routes, the seed script, and `backtesting/engine.py` — out of scope for Task 1, the field is just unused by DecisionAgent now. (4) Eval `EvalOutput.position_size_pct` is preserved (defaulted to None on live runs) because removing it would invalidate every checked-in eval recording in `backtesting/evals/reports/`. (5) Mock-mode `position_size_pct=0.10` for entry directions is preserved untouched so the existing CI smoke assertion `assert out.position_size_pct == pytest.approx(0.10)` doesn't break. (6) PROMPT_VERSION inside the prompt file went 1.0 → 1.1 (PATCH bump) but `quantagent/version.py["decision_agent"]` went 2.0 → 2.1 (also a PATCH bump). The two version strings have always been desynced and the bump direction matches.

### 2026-04-09
- **Sprint Paper-Trading Task 4: LangSmith per-mode project routing (process-level) + two real bug fixes** — Closes the paper-trading sprint by completing the per-mode observability story. Two real bugs fixed and one big design decision deferred. **The deferred decision**: an audit of `llm/claude.py::_trace_call` showed the existing implementation already reads `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT` PER CALL from `os.environ` (line 261), which means the process-level env var that the CLI dispatcher sets in `main()` is ALREADY sufficient for the single-mode-per-process workflow Tasks 1-3 set up. Adding a per-call API parameter (`langsmith_project: str | None = None`) — the spec's "preferred approach" — would require: ABC change in `llm/base.py` (2 method signatures), impl change in `llm/claude.py` (thread the param through `_call` to `_trace_call`), and 8 agent files passing the param through (indicator, pattern, trend, conviction, decision, reflection, quant_scientist, macro_regime). 10 files total, exceeding the spec's documented "if this requires touching too many files (>5 agent files + pipeline + factory): Skip the per-call routing" threshold. Per-call routing is therefore deferred as a follow-up task for when we run mixed modes within a single process — the spec explicitly anticipates this fallback path. **The two bugs fixed**: (1) **Shadow mode never set `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT`** before this task. Task 3 added the paper-mode env var setup but the shadow branch only set `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW=1`; shadow runs were inheriting the operator's `.env` value (almost universally `quantagent-live`), meaning every shadow LLM call was leaking into the live observability dashboard since Task 3 landed. Hard to spot without staring at the LangSmith URLs after the fact. **Fix**: `quantagent/main.py:436-447` adds `os.environ["LANGCHAIN_PROJECT"] = "quantagent-shadow"` immediately after `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW=1`, mirroring the paper branch's existing assignment. Inline comment cross-references the deferred per-call routing decision so a future reader knows why the routing is process-level. (2) **The default fallback in `_trace_call` was the stale `quantagent-v2`** — a legacy bucket name from before the live/shadow/paper convention existed. An operator running the bare `python -m quantagent run` (no mode flag) without setting `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT` in `.env` would land in a stale bucket. **Fix**: `llm/claude.py:261-275` changed the default from `"quantagent-v2"` to `"quantagent-live"` and added a multi-line comment documenting the routing chain (CLI dispatcher → env var → per-call read inside `_trace_call`) and why the per-call read is load-bearing for any future mixed-mode work. In normal operation the operator's `.env` typically pins `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT=quantagent-live` explicitly, so the default fallback only fires for ad-hoc scripts and dev runs without `.env` — but it's still the right thing to fix because the current default value was a footgun. **6 new tests** in `tests/unit/test_llm.py`. **`TestLangSmithProjectRouting`** class (5 tests) pins the per-call read contract on `_trace_call` directly (no full `_call` flow) so we can read back the `project_name` kwarg that was passed to `langsmith.Client.create_run`: (1) `test_trace_call_reads_langchain_project_from_env` — sets `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT=quantagent-shadow` then calls `_trace_call` and asserts the captured kwarg matches. (2) `test_trace_call_reads_paper_project_when_paper_env_set` — symmetric coverage with `quantagent-paper`, proving the read is genuinely per-call (not cached at provider construction time). (3) `test_trace_call_default_fallback_is_quantagent_live` — env var cleared, asserts default is `quantagent-live` AND specifically NOT `quantagent-v2` (the second assertion catches a regression that would silently restore the legacy default). (4) `test_trace_call_reads_env_per_call_not_cached` — the load-bearing test for any future per-bot routing work: same provider instance, two `_trace_call` invocations, mutating `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT` between them, asserts both calls captured the right project. Proves the env read happens at trace time, not at `__init__` or module load. (5) `test_trace_call_silent_when_tracing_disabled` — patches `_TRACING_ENABLED=False` and `_traceable=None`, calls `_trace_call`, asserts no exception AND `langsmith.Client` was never instantiated. Defends against a future refactor that might accidentally move the early-out below the `Client()` call. **`TestShadowFlagSetsLangSmithProject`** class (1 test): `test_shadow_flag_sets_langchain_project_quantagent_shadow` — calls `main()` with `--shadow` mocked into `sys.argv` (and `run`/`migrate`/`seed` patched to no-ops), asserts `os.environ["LANGCHAIN_PROJECT"] == "quantagent-shadow"` after the dispatcher returns. End-to-end pin from CLI flag to env var. **Test fixtures**: both new test classes use autouse `restore_*_env` fixtures with two-phase isolation (snapshot at setup → CLEAR at test start → restore at teardown) so upstream pollution from other test files (e.g. `test_main_cli.py` setting `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT`) cannot leak into our snapshot. **Mocking gotchas**: (a) `_TRACING_ENABLED` is set ONCE at module load from `LANGCHAIN_TRACING_V2`, so flipping the env var inside a test would be too late — instead I `patch.object(claude_module, "_TRACING_ENABLED", True)` to force the trace path to execute regardless of operator env. (b) `langsmith.Client` is imported LAZILY inside `_trace_call`'s try block (`from langsmith import Client`), so the test patches `langsmith.Client` at the SOURCE module, NOT `llm.claude.Client` (which doesn't exist at the test's import time and would silently no-op). (c) `_traceable` is patched to `lambda f: f` so the `if not _TRACING_ENABLED or _traceable is None: return` early-out doesn't fire. **Existing test updated**: `tests/unit/test_main_cli.py::test_shadow_alone_does_not_set_paper_env_vars` previously asserted `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT is None` after `--shadow`. That's no longer true — shadow now DOES set it to `quantagent-shadow`. Updated the assertion to pin BOTH halves of the new contract: `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT == "quantagent-shadow"` AND `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT != "quantagent-paper"` (so a future regression that accidentally swapped the two values would be caught). The test docstring was updated with a cross-reference to the new dedicated test in `test_llm.py`. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) **Per-call API parameter deferred**, process-level routing chosen instead — full rationale above. The contract the deferred criteria describe is satisfied by the existing per-call env-var read; we just don't support mixing modes within a single process. (2) **Two bugs fixed alongside the deferral** — the shadow-mode env var leak and the stale `quantagent-v2` default. Both surfaced during the audit and were fixed because they completed the per-mode routing story without touching any agent files. (3) **Tests live in `test_llm.py`** because the new `TestLangSmithProjectRouting` class is scoped to `ClaudeProvider._trace_call` semantics, and the cross-cutting `TestShadowFlagSetsLangSmithProject` (which calls `main()`) lives there too because it's testing the LangSmith routing contract this task adds, not a general CLI flag. Inline class docstring explains the file placement decision. (4) **Force-patched module globals** (`_TRACING_ENABLED`, `_traceable`) instead of monkeypatching `LANGCHAIN_TRACING_V2` — necessary because the booleans are resolved at module load time. (5) **`langsmith.Client` patched at the source module**, not at `llm.claude.Client` — necessary because the import is lazy inside the try block. (6) **Engine version bumped MINOR** (`2026.04.3.4.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.5.0-alpha.1`) — borderline between PATCH (two bug fixes) and MINOR (new env-var surface in shadow branch + new test contracts), erring on MINOR per CLAUDE.md. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1669 passed in 14.45s** (1663 → 1669, +6 net), zero regressions. PROJECT_CONTEXT.md line 4 synced. **Sprint Paper-Trading COMPLETE — all 4 tasks landed.**
- **Sprint Paper-Trading Task 3: `--paper` CLI flag + multi-mode `_run_server` + 13 new CLI tests** — Closes the user-facing half of the paper-trading sprint by lighting up the CLI entry point Task 2's wiring already supported. After this lands, `python -m quantagent run --paper` boots the runner with paper-mode bots only, on testnet, on port 8001, with traces routed to a separate LangSmith project. The two flags (`--shadow` and `--paper`) are mutually exclusive at the dispatcher layer because one process is one mode — to run both simultaneously the operator starts two tmux sessions on different ports (the post-sprint deployment workflow). **`quantagent/main.py::main()`** dispatcher rewrite: (1) Replaced the old single-flag block with parallel `shadow_requested = "--shadow" in args` / `paper_requested = "--paper" in args` detection, then a top-of-function mutual-exclusion check that prints `"ERROR: --shadow and --paper are mutually exclusive."` + a hint about running them in separate processes and `sys.exit(1)`s BEFORE mutating any env var. The "exit before mutate" ordering is load-bearing — a future refactor that moves the check below the mutations would silently leak a stale flag into the next process in the same shell session. (2) The shadow branch is unchanged — `os.environ["QUANTAGENT_SHADOW"] = "1"` and the flag is stripped from argv. (3) The new paper branch sets FOUR env vars: `QUANTAGENT_PAPER=1` (the process marker), `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET=true` (so every adapter built downstream — factory path AND any direct ctor in scripts — uses testnet without anyone having to remember), `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT=quantagent-paper` via plain assignment NOT setdefault (the spec says "overriding whatever is in .env" — keeps paper traces out of the operator's default `quantagent-live` project), and `PORT=8001` via `setdefault` so an explicit operator override (e.g. `PORT=9000` for a third process) still wins. (4) Help text gained a new line: `python -m quantagent run --paper    Load paper bots, testnet exchange + port 8001`. (5) Module docstring updated to document all three modes plus the mutual exclusion contract. **`quantagent/main.py::_run_server()`**: (1) Added `paper_mode = os.environ.get("QUANTAGENT_PAPER") == "1"` alongside the existing `shadow_mode` read. (2) Replaced the `mode_label = "shadow" if shadow_mode else "live"` ternary with an explicit three-branch `if/elif/else` chain: shadow → log `"⚠️ SHADOW MODE — loading shadow bots, simulated execution only"` + `bot_mode = "shadow"`; paper → log `"⚠️ PAPER MODE — real orders on Hyperliquid testnet"` + `bot_mode = "paper"`; else → log `"LIVE MODE — real orders on mainnet"` + `bot_mode = "live"`. The paper banner is at WARNING level (matching shadow) so unusual modes don't blend into INFO noise in journalctl scrollback. (3) `_make_bot_factory` call gets the new `paper_mode=paper_mode` kwarg — Task 2 already added the parameter with default False but main.py was passing the default; now it threads through properly so paper-mode bots get pipelines built with `is_shadow=True` for cycle persistence. (4) The bot-loading line switched from a hard-coded `mode_label` ternary to a straight `await repos.bots.get_active_bots_by_mode(bot_mode)` read of the new resolved variable. The log line `f"Loaded {len(active_bots)} {bot_mode} bots from database"` now displays the right label for all three modes instead of just shadow vs live. (5) Block comment above the detection section rewritten to explain all three modes side-by-side and document the mutual-exclusion contract that lives in `main()`. **`tests/unit/test_main_cli.py`** — NEW FILE, 280 lines — covers the dispatcher contract that the existing `test_main_bot_factory.py` doesn't reach. Five test classes: (1) `TestPaperFlagSetsEnvironment` — six tests for the `--paper` env-var mutation: `QUANTAGENT_PAPER=1`, `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET=true`, `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT=quantagent-paper`, `PORT=8001` default, `PORT=9000` operator override RESPECTED via setdefault, and `--paper` flag stripped from argv before subcommand dispatch (verified by patching `run()` and asserting it WAS called with the residual `["run"]`). (2) `TestShadowPaperMutualExclusion` — four tests: both flags exit with code 1 + the error message; both flags exit BEFORE mutating EITHER env var (defense in depth — pinned by `assert "QUANTAGENT_SHADOW" not in os.environ` after the failed call); shadow-alone negative control (asserts `QUANTAGENT_PAPER` etc are NOT set); paper-alone negative control (asserts `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW` is NOT set). (3) `TestHelpText` — two tests: `--help` mentions `--paper` and the word "testnet"; bare invocation (no args) shows help including `--paper`. (4) `TestPaperModeBotLoading` — one async test using a fresh on-disk SQLite repo: insert one bot per mode (live + shadow + 2× paper), call `get_active_bots_by_mode("paper")`, assert exactly the two paper bot ids come back, then cross-check that "live" returns only the live bot and "shadow" returns only the shadow bot — proves the filter is exact-match and pins the second half of the dispatch chain (CLI → `bot_mode` → repo accessor → correct rows). All 13 tests share an autouse `restore_mode_environment` fixture that does TWO-PHASE isolation: snapshot at setup → CLEAR all five mode env vars at test start → restore the snapshot at teardown. The clear-at-start half is critical because other test files (notably `tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py`) sometimes mutate `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW_BALANCE` and similar; if any of those tests forget to clean up and run before our tests in the pytest collection order, the upstream pollution would leak into our fixture's snapshot and our tests would start with `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW=1` already set — exactly the failure mode I hit on the first full-suite run before adding the clear-at-start step. The new test helpers: `_run_main(*argv)` patches `sys.argv` + `quantagent.main.run`/`migrate`/`seed` to no-ops so the dispatcher returns immediately after parsing flags (these tests are about argv parsing + env-var mutation, NOT about actually starting the server). The async repo fixture uses `pytest_asyncio.fixture` (not the bare `@pytest.fixture` I tried first — that doesn't await the coroutine) and creates a fresh SQLite db at `tmp_path / "test_main_cli.db"` per test. **`quantagent/version.py`** + **`PROJECT_CONTEXT.md` line 4**: bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.3.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.4.0-alpha.1` per CLAUDE.md "new feature → bump MINOR, reset PATCH to 0". The CLI flag + multi-mode server support is a feature add. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) **`--paper` test for "loads paper bots only" lives at the REPO layer, not via running `_run_server()`**. The literal reading of the criterion is "paper mode loads paper bots only", which would imply spinning up `_run_server()` in pytest and asserting on the loaded set. That would couple the test to the entire FastAPI stack + uvicorn + signal handling + a real DB, all for a contract that's actually two pieces: (a) the dispatcher resolves `bot_mode` correctly (covered by the env-var mutation tests + the argv-stripping test), (b) the repo accessor returns the right rows (covered by `test_paper_mode_loads_paper_bots_only`). Splitting and testing each in isolation is faster, more focused, and just as strong an end-to-end pin. (2) **No live-port test for the health endpoint**. The criterion says "Health endpoint at `localhost:8001/v1/health` works for paper mode". I did not add a test that opens a socket on 8001 because socket allocation is brittle in CI and the existing API tests already cover `/v1/health` against the FastAPI app via `httpx.AsyncClient(app=...)` without binding to a real port. The unit-level coverage of "paper mode sets PORT=8001" + the existing API tests for `/v1/health` together pin the contract: if PORT is 8001 and the app responds to `/v1/health`, then `localhost:8001/v1/health` works. Documented as a deferred live-port smoke test for the post-sprint deployment checklist. (3) **`LANGCHAIN_PROJECT` is set unconditionally with `os.environ[...] = ...`**, NOT `setdefault`. The spec says "overriding whatever is in .env" and that's what plain assignment does. Operators who explicitly want a custom project name in paper mode (e.g. `quantagent-paper-staging`) cannot achieve it via env var alone. This is correct for the common case (every operator has `LANGCHAIN_PROJECT=quantagent-live` in `.env` and would NOT want their paper traces landing there), but flagged so future operators understand the asymmetry vs `PORT` (which uses `setdefault` to RESPECT operator overrides). (4) **`bot_mode` resolution moved from a ternary to an `if/elif/else` chain**. Cleaner to read AND a future fourth mode (e.g. `mode="dydx-testnet"`) will hit a real branch instead of falling through to `live` silently. (5) **`shadow_mode` retains its dedicated parameter on `BotRunner.__init__`**, but the new `paper_mode` flag is NOT plumbed through to `BotRunner`. The runner only uses its `shadow_mode` flag for the `mode_label` log line, and `_register_bot` already reads the per-bot `mode` from the bot dict and threads it through `adapter_factory(exchange, mode=mode)` — so the runner's behaviour is correct for paper bots WITHOUT any signature change. Adding a `paper_mode` parameter would be cargo-culting from `shadow_mode` without serving any actual use case. (6) **The test file is a new `tests/unit/test_main_cli.py`** instead of extending `test_main_bot_factory.py`. The existing file is scoped to `_make_bot_factory`; CLI dispatcher tests are about argv parsing + env-var mutation, which is a different scope. Splitting them into separate files keeps each focused. (7) **Autouse fixture does TWO-PHASE isolation (clear at start AND restore at end)**. Reason: other test files mutate similar env vars; if any forget to clean up (or run in a different module-load order), upstream pollution leaks into our fixture's snapshot which then "restores" the polluted value for every test in this file. The two-phase fixture defends against upstream pollution by explicitly clearing the slate at test start. This is the fix I added after the first full-suite run failed with `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW=1` leaked from another file — documented inline at `tests/unit/test_main_cli.py:31-47`. (8) **`run()` / `migrate()` / `seed()` are patched out as no-ops** in `_run_main()` so the dispatcher returns immediately after argv parsing. These tests are about CLI parsing + env-var mutation, NOT about actually starting the server, running migrations, or seeding the DB — those have their own coverage elsewhere. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1663 passed in 13.79s** (1650 → 1663, +13 net), zero regressions. - **Sprint Paper-Trading Task 2: `mode="paper"` on ExchangeFactory + `is_shadow` plumbing through pipeline + auto-derive in `save_bot`** — Adds the third execution mode to the per-bot mode pattern: paper trading. Paper mode is the simplest of the three (live/shadow/paper) — it's just the real registered adapter constructed with `testnet=True`. Real signing capability, real order routing, but the venue's testnet endpoint, so fills come from the real testnet orderbook with fake money. Distinct from shadow mode because shadow uses a `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` with virtual fills against a real-data delegate; paper uses NO wrapping and NO key scrubbing. The whole point is to validate the production execution path against a real venue without risking mainnet funds. **`exchanges/factory.py`**: (1) New `_paper_instances: dict[str, ExchangeAdapter] = {}` cache, kept distinct from `_instances` and `_shadow_instances` so all three caches can hold the same exchange name simultaneously. (2) `get_adapter(name, mode, **kwargs)` gains a `mode == "paper"` branch that delegates to the new `_build_paper_adapter` method. (3) `_build_paper_adapter(name, **kwargs)` looks up the cached paper instance, falls through to `cls._registry[name](testnet=True, **kwargs)` if not cached, caches the result, and returns. **`testnet=True` is FORCED, not defaulted**: even if the caller passes `testnet=False` explicitly the factory pops the kwarg and re-injects `True` — paper mode can never accidentally hit mainnet (for mainnet routing the operator must explicitly ask for `mode="live"`). (4) Unknown-exchange handling differs from shadow: shadow falls back to a data-less sim (`data_adapter=None` → loud `RuntimeError` on first `fetch_ohlcv`); paper raises `ValueError("Unknown exchange: ... (paper mode requires a registered adapter — testnet has no usable fallback)")`. There's no testnet endpoint for an unregistered exchange and pretending otherwise would silently mislead the operator. (5) `reset()` now also clears `_paper_instances`. (6) New `reset_paper_cache()` clears only the paper namespace, mirroring the existing `reset_shadow_cache()` for symmetric test isolation. (7) Module docstring + `ExchangeFactory` class docstring updated to document all three modes side-by-side. (8) The `mode != "live"` ValueError message updated from `"expected 'live' or 'shadow'"` to `"expected 'live', 'shadow', or 'paper'"`. **`engine/pipeline.py::AnalysisPipeline.__init__`**: new `is_shadow: bool = False` keyword param stored on `self._is_shadow`. Defaults to False so every existing test fixture and the live production path remain byte-for-byte unchanged. The `cycle_record` dict written in `run_cycle` now carries `"is_shadow": self._is_shadow` so the cycle save propagates the flag into the database. With the existing `CycleRepository.save_cycle` already reading `cycle.get("is_shadow", False)`, this single dict-key addition is enough to flow the flag end-to-end. The reason the path is at the AnalysisPipeline level (not the executor level) is that the Executor doesn't currently call `save_trade` at all (verified — `grep save_trade engine/` returns no hits in execution code). Trade persistence is a future task; this change pins the WIRING for cycles today and the trade-side wiring will be a one-line change when the executor → trade_repo path lands. **`storage/repositories/postgres.py::PostgresBotRepository.save_bot`** and **`storage/repositories/sqlite.py::SQLiteBotRepository.save_bot`**: extended the existing `is_shadow` auto-derive from `mode == "shadow"` to `mode in ("shadow", "paper")`. Mirrors the previous shadow-only auto-derive byte-for-byte; the only difference is the tuple membership check. Inline comment explains the rationale: paper bots trade on testnet (fake money), so the QuantDataScientist mining job (which reads the `live_*` views that strip `is_shadow=true` rows) must NOT see paper-bot fills as real alpha. With the auto-derive in place, ANY bot inserted with `mode="paper"` (including bots inserted via raw SQL like the post-sprint deployment script) gets `is_shadow=true` automatically — single source of truth, no caller responsibility. **`quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory`**: new `paper_mode: bool = False` constructor parameter. The factory's `factory_mode` resolution now branches as `if shadow_mode: "shadow"` → `elif paper_mode: "paper"` → `else: "live"`. **Shadow takes precedence over paper** when both flags are set — the CLI dispatcher in Task 3 will reject the combination upstream, but the factory honours one canonical resolution rule regardless. New `pipeline_is_shadow = shadow_mode or paper_mode` is computed once at factory construction and passed to every `AnalysisPipeline(is_shadow=...)` the closure constructs, so shadow-mode AND paper-mode runners both write `is_shadow=true` cycles. (`_run_server` does NOT yet read `QUANTAGENT_PAPER` from env — that's Task 3's job. Task 2 only adds the wiring; the `paper_mode=True` path is dead code until Task 3 lands the env-var read.) **`quantagent/runner.py::BotRunner._register_bot`**: zero changes. The runner already reads `mode = bot.get("mode", "live")` from the bot dict and threads it through to `self._adapter_factory(exchange, mode=mode)` from the shadow-mode redesign. The factory's new paper branch does the rest. **`quantagent/version.py`** + **`PROJECT_CONTEXT.md` line 4**: bumped MINOR `2026.04.3.2.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.3.0-alpha.1` per CLAUDE.md "new feature → bump MINOR, reset PATCH to 0". The new factory mode + new pipeline parameter + new repo auto-derive together constitute a feature add, not a bug fix. **Tests added**: **9 new factory tests** in `tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py::TestPaperModeParameter` plus 1 fix to the existing `test_invalid_mode_raises`. New `_TestnetAwareAdapter` test stub mirrors `HyperliquidAdapter` structure: an inner ccxt-like `_exchange` namespace with `privateKey`/`secret`/`walletAddress`/`apiKey`, plus wrapper-level `_private_key`, plus a constructor that accepts `testnet: bool = False` and stores it on `self._testnet` so the test can verify the factory injected `True`. Its `fetch_ohlcv` override stamps `_testnet_seen=self._testnet` onto the returned candle so the test can prove the testnet=True kwarg actually reached the live adapter `__init__` (not just stored as a side attribute). Tests: (1) `test_1_paper_mode_returns_real_adapter_with_testnet_True` — `get_adapter("hyperliquid", mode="paper")` returns a `_TestnetAwareAdapter` instance with `_testnet is True`. (2) `test_2_paper_mode_does_NOT_scrub_keys` — verifies `_exchange.privateKey == "deadbeef" * 8`, `_exchange.secret == "topsecret"`, `_exchange.walletAddress == "0xWALLET"`, `_private_key == "deadbeef" * 8` — all credential surfaces intact. The autouse `restore_environment` fixture was extended to also snapshot/restore `_paper_instances` so the new cache stays isolated across tests. The existing `test_invalid_mode_raises` was updated to use `mode="bogus-mode"` instead of `mode="paper"` (which is now valid) — inline comment explains the rename. **3 new repo tests** in `tests/unit/test_repositories.py::TestShadowFiltering`: (1) `test_save_bot_paper_mode_auto_derives_is_shadow_true` — inserts a `mode="paper"` bot, asserts it's absent from default `get_active_bots()`, asserts it's present with `is_shadow=True` when `include_shadow=True`. (2) `test_save_bot_live_mode_keeps_is_shadow_false` — negative control: live bots are NOT auto-marked is_shadow. (3) `test_get_active_bots_by_mode_paper_returns_paper_bots` — inserts live + shadow + paper bots, verifies each `get_active_bots_by_mode` call returns only the matching mode (proves the existing by-mode helper works for the new mode value without any accessor changes). **2 new pipeline tests** in `tests/integration/test_pipeline.py::TestPipelineIsShadowFlag`: (1) `test_is_shadow_defaults_to_false` — pipeline built via the existing `_build_pipeline` helper (no `is_shadow=` kwarg) writes cycles with `is_shadow=0`. Pins the existing test-fixture + production-live default. (2) `test_is_shadow_true_persists_into_cycle_record` — pipeline built BY HAND with `is_shadow=True` (the helper doesn't expose the flag, kept its signature unchanged so existing tests don't have to thread False through), runs one cycle, asserts `get_recent_cycles(include_shadow=False)` returns empty AND `get_recent_cycles(include_shadow=True)` returns the row with `is_shadow=1`. End-to-end pin from constructor flag to DB column. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) **`is_shadow` lives at the AnalysisPipeline level, not per-bot at the executor level**. The acceptance criterion says "trades from paper bots have is_shadow=True", but the Executor doesn't currently call `save_trade` at all — trade persistence is a future task. Plumbed `is_shadow` through the path that DOES write today (cycles via `save_cycle`); the trade-side wiring will be a one-line change when the executor → trade_repo path lands because the repo layer already accepts and persists the flag. (2) **`save_bot` auto-derive extended to ALL paper bots, not just process-mode-paper bots**. The simpler reading of the criterion would be "if main.py is launched in paper mode, set is_shadow on the bots it loads". But that's ergonomically backwards: the bot's mode is its identity, not the runner's. Extending the existing shadow auto-derive from `(shadow,)` to `(shadow, paper)` gives single source of truth — ANY bot with `mode="paper"` (including bots inserted via raw SQL, future API endpoints, etc.) gets `is_shadow=True` automatically with no caller responsibility. (3) **No `paper_mode` env-var detection in `_run_server`**. Task 3 owns the `--paper` CLI flag and the env-var read. Task 2 only adds the WIRING — `_make_bot_factory(paper_mode=True)` accepts the new flag with default False, and main.py keeps passing the default until Task 3 lands. (4) **`shadow_mode` takes precedence over `paper_mode`** when both flags are passed to `_make_bot_factory`. Task 3's CLI dispatcher will reject the combination upstream, but the factory honours one canonical resolution rule regardless: shadow → paper → live. (5) **No new column on the `bots` table** — the criterion "`mode` column accepts `paper`" is already true because the column is `VARCHAR(10) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'live'` with no `CHECK` constraint. No Alembic migration needed; verified by inserting a paper bot via the SQLite repo and reading it back. (6) **`_build_paper_adapter` raises `ValueError` for unknown exchanges** instead of falling back like shadow mode does. Paper has no usable fallback (no testnet endpoint for an unregistered exchange), and pretending otherwise would silently mislead the operator. The error message explicitly explains why. (7) **`testnet=True` is FORCED, not defaulted** — `kwargs.pop("testnet", None)` runs before the constructor call, so even an explicit `testnet=False` from the caller is overridden. Pinned by `test_paper_mode_caller_testnet_kwarg_is_overridden`. (8) **Existing test fix**: `test_invalid_mode_raises` previously asserted `mode="paper"` raises — that's no longer true. Updated to use `mode="bogus-mode"` with an inline comment documenting the rename. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1650 passed in 14.96s** (1628 → 1650, +22 net), zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.3.2.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.3.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new factory mode + new pipeline parameter + new repo auto-derive). PROJECT_CONTEXT.md line 4 synced.
