- **Pipeline: live balance fetch from exchange (replaces $10k hardcoded fallback) + decision-driven order sizing in `run_testnet_cycle.py`** — Two related bugs that surfaced during the testnet validation runs. **(1) `engine/pipeline.py` was hardcoding `balance = self._config.account_balance or 10000.0` at line 149**, with a `# TODO: fetch from exchange adapter in production` comment that nobody ever wired. The `TradingConfig.account_balance` field documents `0 = fetch from exchange` but the implementation just substituted $10k whenever the config was 0 — which is the DEFAULT VALUE, so every bot in production was sizing positions against a fictional $10k balance instead of their real wallet. The DecisionAgent's `compute_position_size` then computed risk-based size against the wrong balance, and the resulting position_size was either too aggressive (real balance < $10k → over-risking) or too conservative (real balance > $10k → leaving alpha on the table). **Fix**: new `AnalysisPipeline._resolve_account_balance(symbol, timeframe)` async helper with documented precedence: (a) `TradingConfig.account_balance > 0` → explicit override (used by backtests + eval framework + tests for deterministic position sizing); (b) `account_balance == 0` → calls `self._ohlcv._adapter.get_balance()` and uses the live value (the pipeline already accesses the adapter via the OHLCVFetcher in the flow code path at line 97 — same accessor, no new threading needed through `_make_bot_factory`); (c) exchange call raises OR returns ≤0 → log WARNING + fall back to `_FALLBACK_BALANCE_USD = 10_000.0` so the cycle still runs, with the fallback constant exposed as a class attribute so tests can pin it. The "fall back not skip" choice is deliberate: SKIP-on-error is the default elsewhere in the pipeline, but skipping every cycle on a transient balance fetch error would silently kill the bot's signal flow without the operator noticing — the WARNING log is the loud failure mode, the fallback keeps the cycle moving. `HyperliquidAdapter.get_balance()` already returns `0.0` on its own internal failure (rather than raising), so the "≤0 fallback" branch catches that path too without forcing the adapter to change. The hot path (Stage 4 of `run_cycle`) replaced the one-liner with `balance = await self._resolve_account_balance(symbol, timeframe)`. **(2) `scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` was computing `order_size = round(15.0 / current_price, 5)`** as a hardcoded $15 notional smoke-test size, completely IGNORING the `position_size` field that DecisionAgent had just computed against the real balance with the right risk-per-trade math. So even after the pipeline started reading the live balance, the testnet script was still placing orders sized as if the balance were $15 — the script and the pipeline were giving conflicting answers about how big the order should be, and the script was winning. **Fix**: the script now reads `action.position_size` (the dollar amount DecisionAgent computed via `compute_position_size`, already factoring in conviction multiplier, ATR-based SL distance, and `max_position_pct`), fetches the live balance from the adapter, applies a testnet safety cap of `min(suggested_usd, live_balance * 0.5)` so a misconfigured signal can never wipe more than half the testnet balance on a single smoke-test order, and converts to base-asset quantity via `round(capped_usd / current_price, 5)` (5-decimal precision matches Hyperliquid's `szDecimals` for BTC/ETH/SOL). The order block now PRINTS BOTH the raw suggested $ and the capped $ with a `-- CAP HIT` marker if the cap kicked in, so the operator can see at a glance whether the safety rail intervened. The script also explicitly handles three failure modes: ticker fetch fails (no price → no order), DecisionAgent returned `position_size=None` (e.g. SKIP / HOLD shouldn't reach this branch but defense in depth), and computed size rounds to 0 (notional too small for the precision floor). **4 new tests** in `tests/integration/test_pipeline.py::TestPipelineAccountBalanceResolution`: (1) `test_zero_config_fetches_balance_from_adapter` — config 0 + adapter returns 500 → DecisionAgent receives 500, exactly 1 `get_balance()` call; (2) `test_positive_config_skips_adapter_fetch` — config 25_000 → DecisionAgent receives 25_000, ZERO `get_balance()` calls (preserves the override path); (3) `test_adapter_failure_falls_back_to_constant` — `RuntimeError("API down")` → DecisionAgent receives 10_000, WARNING captured via `caplog`; (4) `test_adapter_returns_zero_falls_back` — adapter returns 0.0 (HyperliquidAdapter's silent-failure path) → DecisionAgent receives 10_000, "non-positive balance" WARNING captured. Tests use a new `_BalanceTrackingAdapter(MockAdapter)` subclass that records call count + lets the test inject a value or an exception, plus a `_BalanceCapturingDecision` shim that wraps the real `DecisionAgent` and records every `account_balance` argument the pipeline passes through — so the assertion is on the END-TO-END flow from config sentinel → adapter call → DecisionAgent input, not on internal helper return values. **Files modified**: `engine/pipeline.py` (~55 lines added: new `_resolve_account_balance` method + `_FALLBACK_BALANCE_USD` class attribute + Stage 4 hot path replacement + explanatory inline comments), `scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` (~50 lines: order block rewritten — adapter balance fetch, suggested vs capped print formatting, three new failure-mode branches, indentation corrected so positions print only inside the success branch), `tests/integration/test_pipeline.py` (+170 lines: new `TestPipelineAccountBalanceResolution` class + `_BalanceTrackingAdapter` + `_BalanceCapturingDecision` shim + `_build_pipeline_with_adapter` helper), `quantagent/version.py` (MINOR bump 1 → 2). **Test count: 1632 → 1636 passing (+4 new tests)**, zero regressions. Engine version `2026.04.3.1.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.2.0-alpha.1` (MINOR — closes the documented "fetch from exchange" sentinel that was never implemented and changes a hot-path semantic for every bot in production).
- **HyperliquidAdapter: dedicated `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET_*` env vars for testnet credentials** — Operators wanted to keep mainnet and testnet keys cleanly separated in `.env` so testnet runs cannot accidentally reuse mainnet credentials (and vice versa). Before this change, `HyperliquidAdapter.__init__` read `HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS` + `HYPERLIQUID_PRIVATE_KEY` unconditionally regardless of `testnet` mode — meaning the only way to run testnet was to swap the env vars in `.env` between runs, which is error-prone and a footgun for shared `.env` files (one stale `export` from a previous mainnet session and you've signed a real-money order with a testnet key, or worse). **`exchanges/hyperliquid.py::__init__`**: testnet detection now happens FIRST (env var or constructor kwarg), so credential lookup can branch on it. When `testnet` is True, the constructor reads `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET_WALLET_ADDRESS` + `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET_PRIVATE_KEY` first, falling back to the mainnet vars (`HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS` / `HYPERLIQUID_PRIVATE_KEY`) for backward compatibility — operators with existing setups continue to work without any `.env` changes. When `testnet` is False (live mode), the constructor reads ONLY the mainnet vars and ignores the testnet pair entirely, so a leftover `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET_*` value in `.env` cannot leak into a mainnet run. Explicit `wallet_address` / `private_key` kwargs still override env vars unconditionally (the existing precedence was preserved). **`scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py`**: env-var resolution updated to mirror the adapter — preferred order is `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET_WALLET_ADDRESS` → `HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS` → `HYPERLIQUID_API_KEY`, and same for the private key. The error message on missing credentials now lists the testnet var first so operators see the correct name in the failure case. After resolution, the script `setdefault`s the testnet vars (not the mainnet ones) so the adapter constructor sees a canonical source. Module docstring updated to document the new precedence. **4 new tests** in `tests/adapters/test_hyperliquid.py::TestCredentialResolution`: (1) `test_testnet_prefers_dedicated_env_vars` — both pairs set, `testnet=True` → testnet pair wins; (2) `test_testnet_falls_back_to_mainnet_vars` — only mainnet pair set, `testnet=True` → falls back to mainnet (BC contract); (3) `test_live_mode_ignores_testnet_vars` — both pairs set, `testnet=False` and `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET` env var unset → live mode reads ONLY mainnet vars (the testnet vars are completely ignored, no leak); (4) `test_explicit_kwargs_override_env` — testnet vars set in env, but `HyperliquidAdapter(wallet_address=..., private_key=..., testnet=True)` uses the explicit kwargs (precedence preserved). All 4 tests use `monkeypatch` for env mutation and `patch("exchanges.hyperliquid.ccxt")` with a `side_effect` capture closure to read the config dict that the adapter passes to the ccxt constructor — this validates the END-TO-END credential flow without requiring a real ccxt instance or network calls. **Files modified**: `exchanges/hyperliquid.py` (~25 lines: testnet detection moved above credential lookup, branched env-var read with fallback chain), `scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` (env-var resolution + error messages + module docstring), `tests/adapters/test_hyperliquid.py` (+95 lines, new `TestCredentialResolution` class), `quantagent/version.py` (MINOR bump 0 → 1, PATCH reset to 0). **Test count: 1628 → 1632 passing (+4 new tests)**, zero regressions. Engine version `2026.04.3.0.1-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.1.0-alpha.1` (MINOR bump per CLAUDE.md "new feature → bump MINOR, reset PATCH to 0").
- **Bugfix: cycle save crashes on PostgreSQL — pipeline stringified the timestamp** — `engine/pipeline.py` was building the `cycle_record` dict with `"timestamp": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()`, an ISO-8601 string. SQLite's TEXT timestamp columns silently coerce strings, so every unit test passed. PostgreSQL's `cycles.timestamp` is `TIMESTAMPTZ`, and asyncpg refuses to bind a string to a TIMESTAMPTZ argument — every shadow-mode `save_cycle` call against the production DB raised `asyncpg.exceptions.DataError: invalid input for query argument $5` and the pipeline aborted with an exception trace. The fix is two-pronged. **Source side** — `engine/pipeline.py:164` now passes a raw `datetime.now(timezone.utc)` object (no `.isoformat()`); same change applied to `engine/memory/cross_bot.py::publish_signal` (was passing `.isoformat()` to `cross_bot_signals.timestamp`, also TIMESTAMPTZ), `api/routes/bots.py::create_bot` (was passing `.isoformat()` to `bots.created_at`, also TIMESTAMPTZ), and `scripts/seed_dev.py::seed_dev_data` (same — `bots.created_at`). **Sink side defense** — `storage/repositories/postgres.py` replaced its `_now_iso() -> str` helper with `_now_utc() -> datetime` AND added a new `_to_datetime(value)` coercion helper that accepts `datetime | ISO-string | None` and returns a tz-aware datetime. Every `save_*` method that previously substituted `_now_iso()` for missing timestamps now calls `_to_datetime(...)` on the input — so legacy callers that still pass an ISO string don't blow up either. Affected save methods: `save_trade` (entry_time, exit_time), `save_cycle` (timestamp), `save_rule` (created_at), `save_bot` (created_at), `save_signal` (timestamp). Tz-naive datetimes get assumed-UTC; trailing `Z` strings get normalized to `+00:00` so `datetime.fromisoformat` accepts them. Unknown types raise `TypeError` so silent corruption is impossible. **Boundary** — `api/routes/bots.py::_bot_to_response` now normalizes `created_at` to ISO string before constructing `BotResponse` (Pydantic v2 strict on `str` fields won't auto-coerce a datetime), so both legacy SQLite-string callers and new asyncpg-datetime returns serialize correctly through the API. **Why it took until now to find** — every existing PostgreSQL repo test path saved trades/cycles via mocks that accepted strings; the live shadow-mode runner is the first code path that actually exercised `save_cycle` against asyncpg with a real string timestamp, and it fired on the very first cycle. **Test added**: `tests/unit/test_repositories.py::TestCycleRepository::test_save_cycle_with_datetime_timestamp` constructs a cycle with a tz-aware `datetime(2026, 4, 9, 16, 43, 8, tzinfo=utc)` and saves via the SQLite repo, then asserts the round-trip preserves the wall-clock instant and the JSON columns. The test pins the contract that `save_cycle` accepts a datetime object on BOTH backends — so any future regression that accidentally re-stringifies the timestamp will fail SQLite immediately, no longer silently passing. **Audit**: grepped every `.isoformat()` call site in the repo to find dicts that flow into a `*_repo.save_*` method. Hit all 4 production sites (pipeline, cross_bot, api/routes/bots, seed_dev). The remaining `.isoformat()` calls are either (a) in-memory result dicts that never touch the DB (`engine/trader_bot.py` lifecycle `result`, `engine/bot_manager.py` crash result, `sentinel/reaper.py` orphan record, `engine/memory/regime_history.py` ring buffer), (b) display-only formatting (scripts that print the time, tracking modules whose `event.timestamp` is already a datetime that they explicitly stringify for JSON serialization), or (c) test fixtures (`tests/test_mcp/`, `tests/unit/test_forward_r.py`, `tests/unit/test_repositories.py` itself — all SQLite, all string-tolerant). Files modified: `engine/pipeline.py`, `engine/memory/cross_bot.py`, `storage/repositories/postgres.py` (~40 lines: `_now_iso` → `_now_utc`, new `_to_datetime` helper, 5 save_* method updates), `api/routes/bots.py` (`create_bot` + `_bot_to_response` datetime→str normalization), `scripts/seed_dev.py`, `tests/unit/test_repositories.py` (+34 lines test), `quantagent/version.py` (PATCH bump 0 → 1). **Test count: 1627 → 1628 passing (+1 new regression test).** Engine version `2026.04.3.0.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.0.1-alpha.1` (PATCH bump per CLAUDE.md "bug fix → bump PATCH").
- **Sprint Paper-Trading Task 1: `scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` — one-shot Hyperliquid testnet validation script** — First task of the Paper-Trading sprint. A standalone, additive script that runs ONE complete analysis cycle (data → 4 signals → conviction → decision) against Hyperliquid TESTNET and, if the pipeline outputs LONG or SHORT, places one small real market order on the testnet orderbook. Exists so we can validate the entire production pipeline against a live venue (real OHLCV, real orderbook, real fills) WITHOUT touching mainnet money — and BEFORE landing the broader `mode="paper"` work in Tasks 2-4 that would let TraderBots run continuously in paper mode. **`scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` (425 lines, NEW file, no existing files modified)**. **CLI**: `python scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py [--symbol BTC-USDC] [--timeframe 1h]`. Both args have defaults so the bare command works. Help text rendered via argparse. **Env-var contract**: requires `HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET=true` (mandatory — script refuses to run without it, hard exit 1 with the error message `"ERROR: HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET=true is required for this script. This script ONLY runs against testnet."`), `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (Claude credentials), and `HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS` + `HYPERLIQUID_PRIVATE_KEY` (the adapter-native env var names — see deviation #1 below). The .env loader is copied byte-for-byte from `scripts/run_trade.py` so the script reads `_PROJECT_ROOT/.env` if present and respects the same quoting / inline-comment rules. **Script flow**: (1) `_load_env()` to populate from .env. (2) Mandatory env-var safety checks; missing → exit 1 BEFORE constructing any objects. (3) Resolve credentials with the `HYPERLIQUID_API_KEY/SECRET` aliases as fallbacks (see deviation #1). (4) Configure logging at INFO level, silence the noisy third-party loggers (httpx, httpcore, anthropic, ccxt, matplotlib, urllib3). (5) Print the run banner with symbol/timeframe/UTC timestamp. (6) Construct the adapter on a CLEAN factory cache: `ExchangeFactory._instances.pop("hyperliquid", None)` (defense against stale non-testnet cache hits — the factory's live path keys only by `name`, NOT by kwargs, so without the explicit pop a previously-cached non-testnet adapter would be returned and the `testnet=True` kwarg would be silently swallowed) → `import exchanges.hyperliquid` for registration → `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter("hyperliquid", testnet=True)`. (7) Defense-in-depth testnet check: read `adapter._testnet` back off the constructed adapter and assert it's True; if not, exit 1 BEFORE running the pipeline (no LLM cost burned, no order risk taken). (8) Print endpoint URL via `_adapter_endpoint(adapter)` helper that walks `adapter._exchange.urls['api']` and handles both the str and dict variants ccxt uses depending on which call type was last invoked. (9) Print wallet + balance via `await adapter.get_balance()`. (10) Wire the full pipeline — `TradingConfig`, `InProcessBus` (with sync-capture lambdas for `SignalsReady` and `ConvictionScored` so we can pretty-print them after the cycle without interleaving with pipeline logging, plus event lifecycle prints for `DataReady` / `SignalsReady` / `ConvictionScored` / `CycleCompleted`), `_CostTrackingLLM(ClaudeProvider(api_key))` (see deviation #6), SQLite repos, `OHLCVFetcher`, `FlowAgent([CryptoFlowProvider()])`, `SignalRegistry` populated with `IndicatorAgent` + `PatternAgent` + `TrendAgent` + `FlowSignalAgent` (4 producers, FeatureFlags-gated), `ConvictionAgent`, `DecisionAgent`, full `AnalysisPipeline` with `bot_id="testnet-cycle"` / `user_id="dev-testnet"`. (11) Run `pipeline.run_cycle()` with wall-clock timing. (12) Pretty-print captured signals (one line per producer with name/direction/confidence + first 160 chars of reasoning), captured conviction (score/direction/regime + factual/subjective weights + reasoning), and the full `TradeAction` (action/conviction/SL/TP1/TP2/RR/size/reasoning). (13) **Order placement** (only if `action.action in ("LONG", "SHORT")`): fetch ticker → compute `order_size = round(15.0 / current_price, 5)` (~$15 notional with $5 buffer over Hyperliquid's $10 minimum, 5-decimal precision matches Hyperliquid's BTC/ETH/SOL `szDecimals`) → print "PLACING ORDER on testnet..." → `await adapter.place_market_order(symbol, side, size)` → on success print order_id/fill_price/fill_size, sleep 2s, fetch and print positions; on failure print the error. CLOSE_ALL/HOLD/SKIP all print a no-order message. (14) Final "Run summary" banner with `llm.call_count`, `llm.total_cost`, `llm.total_latency_ms`, pipeline wall clock, and total events emitted. **`_CostTrackingLLM` shim class** (in-script, not exported): delegates `generate_text` / `generate_vision` to a wrapped `ClaudeProvider` and accumulates `response.cost` + `response.latency_ms` + `call_count` per call. Built because `ClaudeProvider` does NOT expose accumulated totals — costs are only emitted per-call as INFO log lines, and the spec said "do NOT modify any existing files". The shim is the cleanest way to capture totals without touching `llm/claude.py`. **`_adapter_endpoint(adapter)` helper**: walks `adapter._exchange.urls['api']` defensively (it's sometimes a string, sometimes a dict keyed by call type — depends on which call last triggered ccxt's url builder). Returns "(no api URL)" / "(no urls dict)" / "(adapter has no _exchange — cannot inspect)" for the unhappy paths so the script never crashes during pretty-printing. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) **Env var names**. Spec said "require `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `HYPERLIQUID_API_KEY`, `HYPERLIQUID_API_SECRET`" but `HyperliquidAdapter.__init__` actually reads `HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS` + `HYPERLIQUID_PRIVATE_KEY` (`exchanges/hyperliquid.py:117-118`). Picking the spec's names alone would give the script's env-var checks no relationship to the env vars the adapter actually consumes — the script would happily report "all credentials present" while the adapter constructed with `walletAddress=None` and silently failed at the first `fetch_balance()` call. Compromise: accept BOTH pairs, prefer the adapter-native names, and after resolution call `os.environ.setdefault("HYPERLIQUID_WALLET_ADDRESS", wallet)` + `os.environ.setdefault("HYPERLIQUID_PRIVATE_KEY", private_key)` so the adapter sees one canonical source regardless of which alias the operator set. Documented in the script docstring + inline at the env-check block. (2) **Order method name**. Spec said `adapter.place_order()`, but the `ExchangeAdapter` ABC defines `place_market_order(symbol, side, size)` (and `place_limit_order` separately). Used `place_market_order` since the spec specifies "small market order". (3) **Order size computation**. Spec said "minimum size for the symbol", but `HyperliquidAdapter` does NOT expose a min-lot accessor — the only authoritative min-lot info lives inside CCXT's `markets` dict and would require a `load_markets()` call plus per-symbol parsing. Substituted a deterministic formula: `round(15.0 / current_price, 5)`. The 15.0 numerator targets a $15 notional (Hyperliquid's min is $10, so $5 buffer for slippage); the round-to-5 matches the standard `szDecimals=5` for BTC/ETH/SOL on Hyperliquid mainnet. For BTC at $70k that's 0.00021 BTC ≈ $14.70. Inline comment explains the math. (4) **Testnet endpoint print** + **defense-in-depth check**. Spec said "Print the endpoint URL to confirm it's testnet". `HyperliquidAdapter` does NOT expose a public `endpoint()` method, so the script reads `adapter._exchange.urls['api']` directly via the `_adapter_endpoint` helper. INDEPENDENTLY, the script also asserts `adapter._testnet is True` BEFORE running the pipeline — if the testnet flag did not stick (custom factory dropping kwargs, env-var typo, etc.) the script exits with code 1 BEFORE any LLM call or order placement. The dual check is intentional defense in depth — printing the URL is for the operator's eyes, asserting `_testnet` is for the machine. (5) **Factory cache reset**. Spec didn't mention this, but the live-mode factory cache (`_instances`) keys ONLY on `name`, not on `(name, kwargs)`. So `get_adapter("hyperliquid", testnet=True)` after a stale cache hit would return the cached non-testnet adapter and silently drop the `testnet=True` kwarg. The script defensively `_instances.pop("hyperliquid", None)`s the live cache before constructing. The `_shadow_instances` cache is untouched (this script doesn't use shadow mode at all). (6) **LLM cost tracking via `_CostTrackingLLM` shim**. Spec said "Print total LLM cost and latency". `ClaudeProvider` doesn't expose accumulated totals — costs are emitted per-call as INFO log lines. Spec also said "Do NOT modify any existing files." Resolved by writing a 23-line in-script wrapper class that delegates both `generate_text` and `generate_vision` to a wrapped `ClaudeProvider`, accumulating `response.cost` and `response.latency_ms` per call. Printed as the final "Run summary" banner. (7) **SQLite repo backend** (matches `scripts/run_trade.py`). The cycle / rule / cross-bot writes from one one-shot test cycle are throwaway — using PostgreSQL would require DB credentials in the operator's shell and a schema migration check. SQLite is created fresh each run by `get_repositories("sqlite")`. (8) **No pytest coverage added**. The script is operational tooling under `scripts/`, NOT a library module — adding pytest tests would couple the test runner to local PostgreSQL and Hyperliquid testnet credentials. Smoke-tested manually: `python scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py --help` parses argparse and prints the help text; `env -u HYPERLIQUID_TESTNET python scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` exits with code 1 and prints the missing-env-var error message — proving the import path is clean and the first safety guard fires correctly. The downstream guards (ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, wallet, private_key) are simple chained env-var checks of the same form so they're not separately tested. The full live network path was deliberately NOT smoke-tested to avoid burning LLM cost or risking an unattended testnet order. **Verification**: no existing files modified (verified via `git status` showing only the new `scripts/run_testnet_cycle.py` plus the docs updates), test count unchanged at **1627 passing** (no need to re-run pytest because no library code was touched). Engine version unchanged at `2026.04.3.0.0-alpha.1` (no bump — additive operational tooling, no public-surface change).
- **LLM Determinism Audit: Eval Judge `temperature=0.0` verified + audit table** — Pre-baseline check before the 200-scenario eval run, requested so the judge's scoring is deterministic and any future drift between runs can be attributed to the agent under test, NOT to LLM sampling noise on the judge side. **Audit scope**: grepped every `generate_text` / `generate_vision` / `client.messages.create` call site across the codebase, classified each by purpose (signal agent / conviction / decision / reflection / judge / MCP / other), and recorded the temperature value at the call site. **Production call sites (9 total)**: (1) `engine/signals/indicator_agent.py:86` IndicatorAgent text — `0.3`. (2) `engine/signals/pattern_agent.py:100` PatternAgent vision — `0.3`. (3) `engine/signals/trend_agent.py:96` TrendAgent vision — `0.3`. (4) `engine/conviction/agent.py:177` ConvictionAgent text — `0.3`. (5) `engine/execution/agent.py:143` DecisionAgent text — `0.2`. (6) `engine/reflection/agent.py:62` ReflectionAgent text — `0.4`. (7) `mcp/quant_scientist/agent.py:186` QuantDataScientist text — `0.3` (via module-level `_LLM_TEMPERATURE`). (8) `mcp/macro_regime/agent.py:310` MacroRegimeManager text — `0.2` (via module-level `_LLM_TEMPERATURE`). (9) `backtesting/evals/judge.py:153` Eval Judge text — **`0.0` (already deterministic)**. Non-production: `scripts/debug_agents.py` has 4 calls (debug ping at 0.0, three manual agent reruns at 0.3 — acceptable, debug-only). **LLMProvider abstraction status**: `llm/base.py::LLMProvider.generate_text` and `generate_vision` ALREADY accept `temperature: float = 0.3` as a kw param (lines 32 and 45), and `llm/claude.py::ClaudeProvider._call` ALREADY threads it through to `client.messages.create(temperature=temperature)` at line 167. The temperature plumbing was correct from day one — no ABC change needed, no Claude-impl change needed. **Result**: The eval judge was already calling `generate_text(..., temperature=0.0, ...)` (line 158 of `backtesting/evals/judge.py`). **No code changes were made** — this task was a pure verification + audit. The eight pipeline-agent temperatures (0.2-0.4) were INTENTIONALLY left untouched per task instructions: agent temperatures will be tuned separately AFTER the 200-scenario eval baseline is established with current settings, then changed one variable at a time to attribute every score delta to a specific change. **Spec deviations**: (1) The task spec said "If [the abstraction] doesn't support temperature, add `temperature: float = 1.0` to the base ABC" — but the abstraction already supports temperature with default `0.3` (NOT 1.0). The default was chosen at the original design time to give pipeline agents low-but-not-zero variance; changing the ABC default to 1.0 now would silently raise temperature on every existing caller that doesn't pass an explicit value. Since every production caller DOES pass an explicit value (verified by the audit), the default never fires in practice; left it at 0.3 for consistency with existing tests. (2) The task spec said "find the LLM call that scores pipeline outputs ... ensure it passes temperature=0" — judge already passed `temperature=0.0` (it was set during the original judge implementation). The task is therefore VERIFICATION ONLY, not a fix. The audit table is the real deliverable. (3) Audit report printed to chat (markdown table) rather than to a script-output file — no operational tooling needed since the audit is a one-shot verification before the eval baseline run. **Verification**: no code changes, no test changes, test count unchanged at **1627 passing**. Engine version unchanged at `2026.04.3.0.0-alpha.1` (no bump — pure verification, no code touched).
- **Sprint Shadow-Redesign Task 4: Nuke shadow infrastructure + rewire main.py + BotRunner per-bot mode** — Closes the Shadow-Redesign sprint by deleting the legacy env-var-driven shadow infrastructure entirely and rewiring the production startup path around the per-row mode column from Task 1 + the explicit `mode` parameter from Task 3. After this lands, a `--shadow` boot is just `os.environ["QUANTAGENT_SHADOW"] = "1"` plus mode-filtered bot loading; there is NO DB swap, NO config mutation, NO shadow-DB pre-create, and NO separate startup path. **Files DELETED**: (1) `backtesting/shadow.py` — the entire 339-line module is gone. Removed: `is_shadow_mode()`, `enable_shadow_mode()`, `disable_shadow_mode()`, `_SHADOW_ENV_VAR`, `_SHADOW_SUFFIX`, `_TRUTHY`, `get_shadow_db_url()`, `_shadow_network_db_url()`, `_shadow_sqlite_url_string()`, `ShadowConfig` dataclass, `configure_shadow()`, `_set()`, `_get()`, `ensure_shadow_db()`, `_create_postgres_db_if_missing()`, `_run_alembic_upgrade()`. Every function this module exposed has either been replaced by an explicit-mode pattern (factory swap, repo filter) or is dead because the use case it served (separate shadow DB) no longer exists. (2) `scripts/debug_shadow.py` — the diagnostic script written to investigate the OLD broken shadow path. It imported `configure_shadow`, `ensure_shadow_db`, `is_shadow_mode`, `_RuntimeConfig` and walked through the legacy startup sequence step-by-step. With the legacy path gone, the script can't even import. Deleted instead of repaired because the new mode-driven path is straightforward enough that a generic startup smoke test (`python -m quantagent.main run --shadow`) is sufficient — there's no labyrinth left to diagnose. **`backtesting/__init__.py`**: removed the `from backtesting.shadow import (...)` block and the corresponding entries from `__all__`. The package's public surface no longer exposes ANY shadow-mode helper. **`quantagent/main.py` rewrite**. (a) `_setup_logging()`: added `force=True` to `logging.basicConfig(...)` so handlers installed by uvicorn / anthropic / ccxt at import time don't silently no-op the engine's startup log lines (this was diagnostic root cause #5 from the previous shadow-hang investigation — the "Initializing infrastructure..." line never appeared because something had touched root handlers first). Inline comment explains why. (b) `_make_bot_factory()` gains a `shadow_mode: bool = False` parameter. The closure resolves `factory_mode = "shadow" if shadow_mode else "live"` ONCE at construction time and threads it through to `adapter = adapter_factory(exchange, mode=factory_mode)` for every spawned TraderBot. Since main.py loads bots filtered by mode at startup, every bot the factory sees belongs to the same mode as the runner — there's no mismatch case in production. (c) `_run_server()` is rewritten end-to-end. Removed: the `from backtesting.shadow import (ensure_shadow_db, is_shadow_mode)` import, the `if is_shadow_mode():` block, the `await ensure_shadow_db(shadow_url)` call, and the warning log that referenced "shadow database". Replaced with: `shadow_mode = os.environ.get("QUANTAGENT_SHADOW") == "1"`; if true, log `"⚠️ SHADOW MODE — loading shadow bots, simulated execution only"`. The `adapter_factory` closure now accepts `mode: str = "live"` and forwards it to `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter(exchange, mode=mode)`. The bot factory call gets `shadow_mode=shadow_mode`. The `BotRunner(...)` constructor call gets `shadow_mode=shadow_mode`. Bot loading switched from `await repos.bots.get_active_bots()` to `mode_label = "shadow" if shadow_mode else "live"; active_bots = await repos.bots.get_active_bots_by_mode(mode_label)` — a shadow boot loads ONLY shadow bots, a live boot loads ONLY live bots. The "Loaded N bots" log line includes the mode label. (d) `main()` CLI dispatcher: deleted the `_RuntimeConfig` class and the `from backtesting.shadow import configure_shadow` + `configure_shadow(_RuntimeConfig)` call. The `--shadow` flag handling collapsed to a single line: `os.environ["QUANTAGENT_SHADOW"] = "1"`. Help text updated from "Same runner, sim exchange + shadow DB" to "Load shadow bots, simulated execution". **`quantagent/runner.py` rewrite**. `BotRunner.__init__` accepts `shadow_mode: bool = False` keyword param, stores as `self._shadow_mode`, exposes via a `shadow_mode` property. `_register_bot(bot)` reads `mode = bot.get("mode", "live")` from the bot dict (defaults to live for backward compat with rows that pre-date Alembic 003) and threads it through to `adapter = self._adapter_factory(exchange, mode=mode)` when constructing the per-symbol sentinel. Inline docstring explains the relationship between the process-wide `shadow_mode` flag and the per-bot `mode` field: in a single-mode runner they always agree (because main.py filters bots by mode), in a mixed-mode runner (the integration test) the per-bot mode wins so each sentinel gets the right adapter type. **Test fixes**. (1) `tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py`: deleted 19 obsolete tests covering the deleted symbols — `test_shadow_mode_off_by_default`, `test_shadow_mode_on_when_env_var_set`, the parameterised `test_truthy_env_values_enable_shadow` (7 cases) and `test_falsy_env_values_keep_shadow_off` (6 cases), `test_enable_and_disable_shadow`, the 9 `get_shadow_db_url` URL-transform tests, the 4 `configure_shadow` mutation tests, and the `test_end_to_end_configure_then_factory_returns_sim` integration test. The remaining 16 tests (factory mode swap + key scrubbing from Task 3) all stayed; the file's module docstring was rewritten to explain the deletion. The `restore_environment` fixture lost the `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW` / `DATABASE_URL` env-var snapshotting since no remaining test touches them. The `dataclass` import + `_Cfg` helper class were removed. (2) `tests/unit/test_runner.py`: the `adapter_factory` fixture now accepts an optional `mode: str = "live"` kwarg and caches by `(exchange, mode)` so each (exchange, mode) tuple gets a distinct adapter — this lets new mode tests verify a shadow bot and a live bot for the same exchange receive different adapter instances. The MagicMock adapter also stores its mode on `_mode` for assertion. (3) `tests/unit/test_main_bot_factory.py`: every test's `adapter_factory` lambda was updated to accept `(exchange, mode="live")` because the `_make_bot_factory` closure now calls `adapter_factory(exchange, mode=factory_mode)`. (4) Added 5 new tests in `tests/unit/test_runner.py::TestPerBotMode`: `test_shadow_mode_constructor_param_default_false`, `test_shadow_mode_constructor_param_true`, `test_register_bot_threads_per_bot_mode_to_adapter` (two bots different symbols + different modes → two distinct sentinel adapters with the right `_mode` markers), `test_register_bot_defaults_to_live_when_mode_missing` (legacy bot dict without `mode` key still works), and `test_mixed_mode_runner_uses_real_adapter_classes` — the spec's required integration test: registers `_LiveAdapter` with the REAL `ExchangeFactory`, builds a `real_adapter_factory` closure that calls `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter(exchange, mode=mode)`, creates a `BotRunner` with two bot configs (one `mode='live'` BTC-USDC, one `mode='shadow'` ETH-USDC), starts them in one runner, and asserts the live sentinel's adapter is an `_LiveAdapter` instance and the shadow sentinel's adapter is a `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` instance. The factory state is snapshotted + restored via try/finally so the test can't poison the suite-wide registry. (5) Added 1 new test in `tests/unit/test_main_bot_factory.py`: `test_factory_passes_shadow_mode_to_adapter_factory` — `_make_bot_factory(shadow_mode=True)` must call its `adapter_factory` with `mode='shadow'` for every spawned bot. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The spec said "Server starts cleanly with `python -m quantagent.main run --shadow` and logs 'Loaded N shadow bots' followed by 'started with N bots, M sentinels'". The first log line lands as `"Loaded {N} shadow bots from database"` (matches the spec literally). The second log line is unchanged from `BotRunner.start_with_bots`: `"BotRunner: started with {N} bots, {M} sentinels"`. Verified by smoke-running `python -m quantagent.main --help` (full server start requires DB credentials, so it's left to the post-sprint deployment checklist). (2) The spec said "Add integration test: create 2 bot configs (one mode='live', one mode='shadow'), start BotRunner, assert the shadow bot's sentinel uses SimulatedExchangeAdapter and the live bot's sentinel uses the real adapter". Implemented as `test_mixed_mode_runner_uses_real_adapter_classes` — uses different SYMBOLS for the two bots so the `if symbol not in self._sentinels` short-circuit doesn't make them share a sentinel (which would be a bug case the test ISN'T meant to cover — same-symbol-different-mode is technically possible but isn't a Task 4 acceptance criterion). The integration test imports `_LiveAdapter` from `tests.test_backtesting.test_shadow` for adapter-class isolation; this couples the two test files but the alternative is duplicating the 50-line stub. (3) The `_make_bot_factory` closure passes `mode=factory_mode` to its inner `adapter_factory`, where `factory_mode` is set ONCE from the constructor's `shadow_mode` flag. This means within a single BotRunner, every spawned TraderBot's executor sees the same mode — consistent with the production assumption that one runner runs one mode. The integration test exercises BOTH modes within ONE runner via the SENTINEL adapter path (which IS per-bot via `_register_bot`), but the EXECUTOR adapter inside the spawned TraderBot would still use the runner's process-wide mode if the bot factory ever fired. The integration test doesn't actually spawn a TraderBot (it only checks sentinel construction), so this gap doesn't affect test correctness. Closing the gap fully would require threading per-bot mode through `BotManager.spawn_bot` → `factory(symbol, bot_id, mode=...)` → executor adapter, which is a wider refactor flagged for a follow-up task. The single-mode happy path (one runner, one mode) is unaffected. (4) `scripts/debug_shadow.py` was deleted in full rather than rewritten because the new mode-driven path is simple enough that step-by-step instrumentation isn't needed; if a shadow boot fails, the existing logging is sufficient to diagnose. (5) Test count dropped from 1651 → 1627 (-24): -29 deleted tests (with parameterisation expansion) + 5 new TestPerBotMode tests + 1 new test_main_bot_factory test = -23 net (the +1 difference is one of the parameterised cases). Net loss is intentional — every deleted test covered code that no longer exists. (6) `test_end_to_end_configure_then_factory_returns_sim` was the only test that exercised both `configure_shadow` AND the new explicit-mode factory path simultaneously; it was deliberately deleted because (a) `configure_shadow` doesn't exist anymore and (b) the factory's explicit-mode path is exhaustively covered by `TestShadowModeParameter` from Task 3. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1627 passed in 15.06s**, zero regressions. CLI smoke: `python -m quantagent.main --help` prints the updated help text including `run --shadow   Load shadow bots, simulated execution`. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.21.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.3.0.0-alpha.1 (MAJOR — public surface changes: `backtesting/shadow.py` deleted entirely, `BotRunner.__init__` signature gained a new param, `quantagent.main._make_bot_factory` signature gained a new param, `backtesting/__init__.py` no longer re-exports any shadow helpers). Sprint Shadow-Redesign COMPLETE — all 4 tasks landed. 1627 tests passing.
- **Sprint Shadow-Redesign Task 3: ExchangeFactory per-bot `mode` parameter + signing-key scrubbing** — Replaces the global `is_shadow_mode()` env-var check inside `ExchangeFactory` with an explicit `mode` argument on `get_adapter`, and adds defense-in-depth signing-key scrubbing on the live adapter that gets wrapped as the shadow sim's data delegate. After this lands, a single BotRunner process can host both live and shadow bots side-by-side because the shadow swap is per-call instead of process-global. Task 4 will rip the env-var path out entirely; Task 3 makes the new path the only one the factory honours. **`exchanges/factory.py` rewrite**: `get_adapter(name: str, mode: str = "live", **kwargs)` now branches on mode at the top of the method. `mode="live"` keeps the existing behaviour byte-for-byte (registry lookup → cached singleton in `_instances`); `mode="shadow"` delegates to `_build_shadow_adapter(name, **kwargs)`; any other mode value raises `ValueError("Unknown adapter mode: <repr> (expected 'live' or 'shadow')")` rather than silently falling through, so a typo in a config can't accidentally place real trades. The `from backtesting.shadow import is_shadow_mode` import and the `if is_shadow_mode():` branch are GONE. The old `_get_shadow_adapter` private method was renamed to `_build_shadow_adapter` to reflect that it's an explicit mode-driven entry point now, not an env-var fallback. Live (`_instances`) and shadow (`_shadow_instances`) caches stay in separate dicts so toggling between modes within one process can never poison the other namespace. **`_build_shadow_adapter` flow**: (1) cache hit in `_shadow_instances` → return immediately. (2) Pop `initial_balance` from kwargs (it's consumed by the sim, NOT forwarded to the live constructor — without the pop, ccxt would reject it as an unknown kwarg). Resolve balance from kwarg → `QUANTAGENT_SHADOW_BALANCE` env → `_DEFAULT_SHADOW_BALANCE` (10_000.0). (3) If the requested name is in `_registry`, construct the live adapter via `cls._registry[name](**kwargs)`, then immediately call `_scrub_signing_keys(adapter)`. If construction raises (typically a missing-credentials error in dev), the failure is logged at ERROR via `logger.exception(...)` and `data_adapter` falls through to `None` — the operator will then see an explicit `RuntimeError("no data source")` on the first `fetch_ohlcv` call, which is the loud failure mode (NOT a silent crash at process boot). (4) Wrap in `SimulatedExchangeAdapter(initial_balance=balance, data_adapter=scrubbed_live, name=f"shadow-{name}")`, cache, return. **`_scrub_signing_keys(adapter)` helper**: walks two distinct layers of credential storage. **Inner ccxt layer** (`_CCXT_SIGNING_ATTRS = ("privateKey", "secret")`): the `HyperliquidAdapter` stores its credentials inside the underlying `ccxt.hyperliquid` object on `self._exchange`; the scrubber sets both `inner.privateKey = None` and `inner.secret = None`. `privateKey` is what hyperliquid uses for signing; `secret` is the standard ccxt name on most other venues — both go to None so the scrub works on every adapter that conforms to the ccxt convention. **Wrapper-level layer** (`_ADAPTER_SIGNING_ATTRS = ("_private_key", "private_key", "_secret")`): handles future adapters that might store credentials directly on the wrapper class outside the ccxt object (e.g. a non-ccxt direct-API adapter). Setattr failures (e.g. `__slots__` or read-only properties) are caught and logged at DEBUG — the sim's order layer is the primary defense; scrubbing is hardening, not a hard guarantee. **What is NOT scrubbed**: `walletAddress` on the inner ccxt object (load-bearing input to `fetch_user_fees` and account metadata), and `apiKey` (a public identifier on most venues; signing requires the paired `secret` which IS gone). The exact attribute lists are module-level tuples so future adapters can be audited at a glance and unit tests can pin them. **Existing test migration**: 9 tests in `tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py` previously toggled the factory swap via `enable_shadow_mode()` / `disable_shadow_mode()` environment-variable side effects. Each was rewritten to pass `mode="shadow"` explicitly. The two callers that test the live path (`test_factory_returns_real_adapter_when_not_shadow`, `test_factory_reset_shadow_cache_only`) drop the `disable_shadow_mode()` setup line because the factory no longer reads the env var at all. `test_end_to_end_configure_then_factory_returns_sim` was rewritten to verify the OPPOSITE invariant — that even after `configure_shadow(cfg)` flips the env var, the factory still returns a live adapter unless `mode="shadow"` is passed explicitly, AND the explicit-mode call returns a sim regardless. This test will be deleted entirely in Task 4 along with `configure_shadow`, but for now it documents the per-call swap. **7 new tests** in `tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py::TestShadowModeParameter` (one extra over the 6 in the spec). New `_CredentialedAdapter` test helper at module scope: extends `_LiveAdapter` with both layers of credential storage — an inner `_InnerCcxt` namespace object holding `privateKey` / `secret` / `walletAddress` / `apiKey`, plus a wrapper-level `_private_key` attribute. Its `place_market_order` override raises `RuntimeError("auth: no signing key configured...")` if both layers are scrubbed, so test 5 can prove the scrubbed adapter actively REFUSES to place an order. Tests: (1) `test_1_shadow_mode_returns_simulated_exchange_adapter` — `get_adapter("hyperliquid", mode="shadow")` returns a `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` with `name() == "shadow-hyperliquid"`. (2) `test_2_shadow_data_adapter_has_nulled_private_key` — extracts `adapter._data_adapter`, asserts both `_exchange.privateKey` AND `_exchange.secret` AND wrapper-level `_private_key` are all `None`. (3) `test_3_shadow_data_adapter_wallet_address_is_preserved` — asserts `_exchange.walletAddress == "0xWALLET"` and `_exchange.apiKey == "public-id-not-secret"` survive the scrub. (4) `test_4_shadow_fetch_ohlcv_delegates_to_real_adapter` — uses a `_SpyAdapter` subclass that records every `fetch_ohlcv` call as a tuple, calls `adapter.fetch_ohlcv("BTC-USDC", "1h", limit=1)` via `asyncio.run`, asserts the spy received exactly one call with the matching args AND the candle list matches the spy's canned response. Proves the read-only delegate path is wired end-to-end. (5) `test_5_shadow_place_order_uses_virtual_portfolio_not_data_adapter` — uses an `_OrderSpyAdapter` subclass that records every `place_market_order` call. Pushes a current candle into the sim via `set_current_candle`, calls `adapter.place_market_order("BTC-USDC", "buy", 0.1)`, asserts the result is `success=True` (sim filled it on the virtual portfolio), then asserts `spy.order_calls == []` (the delegate was never reached). Then directly invokes the delegate's `place_market_order` and asserts it raises `RuntimeError("no signing key")` — proving that even the path the sim DOESN'T take would fail loudly thanks to scrubbing. (6) `test_6_live_mode_returns_real_adapter_unchanged` — `get_adapter("hyperliquid")` and `get_adapter("hyperliquid", mode="live")` both return the unmodified `_CredentialedAdapter` with all credentials INTACT (`privateKey`, `secret`, `_private_key`, `walletAddress` all preserved), AND the two calls return the same cached instance. (7) `test_invalid_mode_raises` — `mode="paper"` raises `ValueError("Unknown adapter mode...")` rather than silently treating it as live. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The spec said "set the adapter's private key / secret attribute to None (check the HyperliquidAdapter to find the exact attribute name — likely `self._private_key` or similar)". Inspection shows `HyperliquidAdapter` does NOT actually have a `self._private_key` attribute — it passes the key directly into the `ccxt.hyperliquid({"privateKey": ...})` config dict, and ccxt stores it as `self._exchange.privateKey`. The scrubber walks BOTH layers (inner ccxt + wrapper-level) so the spec's literal expectation is honoured AND the actual attribute is cleared. (2) `apiKey` is intentionally NOT in the scrub list. The spec didn't mention it, but I wanted to call this out: signing on every ccxt-supported venue requires the paired `secret`, which IS scrubbed; nuking `apiKey` would break read-only authenticated calls (`fetch_user_fees`, account metadata) on venues that use it for read identification. The wallet-address preservation rationale extends to apiKey for the same reason. (3) `_scrub_signing_keys` catches `setattr` failures rather than raising — some ccxt classes may use `__slots__` or read-only properties on certain attributes. The sim's order layer is the primary defense (every order method on `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` stays on the virtual portfolio); scrubbing is hardening that protects against future code paths leaking through. Logging at DEBUG so test runs don't get noisy. (4) The `mode="shadow"` cache key is just `name` (same as before) — there's no `(name, mode)` composite key. This means asking for `get_adapter("hyperliquid", mode="shadow")` twice returns the same cached sim, which is the desired behaviour for per-bot consistency within one BotRunner. The separate `_instances` / `_shadow_instances` dicts already provide the mode isolation — a composite key would be redundant. (5) The `initial_balance` kwarg is `kwargs.pop("initial_balance", None)` rather than `kwargs.get(...)`. Without the `pop`, `kwargs` would still contain `initial_balance` when passed to the live adapter's ctor and ccxt would reject it as an unknown parameter. The pop is required for the path where `mode="shadow"` is called with `initial_balance=N` and the registry has a real entry. (6) Test `test_end_to_end_configure_then_factory_returns_sim` was kept (and rewritten) instead of deleted because it documents an important invariant during the Task 3 → Task 4 transition: even when the legacy `configure_shadow` is still being called (as it is in `quantagent/main.py` until Task 4 lands), the factory now ignores it. Task 4 will delete this test along with `configure_shadow`. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1651 passed in 14.84s** (1644 → 1651, +7), zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.20.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.21.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new `mode` parameter on `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter` + new `_scrub_signing_keys` helper). 1651 tests passing.
- **Sprint Shadow-Redesign Task 2: Repository-level shadow/live data isolation** — Builds on Task 1's schema by enforcing the shadow filter at the repository layer so production code paths cannot accidentally surface shadow rows. The pattern is "live-only by default, opt-in to see shadow data" — adding `include_shadow=True` is now the only way to read shadow trades, cycles, or bots out of the shared DB. **`storage/repositories/base.py` (ABC contract)**: every list-returning read method on `TradeRepository`, `CycleRepository`, and `BotRepository` gains a keyword-only `include_shadow: bool = False` parameter. Specifically: `TradeRepository.get_open_positions(user_id, bot_id, *, include_shadow=False)`, `TradeRepository.get_trades_by_bot(bot_id, limit=50, *, include_shadow=False)`, `CycleRepository.get_recent_cycles(bot_id, limit=5, *, include_shadow=False)`, and `BotRepository.get_active_bots(*, include_shadow=False)`. The `*,` separator makes them strictly keyword-only so existing positional callers can never accidentally pass `True` as the third positional argument. `TradeRepository.get_trade(trade_id)` is intentionally NOT filtered — it's a single-row primary-key lookup where the caller already knows the row's identity, and filtering would silently turn legitimate fetches into `None` returns. New abstract method `BotRepository.get_active_bots_by_mode(mode: str) -> list[dict]` returns active bots whose `mode` column equals the argument exactly — this is the path the shadow-redesigned main.py will use so a single BotRunner can be booted in either mode without inverse filtering. Module-level docstrings on `TradeRepository` and `CycleRepository` codify the contract: writes accept `is_shadow` in the input dict and persist it; `is_shadow` is NEVER inferred from the bot record at the repo layer because that would couple Trade/Cycle repositories to BotRepository and force a second query on every write — the caller (the executor / pipeline / Task 4 wiring) is responsible for passing the bot's mode through. **`storage/repositories/postgres.py`**: read methods append `AND is_shadow = FALSE` when `include_shadow=False`, with no parameter substitution since the literal is constant. `save_trade` and `save_cycle` extend the INSERT to include the new column, reading `bool(trade.get("is_shadow", False))` / `bool(cycle.get("is_shadow", False))` from the input dict. `save_bot` derives `is_shadow=True` from EITHER `bot["is_shadow"]` OR `bot["mode"] == "shadow"` so callers can pass either flag — the OR is important because the default `mode` is `"live"` and most production callers will only set `mode`, not the redundant `is_shadow` boolean. `get_active_bots` gets the new kwarg; `get_active_bots_by_mode(mode)` is new. The DDL fallback (`_CREATE_TRADES`, `_CREATE_CYCLES`, `_CREATE_BOTS`) is also extended to include the new shadow columns — this is what `init_db()` runs in dev/test environments where Alembic isn't invoked. The two paths are NOT redundant: Alembic 003 is the production source of truth, the DDL fallback is the local-dev / unit-test backstop, and they have to stay in sync. **`storage/repositories/sqlite.py`**: same pattern as postgres but with SQLite's `is_shadow = 0` integer literal instead of `FALSE`. `save_bot` derives the integer 0/1 from the same `mode == "shadow"` heuristic. `get_active_bots_by_mode` is new. The DDL was already updated in Task 1, so only the read methods + the new method needed touching here. **Backwards compatibility audit**: grep'd every caller of these methods across the codebase. Eight call sites total: `quantagent/main.py:253` (`get_active_bots()` no kwarg → still defaults to live-only, exactly the production behaviour), `api/routes/positions.py:36` (`get_open_positions(user_id, bot_id)`), `api/routes/bots.py:145, 207` (`get_recent_cycles(bot_id, limit=1)`), `api/routes/trades.py:57, 63` (`get_trades_by_bot(bot_id, limit=...)`), `engine/memory/cycle_memory.py:28` (`get_recent_cycles(bot_id, limit)`), `mcp/quant_scientist/agent.py:252` and `backtesting/evals/auto_miner.py:109` (`get_trades_by_bot(bot_id, limit=...)`), and `tests/integration/test_pipeline.py:432`. ALL of them call positionally with at most `(bot_id, limit=...)` and none pass a third positional — every single one continues to work unchanged and now silently filters shadow rows out, which is the desired Task 2 outcome. The 4 in-test mock repositories (`MockBotRepository` / `MockTradeRepository` / `MockCycleRepository` in `tests/api/test_endpoints.py`, `tests/unit/test_runner.py`, `tests/test_backtesting/test_evals/test_auto_miner_wiring.py`, `tests/test_mcp/test_quant_scientist/test_runner.py` and `test_agent.py`) are STRUCTURAL (no ABC inheritance) so they don't break when the ABC adds new abstract methods, and their call sites only ever pass the legacy positional args. Verified by running the full suite. **7 new tests** in `tests/unit/test_repositories.py::TestShadowFiltering` (matches the user's stated minimum of 6, with one additional cycle test for symmetry). Each test uses the SQLite-backed `repos` fixture for speed (no Postgres dependency): (1) `test_get_active_bots_excludes_shadow_by_default` — saves one `mode='live'` and one `mode='shadow'` bot, asserts `get_active_bots()` returns ONLY the live one. (2) `test_get_active_bots_includes_shadow_when_asked` — same setup, asserts `get_active_bots(include_shadow=True)` returns BOTH. (3) `test_get_active_bots_by_mode_returns_only_matching_mode` — saves 2 live + 2 shadow bots, calls `get_active_bots_by_mode("shadow")` and asserts it returns exactly the 2 shadow ones, then calls it with `"live"` and asserts the inverse — proves the filter is exact, not substring/prefix. (4) `test_save_trade_persists_is_shadow_flag` — round-trip: saves one trade with `is_shadow=True`, one without, asserts the column reads back as 1/0 respectively. (5) `test_get_trades_by_bot_excludes_shadow_by_default` — saves a single shadow trade for `bot_id="shadow-bot"`, asserts `get_trades_by_bot("shadow-bot")` returns `[]` (the strongest possible isolation guarantee: even with the bot ID known, you cannot leak shadow data without opting in). Same check for `get_open_positions`. (6) `test_get_trades_by_bot_includes_shadow_when_asked` — saves one live trade and one shadow trade for the same bot, asserts default returns only the live one and `include_shadow=True` returns both. Mirror check for `get_open_positions`. (7) `test_get_recent_cycles_excludes_shadow_by_default` — same shape for the cycle repository, proves the contract is symmetric across all three filtered repos. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) `get_open_positions` and `get_trades_by_bot` use a constant `" AND is_shadow = FALSE"` literal in the SQL string when filtering, NOT a parameterised `$N` placeholder. Safe because the value is a Python boolean literal not user input — there's no injection surface — and avoids burning a parameter slot just for a constant. The same pattern is already used by other parts of the postgres repo (`status = 'open'` in `get_open_positions`). (2) The `*,` keyword-only marker means callers MUST use `include_shadow=True` syntax, not positional `True`. This is intentional defensive coding — it prevents the easy bug where someone refactors a positional call and passes `True` to the wrong slot. (3) `get_trade(trade_id)` is NOT filtered. Single-row primary-key lookups are used by `update_trade` workflows, position-sync correction passes, and trade-history detail views — all of which already know the row exists and want it back. Filtering would silently break these flows. (4) The repository changes do NOT yet wire the `is_shadow` flag through the executor / pipeline call sites — that's Task 4's responsibility. Task 2 only ensures the filter EXISTS and is the default; Task 4 will make sure shadow bots' executor calls pass `is_shadow=True` to `save_trade`. Until Task 4 lands, shadow bots will still write `is_shadow=False` from the executor (because no caller passes the flag), which means the new filter is functionally a no-op end-to-end. This is OK for Task 2 because the column-write path is unit-tested directly via the new tests; Task 4 just connects the wires. (5) The PostgreSQL `_CREATE_TRADES` / `_CREATE_CYCLES` / `_CREATE_BOTS` DDL fallback was updated even though Task 1 only updated the SQLite DDL, because `PostgresRepositories.init_db()` runs the same `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` strings on a fresh dev/test PostgreSQL DB and would otherwise omit the new columns. The fallback is intentionally not a substitute for Alembic in production — it's a local-dev convenience. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1644 passed in 14.66s** (1637 → 1644, +7), zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.19.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.20.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new repository contract surface and new abstract method on `BotRepository`). 1644 tests passing.
- **Sprint Shadow-Redesign Task 1: Alembic 003 — `is_shadow` / `mode` columns + `live_*` views + bot migration script** — Lays the schema foundation for collapsing the separate `quantagent_shadow` PostgreSQL database into the shared `quantagent` DB with per-row mode tagging. **Migration `alembic/versions/003_shadow_mode_columns.py`**: adds `is_shadow BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false` to `bots`, `trades`, and `cycles`; adds `mode VARCHAR(10) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'live'` to `bots` (valid values: `live`, `shadow`); creates two PostgreSQL views — `live_trades AS SELECT * FROM trades WHERE is_shadow = false` and `live_cycles AS SELECT * FROM cycles WHERE is_shadow = false` — as ergonomic shadow-free reads for analytics and dashboards. Existing rows backfill to `is_shadow=false / mode='live'` via column server defaults so the upgrade is non-blocking. Symmetric `downgrade()` drops the views first, then the columns in reverse order. Revision chain: 002 → 003. **`scripts/migrate_shadow_bots.py`**: standalone async one-shot copy script for the cutover. Reads `DATABASE_URL` (prod) and `SHADOW_DATABASE_URL` (legacy shadow DB; defaults to the prod URL with `/quantagent` rewritten to `/quantagent_shadow` so the operator usually only needs `DATABASE_URL` set). Walks every row of `quantagent_shadow.bots`, inserts into `quantagent.bots` with `is_shadow=true, mode='shadow'`, **preserves bot IDs** so existing trades / cycles / Sentinel escalation state stay joinable across the migration, skips duplicates by primary key (re-run safe), JSON-serialises `config_json`/`last_health` if asyncpg returns them as dicts rather than text, normalises `postgresql+asyncpg://` and `postgres://` DSN prefixes back to plain `postgresql://` for `asyncpg.connect`, prints `inserted/skipped/failed` summary, exits 1 if any insert fails. To be run once on the server after `alembic upgrade head` lands revision 003, then the legacy DB can be dropped with `dropdb quantagent_shadow`. **`storage/repositories/sqlite.py`**: SQLite DDL parity — `bots` table gains `is_shadow INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` and `mode TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'live'`; `trades` and `cycles` gain `is_shadow INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`. All three INSERT statements (`save_bot`, `save_trade`, `save_cycle`) now persist the new columns: `save_bot` derives `is_shadow` from either `bot["is_shadow"]` OR `bot["mode"] == "shadow"` so callers can pass either flag; `save_trade` and `save_cycle` accept an `is_shadow` key in their dict and coerce to 0/1. PostgreSQL repo writes are unchanged in this task — Task 2 will wire `is_shadow` through the read/write paths and add `get_active_bots(include_shadow=...)` plus `get_active_bots_by_mode(mode)`. **Tests** (`tests/integration/test_migrations.py`): updated `test_bots_table_columns` / `test_trades_table_columns` / `test_cycles_table_columns` expected sets to include the new columns. **Added `test_shadow_mode_migration_exists`** — asserts the 003 migration file exists, revision is `"003"` with `down_revision="002"`, schema additions cover all three tables and both new columns, both views are created via `CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW`, and `downgrade()` symmetrically drops the views and columns. **Added `test_shadow_columns_persist_on_fresh_db`** — initialises a fresh SQLite DB via `repos.init_db()`, saves a bot with `mode="shadow"` and a bot with no mode (defaults to live), asserts both `is_shadow` and `mode` round-trip correctly via direct table query, then saves a trade and cycle with `is_shadow=True` and asserts both flags persist. Test count: 1635 → 1637 (+2). All 1637 tests pass. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The acceptance criteria mentioned "use raw SQL INSERT...SELECT across databases" as one option for the cross-DB copy. asyncpg cannot do cross-database SQL within a single connection, so the script uses two separate connections (read from shadow, write to prod) and a Python loop. This is the more portable path and matches the explicit fallback mentioned in the same criterion ("create a one-time `scripts/migrate_shadow_bots.py`"). (2) The migration uses `op.add_column` with a `server_default` rather than a separate `op.execute("UPDATE ... SET is_shadow=false")` data-migration step because the server default handles the backfill atomically as part of the column add — no separate UPDATE needed. (3) Repository read filtering and the `mode` parameter on `get_active_bots` are scoped to Task 2, not this task. The columns exist in the schema but no read path filters on them yet — existing queries continue to return all rows including (eventually) shadow rows, which is intentional because Task 1 only lays the schema groundwork. (4) PostgreSQL repository writes (`PostgresBotRepository.save_bot`, etc.) were NOT updated in this task because (a) the server defaults handle existing call sites without crashing, (b) `migrate_shadow_bots.py` writes via raw asyncpg SQL with the new columns explicitly, and (c) Task 2's repository changes will rewire all the postgres writes uniformly. Touching them here would create merge conflict surface for Task 2. (5) No Alembic test that *actually applies* the migration to a real DB — `test_migrations.py` historically tests structure (file exists, revision chain, table columns via SQLite parity) rather than running `alembic upgrade head`, because the latter requires a real PostgreSQL instance and would tie pytest to local DB state. The new test exercises the equivalent code path via SQLite DDL + INSERT round-trip, which is the same pattern used by the existing `test_bots_table_columns` etc. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1637 passed in 15.04s** (1635 → 1637, +2), zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.18.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.19.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new schema migration + new operational script). 1637 tests passing.
- **Diagnostic-only: shadow-mode Sentinel hang investigation + `scripts/debug_shadow.py`** — User reported `python -m quantagent.main run --shadow` shows uvicorn starting but: (1) `"Initializing infrastructure..."` log line never appears, (2) no Sentinel scanning activity, (3) all API routes return 404, (4) 0 trades in shadow DB, (5) `RuntimeWarning: coroutine 'run_async_migrations' was never awaited` in stderr. **No code fixes applied** — user explicitly asked for investigation only. **Five root causes / observations identified, in order of severity**: (1) **`backtesting/shadow.py::_run_alembic_upgrade` is fundamentally broken when called from inside an event loop**. It's a SYNC function called from `await ensure_shadow_db(...)` (an async function). It calls `command.upgrade(cfg, "head")` which loads `alembic/env.py`. That file's module-level code at line 93 calls `run_migrations_online()` → `asyncio.run(run_async_migrations())`. From inside a running event loop, `asyncio.run()` raises `RuntimeError("asyncio.run() cannot be called from a running event loop")` AND leaks the coroutine object — the coroutine was created by calling `run_async_migrations()` but never awaited because `asyncio.run` aborted before reaching the await. That's the EXACT `RuntimeWarning` the user observed. The RuntimeError IS caught by `ensure_shadow_db`'s `try/except Exception` block (line 296 → `logger.exception(...)`), so the function returns normally — but **the shadow DB schema is never migrated by Alembic**. Tables only exist via the `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` raw-DDL fallback in `PostgresRepositories.init_db()`, which silently masks the alembic failure. (2) **`get_repositories()` does NOT hang silently** — `asyncpg.create_pool` has a default 60s connect timeout per attempt, and the `init_db()` raw DDL fallback runs `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` for every table in `_ALL_TABLES`. NOT a primary suspect. (3) **`api/app.py::create_app` is NOT a bare FastAPI()** — it registers FIVE routers (`bots`, `trades`, `health`, `positions`, `rules`), all prefixed with `/v1/...`. **The "API routes return 404" symptom is most likely a path-prefix mismatch** — caller hitting `/bots` instead of `/v1/bots`. There is no catch-all root, no `/` redirect. (4) **`BotRunner.start_with_bots` code path is intact** — iterates `_register_bot` per bot, dedupes sentinels per unique symbol, calls `sentinel.subscribe_results()`, creates `asyncio.create_task(_run_sentinel_safe(...))`. **Critical observation**: the `adapter_factory` closure in `quantagent/main.py:218` runs `import exchanges.hyperliquid` LAZILY on first call. If `start_with_bots` is called with 9 active bots BEFORE the very first `adapter_factory(...)` invocation, the import side-effect runs inside the runner's loop — and any import-time failure (ccxt missing, syntax error, etc.) would propagate out of `_register_bot` and break the whole loop. **Most plausible primary cause of "0 sentinels"**: the user's 9 active bots live in the LIVE DB, not the shadow DB. `configure_shadow()` swapped `DATABASE_URL` to `..._shadow`, the shadow DB was just created (or already existed empty), `repos.bots.get_active_bots()` returned 0 rows, and the runner started with 0 sentinels → 0 scanning → 0 trades. (5) **`_setup_logging()` calls `logging.basicConfig` WITHOUT `force=True`** — if anything imported before `run()` touches root handlers (uvicorn import, anthropic SDK, ccxt, etc.) the basicConfig is silently a no-op. uvicorn's later `Config(...)` call at main.py:276 invokes `configure_logging()` which uses uvicorn's default `LOGGING_CONFIG` dict; with `disable_existing_loggers=False` it shouldn't clobber app loggers but DOES install its own handlers on root. **Plausible explanation for the "Initializing infrastructure..." log line never appearing**: either `basicConfig` was a no-op (root already had handlers) or uvicorn's later `dictConfig` reset handler list and lost any in-flight buffered output. **`scripts/debug_shadow.py` written** as the deliverable — 7 numbered diagnostic banners (`configure_shadow + is_shadow_mode`, `ensure_shadow_db`, `get_repositories`, `repos.bots.get_active_bots`, `BotRunner.start_with_bots` with stub factories, sleep 5s + re-check sentinel state, graceful shutdown), each wrapped in its own `try/except` + wall-clock timing + `asyncio.wait_for` timeout (60s / 30s / 15s / 30s) so a hang on one step doesn't mask the next. Output is plain `print()` statements (NOT `logging`) so the diagnostic bypasses any basicConfig collisions. The script does NOT modify any files and does NOT spawn the FastAPI server — `start_with_bots` is exercised with stub adapter + stub bot factories so the diagnostic only measures whether sentinels get constructed, not whether they can fetch real OHLCV. **Spec deviations**: (1) NO fix applied per user instruction — `quantagent/main.py`, `backtesting/shadow.py`, `alembic/env.py`, `quantagent/runner.py`, `api/app.py`, and `storage/repositories/*` are ALL untouched. (2) NO version bump — diagnostic only, no functional change. (3) NO tests added — the debug script is one-shot operational tooling, lives in `scripts/`, not `tests/`. Coupling it to the test suite would tie pytest to local Postgres state. (4) The findings list FIVE distinct root causes because the user's symptom report combined multiple unrelated issues — the report disentangles them so each can be fixed independently. **Recommended fix order** (for a follow-up task, NOT this one): (a) make `_run_alembic_upgrade` async-safe (`asyncio.to_thread(command.upgrade, ...)` or subprocess), (b) add `force=True` to `logging.basicConfig`, (c) seed shadow DB with the live `bots` table on first creation so `get_active_bots()` returns the same set, (d) document the `/v1/...` route prefix in the main README so 404s stop. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1635 passed in 14.42s** (no test changes), zero regressions. 1635 tests passing.
- **Real bot_factory wiring in `quantagent/main.py` (closes the BotManager → TraderBot gap)** — Before this change, `quantagent/main.py` constructed `BotManager` with a `bot_factory` stub that just `raise NotImplementedError(...)` and pointed users at `scripts/run_trade.py`. The result: Sentinel could fire `SetupDetected` events forever, BotManager would receive them, dispatch to `_run_bot` → `spawn_bot` → `self._bot_factory(symbol, bot_id)`, and immediately crash. The Task 11 escalation feedback loop, the active-bot DB restore, and the shadow-mode data delegate were all wired and tested in the previous tasks, but the actual production code path from "Sentinel detects setup" to "TraderBot runs analysis cycle" was broken end-to-end at the very last step. **`quantagent/main.py::_make_bot_factory`**: new module-level helper that returns a closure satisfying `Callable[[str, str], TraderBot]`. The closure captures `repos`, `llm_provider`, `adapter_factory`, `event_bus`, and `feature_flags` by reference so they're constructed ONCE at startup and reused across every spawned bot. PER bot it builds: `TradingConfig(symbol, timeframe)`, `OHLCVFetcher(adapter, config)`, `FlowAgent([CryptoFlowProvider()])`, a `SignalRegistry` populated by polling each of the four signal-agent feature flags (`indicator_agent`, `pattern_agent`, `trend_agent`, `flow_signal_agent`), `ConvictionAgent(llm)`, `DecisionAgent(llm, config)`, `Executor(adapter, bus, config)`, `PositionManager(adapter, bus)`, the four memory wrappers (`CycleMemory`, `ReflectionRules`, `CrossBotSignals`, `RegimeHistory`), and the full `AnalysisPipeline` constructed from all of the above with `bot_id`/`user_id` plumbed through. The pipeline + executor + position_manager are wrapped in a `TraderBot` and returned. Mirrors the wiring used by `scripts/run_trade.py` byte-for-byte so that single-cycle dev runs and the production BotRunner exercise the same dependency graph — only the lifecycle differs (run-once script vs. dynamic spawn-on-demand). **`_run_server` rewiring**: the LLM provider is now constructed ONCE at the top of `_run_server` (`ClaudeProvider(api_key=ANTHROPIC_API_KEY)`); if the env var is missing, a WARNING is logged and `llm_provider` stays `None` so the existing repo-only paths (e.g. `repos.bots.get_active_bots()` for state restoration) still work and the failure surfaces only when something actually tries to spawn a bot. The `adapter_factory` closure was hoisted ABOVE `bot_factory` (it was defined later in the original layout) and now also runs the side-effect import of `exchanges.hyperliquid` so the `ExchangeFactory` registry is populated before the first `get_adapter("hyperliquid")` call in shadow mode (otherwise the new shadow data-delegate wiring from the previous task would silently fall through to `data_adapter=None` because the registry would be empty at that moment). The `BotRunner` ctor now receives the actual `llm_provider` instead of `None`. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The factory closure currently uses sane defaults (`timeframe="1h"`, `exchange="hyperliquid"`, `user_id="system"`) when called from `BotManager.spawn_bot` because the spawn signature is `factory(symbol, bot_id)` — there's no per-bot dict at the spawn site. The bot dict IS available in `BotRunner._bot_configs[bot_id]`, but the BotManager → factory call doesn't carry it through. A follow-up could thread the dict via `BotManager.spawn_bot(symbol, bot_id, bot_config=...)`, but that's a wider refactor (changes `BotManager`'s public surface, the SetupDetected dispatch path, and the factory contract). For now the defaults match the most common production case (BTC-USDC + 1h + hyperliquid + system user) and any deviations get fixed up by the analysis pipeline's own per-cycle context. (2) `feature_flags = FeatureFlags()` is loaded ONCE in `_run_server` and passed into `_make_bot_factory`. Hot-reloading flags requires a restart — same as before, this isn't a regression. (3) The `_make_bot_factory` helper does its imports lazily inside the function body so importing `quantagent.main` doesn't pull the entire engine module graph at CLI parse time (matters for `python -m quantagent --help` startup latency). The closure body's imports are also kept local to dodge a circular-import risk between `engine.pipeline` and `engine.bot_manager` if the latter ever imports `quantagent.main` for type hints. (4) The `bot_dict` lookup inside the closure is a placeholder `try/except: pass` that always falls through to defaults — wired this way intentionally because `factory(symbol, bot_id)` is a sync entrypoint and we'd need to await `repos.bots.get_bot(bot_id)` to actually fetch the dict. The cleaner fix is to thread `bot_dict` through `BotManager.spawn_bot`, which is the wider refactor flagged in (1). The `try/except` block is left in place as a hook for that future change so the spec deviation is visible in code, not just the changelog. (5) The factory does NOT subscribe the bot to any event topics — `Executor` already publishes `TradeOpened` / `TradeClosed`, `AnalysisPipeline` already publishes the data/signal/conviction/cycle events, and `BotManager` already publishes `SetupResult` after the spawn completes. No additional plumbing needed. (6) The factory does NOT register an LLM cache — `ClaudeProvider` constructs its own internal cache on first use, and per CLAUDE.md "Never cache LLM responses" the cache is for prompt-cache hits (system prompt reuse), not response memoization. **4 new tests** in `tests/unit/test_main_bot_factory.py`: `test_factory_returns_traderbot_for_symbol` (factory("BTC-USDC", "test-bot-001") returns a `TraderBot` instance with the right `bot_id`, and `adapter_factory` was called once with `"hyperliquid"`), `test_factory_pipeline_carries_symbol_and_bot_id` (the `TraderBot._pipeline._config.symbol` and `_pipeline._bot_id` match the call args — proves the data moat keys flow through correctly), `test_factory_registers_only_enabled_signal_agents` (writes a tmp `features.yaml` with `pattern_agent: false, trend_agent: false`, asserts the registry only contains `indicator_agent` + `flow_signal_agent` — feature-flag gating is honoured), `test_factory_calls_adapter_factory_per_invocation` (two `factory()` calls → two `adapter_factory` calls, proves shadow-mode swap is respected even on re-spawns). New `_StubLLM` test helper at module scope satisfies the `LLMProvider` ABC with no-op `generate_text` / `generate_vision` returning empty `LLMResponse` — needed because the factory only stores the LLM ref but the `ConvictionAgent`/`DecisionAgent`/`IndicatorAgent` ctors all type-check it. The test never actually runs `bot.run()` so no LLM call ever fires. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1635 passed in 14.47s** (1631 → 1635, +4), zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.17.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.18.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — closes a critical NotImplementedError gap in production wiring). 1635 tests passing.
- **Shadow mode: live data via real-adapter delegate, virtual fills (`SimulatedExchangeAdapter.data_adapter`)** — Before this change, shadow mode crashed because `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` had no data source: the factory built it with only `initial_balance`, and `fetch_ohlcv` would either raise `RuntimeError("no data loader")` or — worse — return whatever stale candles had been pushed via `set_current_candle` (which is a backtest-only control surface that never gets called in live shadow mode). The whole point of shadow mode is that Sentinel + signal agents see REAL market data so the engine's behaviour is identical to live trading; only the order side should be virtualised. **`backtesting/sim_exchange.py`**: new optional `data_adapter: ExchangeAdapter | None` constructor parameter. When set, it takes priority over `data_loader` (which is preserved for offline backtests) and services every read-only ABC method by delegation: `fetch_ohlcv`, `get_ticker`, `fetch_orderbook`, `get_funding_rate`, `get_open_interest`, `fetch_meta`, `fetch_user_fees`. **NOT delegated** (intentionally): `get_balance`, `get_positions`, and ALL order methods (`place_market_order`, `place_limit_order`, `place_sl_order`, `place_tp_order`, `cancel_order`, `cancel_all_orders`, `close_position`, `modify_sl`, `modify_tp`) — these stay 100% on the virtual portfolio because virtualising fills is the entire point of shadow mode. The error message in the no-data-source path now mentions both `data_loader=` and `data_adapter=` so operators can pick the right knob. **`exchanges/factory.py::_get_shadow_adapter`**: when the requested exchange is in the registry, the factory now constructs the real adapter via `cls._registry[name](**kwargs)` and passes it as `data_adapter=` to the new sim. If the live adapter ctor blows up (typically a missing-credentials error in dev), the factory logs the exception via `logger.exception` and falls through to a sim with `data_adapter=None`.
