That second path is intentional: a data-less sim still satisfies the ABC, and the operator will see the explicit `RuntimeError("no data source")` on the FIRST `fetch_ohlcv` call rather than at process boot, which is the right failure mode (loud, traceable, and lets test fixtures construct a sim without registering live adapters first). The unknown-exchange path (no registry entry at all) keeps its existing behaviour for the same reason. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The user's spec said "construct sim_adapter in `backtesting/shadow.py` or `quantagent/main.py`", but the cleanest swap point is `_get_shadow_adapter` in `exchanges/factory.py` — it's already the central place where every shadow adapter request gets routed, and putting the wiring there means the existing 8 factory tests automatically cover the new code path. main.py and shadow.py never have to know about the data-delegate pattern. (2) Spec said "Register `sim_adapter` as the exchange adapter (so orders go to sim)" — this is already the existing behaviour: every consumer in the codebase calls `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter(name)`, and the factory returns the sim in shadow mode regardless of what name was asked for. No registration step needed. (3) The factory passes `**kwargs` to the live-adapter ctor in shadow mode, which means if a caller passes `initial_balance=...` to `get_adapter`, it propagates through to the real adapter ctor. Hyperliquid's ctor signature has no positional kwargs that conflict with `initial_balance`, but a future adapter might. Kept the simple forward because the alternative (filtering kwargs) is brittle. (4) `data_adapter` takes strict priority over `data_loader` when BOTH are provided — there's no merge / fallback. This matches the user's spec literally and avoids ambiguity in shadow mode where `data_loader` shouldn't be in the picture at all. **7 new tests** across 2 files. **`tests/test_backtesting/test_sim_exchange.py`** (5 new): `test_data_adapter_delegates_fetch_ohlcv_without_data_loader` (delegate path returns the canned OHLCV with no `RuntimeError`), `test_data_adapter_takes_priority_over_data_loader` (when both are set, the loader's `load_as_market_data` raises if called — proves it isn't), `test_no_data_source_raises_with_helpful_message` (regex match on the new error mentioning both knobs), `test_data_adapter_delegates_read_only_methods` (asserts the call ORDER on the fake delegate for ticker / orderbook / funding / OI / meta / fees), `test_orders_use_virtual_portfolio_not_data_adapter` (places a market buy → position is virtualised, balance reads 10_000 from the ledger, and the fake delegate has ZERO order-side calls in its recorded list). The new `_FakeDataAdapter` test helper at module scope records every read-only call as a `(method_name, *args)` tuple and serves canned values with sentinel field markers (`tier=2`, `funding=0.0001`, `oi=12345.0`) so test assertions can pin both *which* method was called *and* that the response came from the delegate. **`tests/test_backtesting/test_shadow.py`** (3 new): `test_factory_shadow_unknown_exchange_still_works` extended with assertion that `_data_adapter is None` (so the failure mode is the explicit `RuntimeError`, not silent fallback to `set_current_candle` state). `test_factory_shadow_wires_real_adapter_as_data_delegate` (registers `_LiveAdapter`, enables shadow mode, asserts the returned sim's `_data_adapter` is an `_LiveAdapter` instance). `test_factory_shadow_data_delegate_construct_failure_is_nonfatal` (registers a `_BoomAdapter` whose `__init__` raises, asserts the factory still returns a sim with `_data_adapter=None` and that the failure is logged at ERROR level). **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1631 passed in 14.16s** (1624 → 1631, +7), zero regressions. The 65 existing sim_exchange tests all pass unchanged because `data_adapter=None` is the default and every existing call site continues to use the legacy `data_loader` / `set_current_candle` path. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.16.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.17.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new constructor param + new factory wiring). 1631 tests passing.
- **BotRunner restores active bots from DB on startup (`get_active_bots()`)** — Before this change, `quantagent/main.py` started the runner with zero bots and required users to re-register every bot via the API after each restart. The runner had a `start_with_bots(bots)` method ready to receive a pre-loaded list, but main.py was calling the bare `start()` because the only available repo accessor was `get_bots_by_user(user_id)` and main.py has no user context at startup. **Repo additions**: new abstract `BotRepository.get_active_bots() -> list[dict]` in `storage/repositories/base.py` (returns all bots with `status='active'` across users — no user_id filter, this is a startup/admin path not a request path). Concrete implementations in `PostgresBotRepository` (parameterized `WHERE status = $1`) and `SQLiteBotRepository` (parameterized `WHERE status = ?`), both reusing the same `config_json` / `last_health` JSON-decode pattern as `get_bots_by_user`. **main.py wiring**: replaced the old `await runner.start()` (with the stale "we start with no bots" comment) with `active_bots = await repos.bots.get_active_bots()` followed by `logger.info(f"Loaded {len(active_bots)} active bots from database")` and `await runner.start_with_bots(active_bots)`. The order matters: the load is awaited before start so the count log line runs even if the list is empty, and so `start_with_bots` sees the full set in one call rather than streaming. **Test mocks unchanged**: the in-test `MockBotRepository` classes in `tests/api/test_endpoints.py`, `tests/unit/test_runner.py`, `tests/test_backtesting/test_evals/test_auto_miner_wiring.py`, and `backtesting/evals/auto_miner.py`'s ad-hoc duck-typed mock all sidestep the `BotRepository` ABC by not inheriting from it (they're structural mocks, not subclasses), so adding a new abstractmethod to the base class does NOT break their instantiation. Verified by running the full suite — 1624 → 1624 passing, zero changes. The new code path is exercised at the integration level by the existing repository tests that hit real PostgreSQL/SQLite via `repos.bots.save_bot(...)` then `repos.bots.get_bots_by_user(...)`; the new method follows the exact same pattern. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1624 passed in 14.31s**, zero regressions. Engine version bumped 2026.04.2.15.0-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.16.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new repo method + new startup behaviour). 1624 tests passing.
- **Activate Task 11 escalation feedback in production (`subscribe_results` wiring)** — Task 11 shipped the SentinelMonitor escalation state machine + the `SetupResult` event + tests, but deliberately did NOT auto-call `subscribe_results()` in the constructor. That left the feedback loop dormant in production: the escalation logic existed and was fully tested in isolation, but the live `BotRunner` was constructing sentinels without subscribing them, so every spawned bot's SKIP outcome was invisible to the Sentinel and the threshold never ratcheted up. **Wiring change**: in `quantagent/runner.py::BotRunner._register_bot`, immediately after constructing the `SentinelMonitor` and before kicking off the `_run_sentinel_safe` task, call `sentinel.subscribe_results()` so the new sentinel registers its `_on_setup_result` handler on the bot runner's shared event bus. The call happens BEFORE the sentinel's run loop starts so the handler is in place by the time the first downstream `SetupDetected → BotManager → SetupResult` chain can fire. The order is intentional: subscribe → store in dict → spawn task. **Production sites checked but NOT modified**: `scripts/run_cycle.py`, `scripts/run_trade.py`, `backtesting/engine.py`. None of those construct a `SentinelMonitor` instance. `run_cycle.py` runs ONE analysis cycle through `AnalysisPipeline` directly with no Sentinel loop; `run_trade.py` imports `sentinel.position_manager.PositionManager` (a different class — manages SL/TP for open positions, not the readiness scoring loop) but never instantiates `SentinelMonitor`; `backtesting/engine.py` imports `sentinel.conditions.ReadinessScorer` (the standalone scoring function called directly by the mechanical-mode backtest) but doesn't run a Sentinel-as-event-loop. The user's task spec asked me to wire all four; the audit (one grep across all four files for `SentinelMonitor(`) showed only `quantagent/runner.py:227` actually constructs one. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The user's spec wrote `sentinel.subscribe_results(bus)` with a `bus` argument. The Task 11 implementation built `subscribe_results()` to take ZERO arguments because the bus is held internally as `self._bus` (set at construction time). Calling it with the no-arg form here matches the implementation; flagged before writing the edit. (2) Only 1 of the 4 files in the user's spec actually needed touching. The audit results are documented in the post-task summary so the user can verify the conclusion. **3 new tests** in `tests/unit/test_runner.py::TestSentinelEscalationWiring`: `test_add_bot_activates_escalation_feedback` (black-box: add a bot, publish a SKIP SetupResult on the runner's bus, verify the bot's sentinel's `current_threshold()` ratchets up — the test only passes if `subscribe_results()` ran during `_register_bot`), `test_setup_result_for_other_symbol_does_not_escalate` (per-symbol filter still works through bus dispatch — BTC SKIP doesn't escalate ETH's sentinel even though both share the same bus and both are subscribed), `test_trade_outcome_resets_after_escalation` (end-to-end SKIP→escalate→TRADE→reset chain via the runner's bus). All three use the existing `runner` + `event_bus` fixtures so they exercise the production wiring path with no monkeypatching. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1624 passed in 14.37s** (1621 → 1624, +3), zero regressions. The 60+ existing Sentinel tests + 24 BotManager tests + 38 prior Task 11 tests all still pass unchanged. 1624 tests passing.

### 2026-04-08
- **Sentinel escalating readiness threshold + SetupResult feedback loop (Task 11)** — Implements the post-SKIP threshold ratchet from the user's spec, tying it back to BotManager via a new `SetupResult` event so the Sentinel finally gets feedback about what the analysis pipeline did with its triggers. Without this loop, every readiness spike that the pipeline rejected as SKIP would re-fire on the next tick at the same threshold, wasting LLM budget. **`engine/events.py`**: new `SetupResult(Event)` carrying `symbol`, `outcome` ("TRADE" / "SKIP"), `action` (literal `TradeAction.action`), `bot_id`, `conviction_score`. Outcome is the canonical TRADE/SKIP classification used by Sentinel escalation. Docstring spells out the rules so future readers don't have to rediscover them: TRADE = `action ∈ {LONG, SHORT, ADD_LONG, ADD_SHORT}` AND `order_result.success == True`; SKIP = anything else (SKIP / HOLD / CLOSE_ALL / errored bot / failed order / missing order_result). **`sentinel/config.py`**: 4 new module-level constants pinning the spec defaults — `BASE_READINESS_THRESHOLD = 0.30`, `ESCALATION_STEP = 0.10`, `MAX_ESCALATION = 0.25` (ceiling = 0.30 + 0.25 = 0.55), `SKIP_COOLDOWN_SECONDS = 900` (15 minutes). New `get_sentinel_escalation_config()` accessor returns a defensive copy of all four as a dict so tests + callers can grab the bag without importing each constant individually. **`sentinel/monitor.py`** (SentinelMonitor refactor): four new constructor params with config-driven defaults — `base_threshold` (overrides the legacy `threshold` arg as the per-monitor base), `escalation_step`, `max_escalation`, `skip_cooldown_seconds`. Per-symbol escalation state lives in `_current_threshold: dict[str, float]` (keyed by symbol per the spec, even though each monitor is currently single-symbol — future-proofs the data layout for a multi-symbol monitor refactor). The cooldown duration that `_can_trigger` actually checks lives in `_active_cooldown_seconds`, which flips between the candle-period default (`_candle_cooldown_seconds`) and `SKIP_COOLDOWN_SECONDS` in response to SetupResult events. The legacy `_cooldown_seconds` attribute is preserved as a back-compat alias pointing at the candle-period default so the existing 5 `TestSentinelMonitorDynamicDefaults` tests don't have to be touched. New methods: `current_threshold(symbol=None)` (public read of the escalated value with base fallback), `subscribe_results()` (registers `_on_setup_result` on the bus — call once during wiring), `_on_setup_result(event)` (filters by symbol, dispatches to escalate/reset helpers, defensively logs+ignores unknown outcomes), `_escalate_threshold_after_skip` (raises threshold by `ESCALATION_STEP`, capped at `BASE + MAX_ESCALATION`, switches to SKIP cooldown), `_reset_threshold_after_trade` (resets to base, restores candle-period cooldown), `_reset_all_escalations_for_new_candle(new_ts)` (called from `_check_once` when the latest candle's timestamp advances). Candle-close detection lives in `_check_once` via `_last_candle_ts`: the first observation initializes the marker WITHOUT resetting (a fresh-start Sentinel shouldn't immediately wipe escalation state it never built), and subsequent observations only reset when `latest_candle_ts > _last_candle_ts`. The trigger gate at the top of `_check_once` reads `current_threshold()` (the escalated value, falling through to base) instead of the legacy `self._threshold` — this is the only place the threshold gate is evaluated, so escalation flows through one site cleanly. Public read-only properties: `base_threshold`, `active_cooldown_seconds`. **`engine/bot_manager.py`** (BotManager closes the loop): new module-level `_TRADE_ACTIONS` frozenset = `{LONG, SHORT, ADD_LONG, ADD_SHORT}` (the canonical TRADE action set). New static `_classify_outcome(result)` maps a TraderBot result dict to "TRADE" / "SKIP" via the rules in the SetupResult docstring. New async `_publish_setup_result(symbol, bot_id, result)` builds + publishes the event, with try/except so a publication failure logs but never propagates (the bot already finished, the cleanup is done, Sentinel feedback is best-effort). Both `_run_bot` (event-triggered path) AND `spawn_bot` (manual/scheduled path) call `_publish_setup_result` AFTER the active-set lock is released — the handler chain may call into Sentinel state, and we don't want it sitting on our mutex. The concurrency-blocked path in `spawn_bot` does NOT publish: the pipeline never ran, so there's no SKIP/TRADE outcome to feed back, and emitting SKIP would incorrectly escalate the Sentinel for an orthogonal reason. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The user's spec said `self._base_threshold: float = 0.30  # from config, existing value` — but the legacy `SentinelMonitor.threshold` constructor default was `0.7`, NOT 0.30. I preserved the legacy 0.7 as the back-compat default when callers don't pass `base_threshold` (so existing tests + scripts using the old `threshold=` arg keep working), and added `base_threshold` as a separate first-class arg with a `None` default that falls through to the legacy. The new `BASE_READINESS_THRESHOLD = 0.30` constant in `sentinel/config.py` is the *spec* default but is only applied when callers explicitly pass `base_threshold=BASE_READINESS_THRESHOLD` or use `get_sentinel_escalation_config()`. This is the only interpretation that doesn't break the existing 60+ Sentinel tests AND honours the user's "from config, existing value" wording. (2) The spec said "Subscribe to TradeOpened event ... if received within 60 seconds of SetupDetected, treat as TRADE. Otherwise treat as SKIP. Or: have BotManager emit a SetupResult event ... use whichever approach is cleaner" — I went with SetupResult per the spec's stated preference. The 60-second-timeout heuristic is fragile because it conflates "timeout" with "SKIP" and would force the Sentinel to maintain pending-trigger timers for every SetupDetected emission. The SetupResult approach is exactly one publish per spawn, with no timing assumptions. (3) `CLOSE_ALL` is classified SKIP for escalation purposes — a CLOSE_ALL closes a position rather than opening one, so there's no new-entry rationale to reset Sentinel's escalation. The classification rule lives in `BotManager._classify_outcome` and is documented in the SetupResult docstring; future work that wants distinct CLOSE outcome handling can add a new enum value. (4) Concurrency-blocked spawns do NOT publish SetupResult — the pipeline never ran, the bot never even existed. Emitting SKIP would falsely escalate the Sentinel for an orthogonal reason. (5) The candle-close detection treats the first observation as "initialize, don't reset" so a fresh-start Sentinel doesn't wipe nothing on its first tick (cosmetic — wiping nothing has no behavioural effect, but the log line "New candle: resetting" would be misleading). (6) Per-symbol `_current_threshold: dict[str, float]` is overkill for a single-symbol monitor, but matches the spec literally and is forward-compatible with a future multi-symbol monitor refactor. Each `SentinelMonitor` instance still uses only one key. (7) Sentinel does NOT auto-`subscribe_results()` in its constructor — callers must call it explicitly during wiring. Auto-subscribing would surprise tests that build a Sentinel + bus together without expecting bus state to be touched. The `TestSentinelEscalationBusIntegration` tests verify both the subscribed and unsubscribed paths. (8) Engine version bumped to 2026.04.2.15.0-alpha.1 (MINOR — new event + new state machine, not a bug fix). **38 new tests** across 2 files. **`tests/unit/test_sentinel.py`** (28 new): `TestSentinelEscalationConfig` (6 — pin BASE_READINESS_THRESHOLD/ESCALATION_STEP/MAX_ESCALATION/SKIP_COOLDOWN_SECONDS literals, verify `get_sentinel_escalation_config` shape + that it returns a defensive copy), `TestSentinelThresholdEscalation` (8 — initial threshold = base, 1st SKIP 0.30→0.40, 2nd SKIP 0.40→0.50, 3rd SKIP caps at 0.55, 4th+5th SKIP stay capped, TRADE resets threshold AND cooldown, SetupResult for other symbol is ignored, unknown outcome logs+ignores), `TestSentinelEscalationFiringGate` (2 — readiness below escalated threshold does NOT fire, readiness above escalated threshold DOES fire; both tests use the synthetic MockSentinelAdapter score of ~0.9 by picking base thresholds that put the escalated value above/below 0.9), `TestSentinelCandleCloseReset` (2 — new candle wipes all escalation state AND restores candle-period cooldown via in-place candle stream rotation; first observation initializes the marker without resetting), `TestSentinelEscalationPerSymbol` (1 — 2 Sentinel instances on same bus only react to their own symbol's results, BTC escalated to 0.40 leaves ETH at 0.30), `TestSentinelEscalationBusIntegration` (2 — `subscribe_results()` wires the handler end-to-end via the bus; un-subscribed Sentinel ignores bus events). **`tests/unit/test_bot_manager.py`** (10 new + new `FakeBot` test helper): `TestBotManagerSetupResultClassification` (10 pure-function tests pinning every outcome of `_classify_outcome`: LONG/SHORT/ADD_LONG/ADD_SHORT with success → TRADE; LONG with failed order / no order → SKIP; SKIP / HOLD action → SKIP; CLOSE_ALL → SKIP not TRADE; crashed bot → SKIP), `TestBotManagerSetupResultEmission` (7 end-to-end via the bus: spawn_bot emits correct SetupResult for SKIP / LONG-success / LONG-failed / CLOSE_ALL / crashed-bot cases, concurrency-blocked spawn does NOT emit, event-triggered spawn via SetupDetected → BotManager → SetupResult chains correctly). The `FakeBot` helper bypasses TraderBot + Executor entirely so the classification logic can be tested without wiring an executor for every action/order combination. **Verification**: full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1621 passed in 14.23s** (1583 → 1621, +38), zero regressions. The pre-existing 5 `TestSentinelMonitorDynamicDefaults` tests still pass unchanged because the back-compat `_cooldown_seconds` alias still resolves to the candle-period default. 1621 tests passing.
- **OHLCV widening for `price_up_flow_bearish` so FlowSignalAgent Rule 1 fires** — Follow-up to the previous calibration round, which I'd flagged as a pre-existing scenario authoring mismatch. The narrative said "price rising while flow diverges bearishly" but the literal candle close drift over the last 12 candles was only **+0.33%**, well below FlowSignalAgent's `PRICE_UP_THRESHOLD_PCT = 1.0`. Result: BEARISH-divergence Rule 1 stayed dormant on the one scenario specifically designed to test it. Fix scope is exactly what the user authorized: only OHLCV data in `backtesting/evals/scenarios/flow_divergence/price_up_flow_bearish_btc_1h_001.json`. NO prompt changes, NO code changes, NO version bumps. Replaced candles 38-49 (the last 12 of 50, the entire FlowSignalAgent lookback window) with a hand-designed sequence that delivers **+1.75% close-to-close drift** (mid-range of the user's +1.5% to +2.0% target). Anchor close[-13] = 64485.71 (candle [37]) is unchanged so the rest of the price action and computed indicators landing on the earlier portion of the stream stay stable. New candles preserve the existing 1-hour timestamp cadence (3600000ms deltas) and stay in the 1130-1220 volume range to match the "below average volume on the rally" narrative the new `volume_ratio: 0.75` flow_data field expresses. The shape is intentionally NOT a straight ramp: 10 up candles + 2 pullback candles (indices 41 and 45) with realistic upper/lower wicks (15-50 unit deviations from open/close), close-to-close steps in the +0.11% to +0.28% range with the small pullbacks at -0.06% and -0.09%. Each candle's open chains exactly to the previous candle's close (verified at design time before writing the edit). Each candle's high ≥ max(open, close) and low ≤ min(open, close). Final close lands at 65614.20 = 64485.71 × 1.0175. **Smoke verification**: re-built the FlowOutput via the eval adapter's exact `_build_flow()` code path, ran `FlowSignalAgent.analyze()` on the full updated `MarketData` (new OHLCV + the existing flow_data + indicators), result: **BEARISH @ 0.70 confidence** with reasoning *"BEARISH divergence: price +1.75% over the last 12 candles while funding flipped to -0.0002% and OI dropped -5.2% over 4h. Smart money is exiting into retail buying — classic distribution pattern."* Rule 1 now fires correctly. Both flow_divergence scenarios should now exercise their intended FlowSignalAgent rules in the next eval re-run (`price_down_oi_building` → BULLISH @ 0.70 from Rule 2, `price_up_flow_bearish` → BEARISH @ 0.70 from Rule 1). **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The hand-designed candles use rounded values (e.g. 64585.0, 65614.20) instead of the previous synthesised-looking precision (e.g. 64689.3756, 64699.0491). The earlier candles in the file still carry their original 4-decimal precision — slight stylistic inconsistency that's intentional because hand-designing 12 candles to 4 decimals is impractical and the 1-decimal precision is plenty for a 1h BTC scenario. (2) The two pullback candles (indices 41, 45) are the only `c < o` candles in the new sequence; everything else is `c > o`. This is reasonable for "price rising" but a real bull move would have more variation in the up-move size. The simplified shape is OK because the test is about whether the rule fires, not about whether the candle aesthetics fool a chartist. (3) The author-provided indicators in the scenario (RSI 65, MACD positive, volume_ma.ratio 1.0) were NOT touched even though the new OHLCV would technically compute slightly different values if recomputed from scratch. The eval `pipeline_adapter._scenario_to_market_data()` recomputes indicators from candles AND THEN layers the author-provided values on top, so the author's hand-tuned values still take precedence in what ConvictionAgent sees. The narrative remains internally consistent. (4) NO prompt changes, NO version bumps, NO code changes. **Verification**: JSON re-parses clean (50 candles total, unchanged), drift verified at +1.750% via the same close-to-close calculation FlowSignalAgent uses. Full `pytest -q` end-to-end → **1583 passed in 14.46s**, zero regressions. The eval framework's 150 tests still validate the modified scenario against the Pydantic schema. NO eval re-run performed in this task per user instruction. 1583 tests passing (unchanged).
- **Eval scenario calibration round 2 (post-v1.2 results)** — Three targeted scenario JSON adjustments based on the user's first eval pass against the v1.1 prompt + new FlowSignalAgent. NO prompt changes, NO version bumps, NO code changes — pure scenario label tightening + flow_data backfill. New keys: `oi_trend: "RISING"`, `volume_ratio: 1.3`. Funding rate left at -0.0001 (already satisfies the ≤0 condition). **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The user's wording for funding_rate was "verify funding_rate is already negative or set to -0.02 / -0.01". The existing values (-0.0002 and -0.0001) ARE already negative and satisfy FlowSignalAgent's `funding ≤ 0.0` rule, so I did not overwrite them — the literal interpretation of "verify ... or set ..." is "set only if the verification fails". The unit scale (decimal-as-percent vs percent) is technically inconsistent with the new oi_change_4h values within the same file, but funding_rate doesn't need to cross any magnitude threshold for the rule to fire — only the sign matters — so the inconsistency is functionally harmless. (2) `volume_ratio` is added as an extra key in `flow_data` per user instruction, but it is NOT consumed by FlowSignalAgent today — `FlowOutput` has no volume field, and the eval `pipeline_adapter._build_flow()` doesn't read `volume_ratio`. The grounding header reads volume from `MarketData.indicators["volume_ma"]["ratio"]`, which is a separate scope. The new key documents the scenario story for the eval reader and is forward-compatible if a future FlowSignalAgent version starts consuming volume context. Smart money is adding into the pullback") — Rule 2 fires correctly. **`price_up_flow_bearish_btc_1h_001.json` → NEUTRAL @ 0.30** ("No flow signal: funding -0.0002% (within normal band); OI -5.2% over 4h (no clear bias); price +0.33% over last 12 candles") — Rule 1 does NOT fire because the actual close-to-close drift over the last 12 candles in this scenario's OHLCV data is only +0.33%, well below FlowSignalAgent's `PRICE_UP_THRESHOLD_PCT = 1.0`. The scenario's NARRATIVE says "higher highs, RSI 65, MACD positive" but the literal candle data drifts only marginally up — that's a pre-existing mismatch from when this scenario was authored before FlowSignalAgent existed, when "price up" was narrated through indicators rather than required to be visible in the candle close stream. **Flagged for the user before the eval re-run** — see post-task summary. The fix is to widen the late-stage candle drift in the OHLCV array (not in scope for this task per "purely scenario label adjustments and data backfills"). **Verification**: 4 JSON files re-parsed clean, all `expected.conviction_min` / `conviction_max` / `flow_data` fields verified via direct read. - **FlowSignalAgent + N-signal-aware ConvictionAgent (Task 9)** — Elevates flow from a passive data dump in the grounding header into a 4th signal voice that participates in the conviction prompt alongside Indicator/Pattern/Trend. **`engine/data/flow/signal_agent.py`** (new): `FlowSignalAgent(SignalProducer)` — code-only, zero LLM cost, ~microsecond latency. Implements the full SignalProducer ABC with `name() == "flow_signal_agent"`, `signal_type() == "flow"` (new third type alongside `"llm"`/`"ml"`), `requires_vision() == False`, FeatureFlags-gated `is_enabled()`. Constructor takes optional `feature_flags`; default-enabled when no flags supplied (test-friendly). Rules pipeline (first match wins, all thresholds module-level constants for tunability): (1) **BEARISH divergence** — `price_change_pct > +1%` over last 12 candles AND `funding_rate ≤ 0` AND `oi_change_4h ≤ -2%` → confidence 0.70, "smart money exiting into retail buying" reasoning. (2) **BULLISH accumulation** — `price_change_pct < -1%` AND `funding_rate ≤ 0` AND `oi_change_4h ≥ +2%` → confidence 0.70, "smart money adding into the pullback" reasoning. (3) **Extreme crowded long** — `funding_rate > +0.10%` (no other rule fired) → contrarian BEARISH at confidence 0.55. (4) **Extreme crowded short** — `funding_rate < -0.10%` → contrarian BULLISH at confidence 0.55. (5) **Default NEUTRAL** at confidence 0.30 with explicit reasoning enumerating which inputs were missing (funding rate unavailable / OI delta unavailable / insufficient candles / within normal band) so the data moat captures *why* nothing fired. The agent NEVER returns None for "data missing" — that would silently drop the FlowAgent's voice in ConvictionAgent's prompt. None is returned only on truly unrecoverable crashes (caught by `try/except` at the `analyze()` boundary). The price-drift check reads `close` at index `-(PRICE_LOOKBACK_CANDLES + 1)` and `close` at `-1`, returning None when the candle stream is too short or malformed. Tunable constants exposed at module top: `PRICE_LOOKBACK_CANDLES=12`, `PRICE_UP_THRESHOLD_PCT=1.0`, `PRICE_DOWN_THRESHOLD_PCT=-1.0`, `FUNDING_BEARISH_MAX=0.0`, `FUNDING_NON_POSITIVE_MAX=0.0`, `FUNDING_EXTREME_CROWDED_LONG=0.10`, `FUNDING_EXTREME_CROWDED_SHORT=-0.10`, `OI_DROP_THRESHOLD_PCT=-2.0`, `OI_BUILD_THRESHOLD_PCT=2.0`, `DIVERGENCE_CONFIDENCE=0.70`, `EXTREME_FUNDING_CONFIDENCE=0.55`, `NEUTRAL_CONFIDENCE=0.30`. **OI history limitation documented inline** at the top of the module: `CryptoFlowProvider.fetch()` populates `funding_rate` and `open_interest` but does NOT populate `oi_change_4h` because it has no per-symbol OI history buffer (`engine/data/flow/crypto.py:50-57` sets `oi_trend="STABLE"` and leaves `oi_change_4h=None`). As a result, the BEARISH-divergence and BULLISH-accumulation rules will fall through to NEUTRAL in the live engine until the OI-history backfill lands. The unit tests use synthetic FlowOutputs with `oi_change_4h` populated to exercise both paths. Once a future task plumbs OI history through CryptoFlowProvider, the divergence rules start firing automatically — no change to this agent. **`engine/data/flow/__init__.py`**: re-exports `FlowSignalAgent` for ergonomic `from engine.data.flow import FlowSignalAgent` imports + adds `__all__`. **`engine/signals/base.py`** + **`engine/types.py`**: widened `signal_type` docstrings to declare `"llm" | "ml" | "flow"` as the canonical set, with a note that new strings can be added later but consumers should treat unknown values defensively. **`engine/data/charts.py::generate_grounding_header`**: stripped the OI / GEX / liquidation flow dump per the spec — only the funding-rate line stays. The rationale comment in-source explains the move (other LLM agents should focus on their specialties; flow interpretation is now FlowSignalAgent's job and lands in ConvictionAgent's signals_block via FlowSignalAgent's SignalOutput). **`engine/conviction/agent.py`** (ConvictionAgent N-signal refactor): replaced the 3 hardcoded `signal_map.get("indicator_agent" / "pattern_agent" / "trend_agent")` lookups with a new `_build_signals_block(signal_map)` method that renders all known agents in fixed order (defined by module-level `_AGENT_DISPLAY_NAMES` dict: indicator → pattern → trend → flow), followed by any unknown agents alphabetically. Missing known agents render an explicit "Agent did not produce a signal" block so the prompt structure stays predictable for the LLM. The per-agent rendering format mirrors v1.0/v1.1 EXACTLY for the first 3 agents (display names "IndicatorAgent:" / "PatternAgent:" / "TrendAgent:" and the same line layout) so prompt-cache hits and eval calibration don't drift on the existing voices. New `_render_signal_block(agent_key, display_name, sig)` static method handles per-agent rendering with conditional Pattern line (always renders for pattern_agent via `_PATTERN_LINE_ALWAYS_FOR` set, conditionally for others). New `_fallback_display_name(agent_key)` module-level helper title-cases unknown agents (e.g. `"experimental_ml_agent"` → `"ExperimentalMlAgent"`). The 14 format kwargs collapsed to 5 (`symbol`, `timeframe`, `grounding_header`, `signals_block`, `memory_context`). **`engine/conviction/prompts/conviction_v1.py`**: PROMPT_VERSION `"1.1"` → `"1.2"` and USER_PROMPT replaced the three literal `IndicatorAgent: / PatternAgent: / TrendAgent:` blocks with a single `{signals_block}` placeholder. SYSTEM_PROMPT (UNCERTAINTY ANCHOR + STRUCTURAL VETO rules from v1.1) is unchanged — only the user-side template structure changed. **`config/features.yaml`**: added `flow_signal_agent: true` so production runs (run_cycle.py / run_trade.py) actually exercise the new agent — without the flag, FeatureFlags defaults unknown keys to False and the agent would silently disable itself. **Production wiring**: `scripts/run_cycle.py`, `scripts/run_trade.py`, `backtesting/evals/pipeline_adapter.py` all updated to register `FlowSignalAgent(flags)` (or `FlowSignalAgent()` in the eval adapter, which doesn't use FeatureFlags) alongside the 3 LLM agents in the SignalRegistry. The 4th producer runs in parallel with the 3 LLM agents via the existing `asyncio.gather` in `SignalRegistry.run_all()` — no registry changes needed. **`quantagent/version.py`**: PROMPT_VERSIONS gets new `"flow_signal_agent": "1.0"` entry; `conviction_agent` bumped `1.1` → `1.2`; `ENGINE_VERSION` `2026.04.2.13.2-alpha.1` → `2026.04.2.14.0-alpha.1` (MINOR bump per the "new agents/features" rule, NOT a PATCH — this task adds a brand-new agent and refactors the conviction prompt template, not a small fix). **`PROJECT_CONTEXT.md`** line 4 synced. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The user's spec said *"No prompt change needed for this — ConvictionAgent already iterates over whatever signals it receives. But verify the prompt template handles N signals dynamically, not hardcoded to 3"*. Verification showed the prompt + agent.py were BOTH hardcoded to exactly 3 lookups — adding a 4th SignalProducer would land in the signal_map but never reach the LLM. I stopped before writing code, flagged the discrepancy with citations, and offered three options. The user picked Option A (generic N-signal block, prompt v1.1 → v1.2). This is the gated prompt change CLAUDE.md Rule 7 calls out — explicit user authorization recorded in the conversation. (2) The user JUST shipped conviction_agent v1.0 → v1.1 in the previous task with UNCERTAINTY ANCHOR + STRUCTURAL VETO rules and committed to a manual eval re-run before any of this lands in a live bot. v1.2 chains onto the same pre-eval batch — both prompt deltas are now staged together and will be evaluated together. The user is aware. (3) I removed the GEX line from the grounding header even though the user's literal wording was "remove the detailed OI/liquidation dump" — GEX is detailed flow data that falls under the spirit of "the other agents should focus on their specialties". The user explicitly confirmed "strip GEX" in the Option A response. (4) I named the new signal_type `"flow"` per user instruction even though the existing convention (`"llm"`/`"ml"`) describes HOW the signal is computed and `"flow"` describes the DOMAIN — slight inconsistency, but user explicitly chose `"flow"`. (5) The version bump is MINOR, not PATCH, because this is a new agent + a prompt structural refactor — that's a feature add per the version.py docstring conventions, not a bug fix. (6) The eval pipeline_adapter registers `FlowSignalAgent()` without feature flags so it always runs in eval mode regardless of `config/features.yaml` — the eval is meant to exercise the full pipeline. Tests: **31 new tests** across 2 files. **`tests/unit/test_flow_signal_agent.py`** (28): SignalProducer interface conformance (5 — name, signal_type=='flow', requires_vision, default-enabled-no-flags, disabled-by-unset-flag, enabled-by-flag), Rule 1 BEARISH divergence (3 — fires correctly with right reasoning text, doesn't fire when OI only slightly negative, doesn't fire when funding positive), Rule 2 BULLISH accumulation (3 — fires correctly, funding == 0 still qualifies, doesn't fire when OI flat), Rule 3 Extreme crowded long (2 — fires contrarian BEARISH, exact-threshold doesn't fire), Rule 4 Extreme crowded short (2 — fires contrarian BULLISH, exact-threshold doesn't fire), Rule 5 NEUTRAL default + edge cases (5 — normal conditions, no-flow-data, funding-None, oi_change-None documents provider limitation, too-few-candles), Rule precedence (2 — divergence takes priority over extreme funding, accumulation takes priority over extreme short), SignalOutput shape contract (3 — signal_type=="flow" + agent_name + signal_category, data_richness lowercased from FULL to full, raw_output mirrors reasoning), Crash safety (2 — synthetic crash returns None via the boundary try/except, threshold constants pinned against spec). The test helper `_make_candles(start_close, end_close, count)` builds a candle stream where the LAST `PRICE_LOOKBACK_CANDLES + 1` candles drift cleanly from start to end, so tests can pin exact percentages — the first `count - PRICE_LOOKBACK_CANDLES - 1` candles sit flat at `start_close`. **`tests/unit/test_conviction_agent.py`** (2 new): `test_flow_signal_renders_in_user_prompt` — regression test for the v1.1 → v1.2 prompt refactor, verifies the 4th SignalOutput (signal_type="flow") actually reaches the LLM via the signals_block (asserts "FlowAgent:", "BEARISH", "0.70", "smart money exiting" all appear in `last_user_prompt`). `test_flow_block_renders_empty_when_flow_missing` — verifies the FlowAgent slot still renders with "Agent did not produce a signal" reasoning when no flow signal is in the input list, so the prompt structure stays predictable for the LLM. **`tests/unit/test_charts.py`** updates: `test_includes_flow_data` flipped to assert NEGATIVE on OI/GEX/liquidation substrings (`"OI change:" not in header`, `"BUILDING" not in header`, `"POSITIVE_GAMMA" not in header`, `"GEX:" not in header`, `"GEX flip:" not in header`) while keeping the funding-line positive assertions. - **ConvictionAgent prompt v1.1 + 4 eval scenario calibrations** — Two-part change paving the way for the next eval re-run. **PART A — scenario `conviction_max` widened in 4 files**: `regime_transitions/trending_to_ranging_btc_1h_001.json` (0.35 → 0.45), `clear_avoids/low_volume_weekend_001.json` (0.35 → 0.45), `high_impact_events/post_cpi_surprise_eth_1h_001.json` (0.30 → 0.45), `high_impact_events/pre_fomc_btc_1h_001.json` (0.30 → 0.45). All 4 are SKIP-expected scenarios where the prior bands were too tight against the model's natural "uncertain" output range — pushing the ceiling to 0.45 makes "near-miss" answers (0.40-0.45) pass while still rejecting any meaningful conviction (≥0.50). The literal narrative + indicator data are unchanged; only the grading band shifted. **PART B — `engine/conviction/prompts/conviction_v1.py` system prompt v1.0 → v1.1**: appended two new rules to `SYSTEM_PROMPT` AFTER the existing `CONVICTION SCORING RULES` block. Existing prompt content was NOT touched. (1) **RULE — UNCERTAINTY ANCHOR**: tells the LLM that genuine uncertainty / lack of edge / conflicting signals / high-risk macro conditions MUST anchor between 0.10-0.30, and that the 0.40-0.49 range is RESERVED for "near-miss" setups where a clear pattern exists but one specific concern blocks full confidence. Explicitly forbids "default to 0.40 because uncertain" — if uncertain, output 0.15-0.25. The two ranges (0.10-0.30 vs 0.40-0.49) are deliberately disjoint so the model can't smear them together. (2) **RULE — STRUCTURAL VETO (Signals Are Not A Democracy)**: codifies four veto cases that force conviction drops on top of normal scoring: (a) parent 4h bearish + analysis 1h bullish → STRUCTURAL VETO, drop ≥0.25 (multi-TF alignment is required, not a 2-vs-1 vote); (b) 2/3 signal agents agree but the dissenter flags a specific structural risk (RSI/volume divergence, regime transition) → treat as WARNING not minority opinion, drop ≥0.15; (c) all 3 signal agents agree but FlowAgent contradicts (price up + funding/OI bearish) → drop ≥0.15; (d) conviction > 0.75 ONLY when ALL signals agree without ANY structural veto. Both rules are written in plain prose (no JSON braces, no template variables) so they pass through `SYSTEM_PROMPT.replace(...)` cleanly without colliding with the existing `{{symbol}}/{{timeframe}}/{{grounding_header}}` placeholder syntax. **`engine/conviction/prompts/conviction_v1.py`**: `PROMPT_VERSION = "1.0"` → `"1.1"`. **`quantagent/version.py`**: `PROMPT_VERSIONS["conviction_agent"] = "1.0"` → `"1.1"`, `ENGINE_VERSION` 2026.04.2.13.1-alpha.1 → 2026.04.2.13.2-alpha.1 (PATCH bump per the "prompt improvements" rule). PROJECT_CONTEXT.md line 4 synced. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) Per CLAUDE.md Rule 7 ("NEVER modify agent prompt files unless explicitly asked"), this change would normally be gated. The user provided explicit authorization in the task message AND committed to re-running the eval manually after all fixes are applied — the regression-test gate is satisfied by that follow-up, NOT by an in-task eval run, because the eval costs real Claude calls and the user is staging multiple prompt patches before paying for one re-run. (2) The 0.40-0.49 "near-miss" reservation in the new prompt is deliberately the SAME band that PART A widened the scenario `conviction_max` ceilings to. The two halves of this task are coupled: we're telling the model "use 0.40-0.49 only for near-misses" AND simultaneously telling the eval grader "0.40-0.45 is acceptable for SKIP-expected scenarios". If only one half shipped, the calibration would be off in one direction or the other. (3) The `clear_avoids/low_volume_weekend_001.json` scenario was NOT in the user's original wording but is in the user's task list — the file was already at 0.35 and is updated to 0.45 alongside the regime_transitions one (same delta). (4) `pre_fomc_btc_1h_001.json` and `post_cpi_surprise_eth_1h_001.json` had `conviction_max: 0.3` (single decimal place), not `0.30` as the user wrote — same numeric value, JSON normalises trailing zeros. The Edit operation uses the literal source form. (5) Engine version bumped to 2026.04.2.13.2-alpha.1. **Verification**: full test suite re-run end-to-end via `pytest -q` → **1552 passed in 14.40s**, no regressions. (2) Inserted `from dotenv import load_dotenv` at the top of `backtesting/evals/_cli.py` and a module-level `load_dotenv()` call right after the import block, so the `.env` file is read once when `_cli.py` is first imported — which happens before any of the three harness scripts call `build_adapter()` and therefore before any LLM call can fire. The call uses dotenv's default search behaviour (walks up from cwd to find `.env`), so it works whether the harness is invoked from the project root, from `backtesting/`, or via `python -m backtesting.evals.run_smoke`. (3) Installed the package into the existing venv via `/opt/homebrew/Caskroom/miniconda/base/bin/pip --python /Users/alireza/Documents/QuantGOD/QuantAgent_v2/.venv/bin/python install "python-dotenv>=1.0"` because the venv's own `pip` shim is broken (its shebang points at `/Users/alireza/Documents/QuantGOD/QuantAgent v2/.venv/bin/python3.12` — the OLD path with a literal space, before the directory was renamed to `QuantAgent_v2` — so `pip` can't even start; `python -m pip` also fails with `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'pip._vendor.rich'` because the vendored bundle is incomplete). Used the base miniconda pip with `--python` targeting the venv binary as a workaround that doesn't require recreating the venv. - **Binance Data-Download Adapter (Task 7)** — `exchanges/binance.py` ships `BinanceAdapter(ExchangeAdapter)` for USDT-M perpetual futures via CCXT (`options.defaultType="future"`). **DATA DOWNLOAD ONLY** by design: `fetch_ohlcv` is the only implemented method; every order / position / balance method raises `NotImplementedError("BinanceAdapter is data-download only. Trading not yet implemented (Phase 5 Week 10).")` so the live executor cannot accidentally route orders to Binance before the trading surface has been audited. The trading methods all reference a single shared `_TRADING_NOT_IMPLEMENTED` constant so future wording changes only need one edit. Constructor takes `testnet: bool = False` for interface symmetry with other adapters; in data-download mode the venue does not switch (historical kline endpoints are identical between mainnet and testnet) but the flag still calls `set_sandbox_mode(True)` so future trading work inherits the right toggle. **No API key required** for OHLCV — Binance's public kline endpoint is unauthenticated, verified by constructing the adapter without any environment variables. **Symbol mapping** is intentionally programmatic (NOT a hardcoded dict like Hyperliquid): `_to_ccxt_symbol("BTC-USDC")` → `"BTC/USDT:USDT"` for any base, since Binance perpetuals settle in USDT not USDC and there is no USDC-margined perp on Binance Futures. The helper also accepts `BASE-USDT` as a sibling form (caller already knows they want a USDT-quoted contract) and passes already-CCXT-formatted strings through unchanged. Unknown formats raise `ValueError` with a clear message (`"BTCUSDC"`, `"BTC-EUR"` etc. are rejected). The reverse helper `_from_ccxt_symbol("BTC/USDT:USDT")` canonicalises back to `"BTC-USDC"` so the Parquet path stays `data/parquet/binance/BTC-USDC/` and consumers (downloader, loader, backtest engine) never see Binance's USDT shape — same convention as the rest of the codebase. `SYMBOL_OVERRIDES` empty dict kept as the documented escape hatch for future tickers whose Binance ticker doesn't match the BASE prefix (e.g. wrapped variants). **Capabilities** are deliberately set to reflect Binance's long-term feature set (`native_sl_tp=True`, `supports_short=True`, `has_funding_rate=True`, `has_oi_data=True`, `max_leverage=125.0`, `order_types=["market", "limit", "stopMarket", "takeProfitMarket"]`) even though the current implementation only exposes data download — capabilities are read by config / sizing code that may run before trading is enabled, and lying about the venue's properties would mislead downstream cost models. The trading-method `NotImplementedError` is the source of truth for "what's actually wired" — the capabilities dict describes the venue, not the adapter's current surface. **Registered** via `ExchangeFactory.register("binance", BinanceAdapter)` at module bottom (matches Hyperliquid pattern); `scripts/download_history.py` updated with `import exchanges.binance  # noqa` so the registration side-effect fires on every CLI invocation. The factory's singleton cache works unchanged. **No new dependency** added to `pyproject.toml` — CCXT already ships Binance support out of the box. **Verified end-to-end** by a real download against the live Binance API: `python scripts/download_history.py --exchange binance --symbols BTC-USDC,ETH-USDC,SOL-USDC --timeframes 15m,30m,1h,4h --months 6` → **72 files, 82,791 candles, zero errors** in ~3 minutes (3 symbols × 4 timeframes × 6 months = 72 month-files, 1s rate-limit between paginated batches, downloader's pagination loop handles Binance's 1000-candle-per-request limit transparently). On-disk layout exactly matches the spec: `data/parquet/binance/{SYMBOL}/{TIMEFRAME}_{YYYY-MM}.parquet`. Spot-check of `data/parquet/binance/BTC-USDC/1h_2025-11.parquet`: 720 rows (= 30 days × 24 hours, full November), correct schema (`timestamp, open, high, low, close, volume`), BTC range $82,188 → $111,145. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) Tests landed at `tests/adapters/test_binance.py`, NOT `tests/test_exchanges/test_binance.py` as the user spec said. The existing convention is `tests/adapters/test_hyperliquid.py` and adding a new sibling directory for one new file would be inconsistent — the existing layout wins. (2) The factory-registration test had to call `ExchangeFactory.register("binance", BinanceAdapter)` directly after `reset()` rather than re-importing the module, because Python module-import side effects don't fire on the second `import` of an already-loaded module — `sys.modules` caches the first import, so the registration call at the bottom of `exchanges/binance.py` only runs once per process. The test docstring flags this inline. (3) `_from_ccxt_symbol` canonicalises USDT contracts back to `BASE-USDC` rather than preserving the venue's actual quote currency. This is the right call because the rest of the codebase speaks USDC end-to-end and the on-disk Parquet path should not vary by venue — the adapter is the single translation point. (4) Capabilities are aspirational, not actual. They describe the venue's full feature set; the trading-method `NotImplementedError` is the source of truth for what's plumbed today. A future capability check that asks "can Binance do X?" will get the right answer; a future executor that tries to USE method X will get a clear error. (5) Engine version bumped to 2026.04.2.13.0-alpha.1. (6) Pre-existing pattern: trading-method `NotImplementedError` instead of returning a stub `OrderResult(success=False, error="not implemented")` — fail-loud is the right call here because a silent stub would hide the bug from any future caller until production. **35 new tests** in `tests/adapters/test_binance.py`: **TestSymbolConversion** (10): `BTC-USDC` / `ETH-USDC` / `SOL-USDC` map to `*/USDT:USDT`, arbitrary base (AVAX, DOGE) works programmatically, `BTC-USDT` sibling form accepted, CCXT format passes through unchanged, unknown format (`"BTCUSDC"`, `"BTC-EUR"`) raises `ValueError("cannot convert")`, empty base (`"-USDC"`) raises `ValueError("empty base")`, override dict consulted before fallback rule, `_from_ccxt_symbol` canonicalises BTC/ETH/SOL back to BASE-USDC. **TestIdentity** (2): `name() == "binance"`, capabilities is `AdapterCapabilities` instance with the declared Binance perp features. **TestConstructor** (4): `defaultType=future` set in CCXT config, no API key required (constructs without env vars), `testnet=True` calls `set_sandbox_mode(True)`, default mainnet doesn't call sandbox toggle. **TestFetchOHLCV** (5): canonical dict shape returned, translated symbol passed to CCXT positional args (`call.args[0] == "BTC/USDT:USDT"`), ETH symbol routes correctly, error returns empty list (so the downloader's pagination loop interprets `[]` as "stop"), mapping errors raise via `_to_ccxt_symbol` (not silently swallowed by the outer try/except). **TestTradingNotImplemented** (12 parametrised + 1 marker test): all 12 trading methods (`get_ticker`, `get_balance`, `get_positions`, `place_market_order`, `place_limit_order`, `place_sl_order`, `place_tp_order`, `cancel_order`, `cancel_all_orders`, `close_position`, `modify_sl`, `modify_tp`) raise `NotImplementedError` matching `"data-download only"`; the marker constant `_TRADING_NOT_IMPLEMENTED` contains both `"data-download only"` and `"Phase 5"` (so a future task that changes wording fails this test loudly and stays consistent across the suite). **TestFactoryRegistration** (1): `ExchangeFactory.get_adapter("binance")` returns a `BinanceAdapter` instance with `name() == "binance"`. 1552 tests total passing (1517 → 1552, +35).
- **Bugfix: backtest sim never charged fees** — Broken: `BacktestEngine.__init__` constructed `SimulatedExchangeAdapter(...)` at `backtesting/engine.py:149` without passing the `fee_model` argument that the adapter already accepts. The adapter's `_charge_fee()` (`backtesting/sim_exchange.py:763`) early-returned `0.0` whenever `_fee_model is None`, so EVERY simulated entry + exit fill was billed at zero across the entire backtest history. Symptom: 243-trade mechanical backtest reported `Total fees: $0.00` even though `BacktestMetrics.total_fees` aggregates the per-trade `fee` field correctly and `_open_or_add_position` / `_close_or_reduce_position` already call `_charge_fee` on every fill. The full fee plumbing (adapter → trade record → metrics) was intact end-to-end — only the construction-time injection was missing. Fix: (1) added `engine/execution/cost_models/__init__.py::get_cost_model(exchange)` factory that returns `HyperliquidCostModel()` for `"hyperliquid"` (4.5 bps taker at tier 0, no metadata fetch needed) and `GenericCostModel()` (10 bps taker conservative default) for everything else — falls back to a non-None instance so fees are only zero when explicitly disabled. (2) Threaded an optional `cost_model: ExecutionCostModel | None` constructor param through `BacktestEngine.__init__` defaulting to `get_cost_model(config.exchange)`, then passed it to `SimulatedExchangeAdapter` via the existing `fee_model=` parameter. Caller-supplied adapters are honoured unchanged — never silently overwrite caller intent. Verified: re-ran `python scripts/run_backtest.py --mode mechanical --symbols BTC-USDC --timeframes 1h --start 2025-11-01 --end 2026-01-01 --balance 10000`, fees jumped from $0.00 → $905.94 across 243 trades. Final balance dropped $7,535 → $7,015 (the new fee drag plus a few additional margin-limited trades). All 341 backtesting tests still pass — the change is additive (new optional ctor param + new factory module). 1517 tests passing.

- **Blackout Windows + MacroReassessmentRequired Event** — Closes Week 7 / Task 6 + ARCHITECTURE.md §13.2.4 + §13.2.5: wires the §13.2 macro overlay into the live engine and implements the swarm-consensus pipeline for emergency assessments. **`engine/conviction/agent.py`** (ConvictionAgent) gets two new constructor params: `macro_regime_path` (default `Path("macro_regime.json")`, points at the project root by convention) and an injectable `clock` (defaults to `datetime.now(tz=timezone.utc)`). At the START of every `evaluate()` call — BEFORE any LLM work — `_load_active_macro_regime()` reads the file via `mcp.macro_regime.agent.load_macro_regime()`, discards if (a) missing, (b) carrying an `error`, or (c) past `expires`, logging an INFO message in each case so the first cycle after a deploy makes it obvious whether the file was found. The "discard" path is the safe default: the cycle proceeds normally with no overlay applied. When a valid regime IS loaded, `_active_blackout()` walks `macro.blackout_windows` and returns the first one whose `BlackoutWindow.contains(now)` returns True. On hit, the agent SHORT-CIRCUITS THE LLM CALL ENTIRELY via `_blackout_skip(reason, macro)` which returns a `ConvictionOutput` with `conviction_score=0.0`, `direction="SKIP"`, structured `"Blackout window active: {reason}. No new entries permitted."` reasoning, and the new `macro_blackout_reason` field stamped with the event name (`"FOMC_ANNOUNCEMENT"`, `"CPI"`, etc.) so downstream tracking / data moat capture can trace why the cycle was skipped without re-loading the file. The blackout_skip output also stamps the regime label, threshold boost, and size multiplier so the data moat is consistent across blackout vs. non-blackout cycles. For non-NEUTRAL regimes OUTSIDE a blackout, `_format_macro_context(macro)` is appended to the LLM user prompt as a `## MACRO REGIME OVERLAY` block containing: regime label, confidence, reasoning, conviction threshold boost, position size multiplier, avoid_assets, prefer_assets, and an explicit instruction to the LLM: "Treat this as ONE additional input — do NOT override your direction call solely on the macro regime." The macro regime is a contextual signal, not a hard director — that's the §13.2 contract. After parse, `_apply_macro_overlay(output, macro)` stamps the regime label, threshold boost, and size multiplier onto the parsed `ConvictionOutput`. **The score itself is preserved unmutated** — the LLM's actual judgment lands in the data moat without distortion; downstream consumers (DecisionAgent, the threshold gate in the executor's decision pipeline) read the boost field and apply it at the comparison site. This is the only interpretation that preserves data moat fidelity AND lets future code apply the boost wherever the threshold check actually happens. **`engine/types.py`**: 4 new optional fields on `ConvictionOutput` — `macro_regime: str = "NEUTRAL"`, `macro_threshold_boost: float = 0.0`, `macro_position_size_multiplier: float = 1.0`, `macro_blackout_reason: str | None = None`. All defaulted to the no-overlay state so every existing constructor (in tests + production) continues to work unchanged. The fields are added to the existing dataclass — not a new subclass — because ConvictionOutput is the unique payload type for `ConvictionScored` events and consistency across the data moat matters more than preserving the literal class shape. **`sentinel/monitor.py`** (SentinelMonitor) gets matching `macro_regime_path` + `clock` constructor params. Inside `_check_once`, after the readiness score is computed AND the cooldown / daily-budget gate has approved the trigger, `_active_blackout_reason()` is called: it loads the macro file via `load_macro_regime`, honours the `expires` timestamp (a stale regime overlay should NOT keep blocking new entries indefinitely), walks `blackout_windows`, and returns the reason if any contain `now`. On hit: a single `INFO`-level log line (`"Sentinel: {symbol} setup detected (readiness={score:.2f}) but blackout active ({reason}), suppressing"`) and `return` — NO event is emitted, NO daily budget counter is incremented, NO `_last_trigger` is stamped. This is a deliberate deviation from a literal "before emitting" reading of the spec: a blackout that consumes 8 daily triggers would prevent any post-blackout setups from firing, which is exactly the wrong behaviour. The blackout suppression is silent at the bot-spawning layer because the upstream Sentinel state stays warm — when the blackout ends, the next normal tick can fire immediately. The entire blackout check is wrapped in try/except so a malformed JSON cannot crash the Sentinel loop; warnings go to the logger and the cycle continues without suppression. Missing/expired/corrupt files all default to "no suppression". **`engine/events.py`**: 3 new event types added under `MacroUpdated`. **`VolumeAnomaly`** (symbol, severity 0-1, detail) and **`ExtremeMove`** (symbol, severity, move_pct, detail) are emitted by future Sentinel anomaly detectors and consumed by the aggregator — the event TYPES land in this task but no Sentinel code yet emits them; the existing Sentinel only emits `SetupDetected`. Future work in `sentinel/conditions.py` (or a new `sentinel/anomaly.py`) will fire these when single-symbol volume / price anomalies are detected. **`MacroReassessmentRequired`** (triggering_symbols: list[str], anomaly_types: list[str], severity_scores: list[float], triggered_at: str) is the swarm-consensus output. The `triggered_at` field mirrors the dataclass `timestamp` as an ISO 8601 UTC string so downstream JSON serialisation (LangSmith traces, audit logs) doesn't need to format the datetime separately. **`sentinel/macro_aggregator.py`** (new module) ships `MacroEventAggregator` — the swarm-consensus pipeline per §13.2.5. Constructor takes `event_bus`, `window_seconds=60`, `min_unique_symbols=5`, `cooldown_seconds=600` (10 minutes), and an injectable `clock`. Defaults pulled out as module-level constants (`DEFAULT_WINDOW_SECONDS`, `DEFAULT_MIN_UNIQUE_SYMBOLS`, `DEFAULT_COOLDOWN_SECONDS`) so tests pin the literal §13.2.5 numbers. `subscribe()` registers `handle_event` for both `VolumeAnomaly` and `ExtremeMove`; `unsubscribe()` removes it. Pending events are held in an `OrderedDict[(symbol, anomaly_type), _PendingEvent]` — keying on the (symbol, type) tuple deduplicates within-symbol noise (if BTC fires VolumeAnomaly twice in 30 seconds, only the most recent observation lives in the window) WITHOUT collapsing the cross-type signal (a single symbol firing both VolumeAnomaly AND ExtremeMove still contributes both observations). The unique-symbol count is taken at trigger time over symbols only, NOT over (symbol, type) pairs: per §13.2.5 "5 or more active Sentinels across different assets". The OrderedDict uses insertion order ≈ recency so eviction is O(1) per drop — the eviction loop walks from oldest to newest and stops on the first fresh entry. `handle_event(event)` flow: defensive type check, defensive empty-symbol check, increment `events_received`, `_evict_expired(now)`, upsert the (symbol, type) key, `move_to_end` (most-recent observation wins on a re-fire). The cooldown check happens AFTER ingest so the window stays warm during the 10-minute lockout — once cooldown expires, an already-hot window can fire immediately without a fresh batch. `triggers_suppressed_cooldown` increments on every cooldown-blocked emission for observability. Trigger condition: `len({ev.symbol for ev in pending.values()}) >= min_symbols`. On trigger, `_emit_reassessment(now)` builds the payload: per-symbol the highest-severity observation wins (so if BTC has both VolumeAnomaly@0.3 and ExtremeMove@0.9 in the window, BTC's reported severity is 0.9 — the worst observation per asset), `triggering_symbols` is sorted, `anomaly_types` is the deduped sorted union across all pending events, `severity_scores` is the per-symbol max in the same order as `triggering_symbols`. `triggered_at` is the ISO 8601 form of `now`. After publish, the window is CLEARED and `_last_trigger = now` — per §13.2.5 we must NOT re-trigger immediately even if more anomalies arrive. Failed publishes (handler errors) are logged but don't mutate state — the next event will retry. `AggregatorMetrics` exposes `events_received`, `events_dropped_oldest`, `triggers_emitted`, `triggers_suppressed_cooldown` for observability. **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) ConvictionAgent's threshold boost is STAMPED on the output, not applied by mutating `conviction_score` — see commentary above on data moat fidelity. The downstream threshold check site reads `output.macro_threshold_boost` and applies it at the comparison. (2) `position_size_multiplier` is similarly stamped on the output; DecisionAgent will read it in a future task when the sizing pipeline is touched. The wiring of DecisionAgent → `output.macro_position_size_multiplier` is intentionally not in scope. (3) Sentinel blackout check happens AFTER cooldown — preserves daily budget across blackouts. Documented above. (4) `VolumeAnomaly` and `ExtremeMove` are added as event TYPES only — no Sentinel code currently fires them. Future work will add the detectors. (5) Aggregator unique-count is over symbols, NOT (symbol, anomaly_type) pairs. (6) `MacroReassessmentRequired` is published to the bus but no handler is wired to the MCP runner yet — the spec explicitly says "handler not wired to MCP runner yet — that's infrastructure work for later". A future task will add a thin handler that spawns `python -m mcp.macro_regime.runner --mode emergency --trigger-symbols ...` (or calls the runner in-process). (7) The `_FIXED_NOW` clock injection pattern from Task 5 is reused everywhere so tests are deterministic — both ConvictionAgent and SentinelMonitor accept a `clock` constructor param. (8) Engine version bumped to 2026.04.2.12.0-alpha.1. 28 new tests across 2 files. **`tests/test_mcp/test_blackout.py`** (12): `test_blackout_forces_conviction_zero` — full pipeline through ConvictionAgent with a blackout-active macro file, asserts conviction_score=0.0, direction=SKIP, macro_blackout_reason="FOMC_ANNOUNCEMENT", "Blackout window active" in reasoning, AND the LLM call_count==0 (short-circuit verified). `test_blackout_outside_window_proceeds` — blackout window 5h in the future, LLM IS called normally, score is the LLM's value, no blackout reason stamped. `test_risk_off_stamps_boost_and_multiplier` — RISK_OFF non-blackout regime, asserts `macro_regime`, `macro_threshold_boost`, `macro_position_size_multiplier` all populated AND the conviction score is preserved unmutated. `test_risk_off_injects_macro_context_into_prompt` — captures the user_prompt via a recording LLM stub, asserts `MACRO REGIME OVERLAY`, `RISK_OFF`, and the `TSLA-USDC` avoid asset all appear. `test_neutral_regime_does_not_inject_context` — NEUTRAL regime → no overlay block. `test_missing_macro_file_proceeds_normally` — file path that doesn't exist, LLM called once, default macro fields (`NEUTRAL`, `0.0`, `1.0`, `None`). `test_expired_macro_file_ignored` — file declares a blackout but is 1h past expires, LLM called normally. `test_corrupt_macro_file_proceeds_normally` — invalid JSON, no crash. `test_sentinel_suppresses_setup_during_blackout` — Sentinel with blackout file, verifies `received` is empty AND `daily_triggers_remaining == daily_budget` (budget NOT consumed). `test_sentinel_emits_setup_outside_blackout` — no blackout, normal emission. `test_sentinel_no_macro_file_emits_normally` and `test_sentinel_expired_macro_file_emits_normally` — both default to no suppression. **`tests/test_mcp/test_macro_aggregator.py`** (16): `_Clock` helper for deterministic time advancement. `test_4_symbols_no_trigger`, `test_5_unique_symbols_within_window_triggers` (verifies sorted symbols, types, severities), `test_5_events_same_symbol_no_trigger`, `test_5_events_2_symbols_no_trigger`, `test_5_symbols_spread_over_90s_no_trigger` (eviction kills earlier entries — 5 events 25s apart spans 100s, first one ages out before the 5th arrives), `test_mixed_volume_and_extreme_events_count_toward_threshold`, `test_same_symbol_both_event_types_counts_once` (BTC fires both Volume + Extreme, plus ETH/SOL/AVAX → only 4 unique symbols → no trigger), `test_severity_payload_uses_max_per_symbol` (BTC fires Volume@0.3 + Extreme@0.9 → reported BTC severity is 0.9), `test_cooldown_blocks_immediate_retrigger` (5 fresh symbols within cooldown still don't fire + `triggers_suppressed_cooldown` incremented), `test_retrigger_allowed_after_cooldown` (10s cooldown, advance 15s, fresh swarm fires), `test_window_reset_after_emission` (cooldown=0 still requires a fresh batch — the 5 symbols of the second swarm have to be uploaded one at a time, the 5th triggers), `test_subscribe_wires_to_bus` (publishes through the real `InProcessBus` instead of calling handle_event directly), `test_unsubscribe_stops_handling`, `test_event_without_symbol_ignored` (defensive — empty string symbol drops without crashing), `test_unrelated_event_type_ignored` (defensive — wrong type doesn't crash), `test_default_constants_match_spec` (60s/5/600s pinned). 1517 tests total passing (1489 → 1517, +28). **(1517 total)**

### 2026-04-08
- **Macro Regime Manager MCP Agent (3-tier macro assessment)** — Closes Week 7 / Task 5 + ARCHITECTURE.md §13.2: a complete offline agent that fetches macro-economic data, classifies the current regime, and produces `macro_regime.json` consumed by ConvictionAgent (Task 6) for global risk-parameter overlay and blackout-window enforcement. **5 new modules** under `mcp/macro_regime/`. **`data_fetcher.py`** ships `MacroDataFetcher.fetch()` which pulls from 6 public APIs in series with 1s rate-limiting between calls: VIX/DXY via Yahoo Finance `/v7/finance/quote`, DVOL via Deribit `/api/v2/public/get_index_price`, Crypto Fear & Greed via alternative.me `/fng/`, BTC Dominance via CoinGecko `/api/v3/global`, and Hyperliquid total OI + average funding via `/info` POST `metaAndAssetCtxs`. The HL aggregator sums `openInterest * markPx` across all markets for total OI in USD and arithmetic-means the per-market `funding` field. Each fetch is wrapped at the dispatch level so a 503 from Yahoo doesn't take down the run — partial data is preferred over no data, and the resulting `MacroSnapshot` carries an `available_sources` set and an `errors` dict so callers (and the LightweightCheck weekend logic) can tell which sources are live. Calendar fetching is hardcoded for now: a small list of FOMC/CPI/NFP dates within a 30-day lookahead, filtered to the current `clock()` so a fixed-clock test always sees a deterministic subset. The fetcher accepts an injected `http_client`, `sleep_func`, and `clock` so tests run offline and deterministically. The default httpx.Client is constructed lazily so `--help` doesn't import httpx. `MacroSnapshot` exposes `to_dict`/`from_dict` for the snapshot persistence layer, plus a `has_data(source)` helper. Helper exports: `parse_iso` (Z-suffix tolerant), `filter_calendar_within(events, ref, hours)`, `EconomicEvent` dataclass with `parsed_time()`. **`lightweight_check.py`** ships `LightweightCheck.run(current, previous)` — the pure-code, no-LLM, ~$0 hourly delta gate per §13.2.1. Triggers `should_trigger_deep` on ANY of: VIX moved >5%, DXY >1%, DVOL >10%, Hyperliquid total OI >10%, Fear & Greed *category* changed (case-insensitive normalisation so "Fear" → "fear" doesn't fire), or a HIGH-impact economic event within the next 24 hours. The `_pct_change_reason` helper returns a human-readable string per fired rule (e.g. `"VIX moved +7.50% (threshold ±5.0%)"`) which the runner surfaces in its summary AND the deep-analysis prompt feeds to the LLM as urgency context. **Weekend special** (§13.2.2): when `now.weekday() ∈ {Sat, Sun}` AND BOTH VIX/DXY timestamps are >24h stale (or missing), the check skips the VIX/DXY rules entirely and bumps the DVOL threshold from 10% to 15%. DVOL becomes the sole volatility signal during TradFi off-hours — a Sunday-night DVOL spike still triggers an emergency assessment. The check persists the current snapshot atomically (tmp+rename) to `macro_regime_snapshot.json` so the next tick has a baseline; `load_previous()` reads it back if `previous=None` is passed. Threshold constants are exported as module-level (`VIX_DELTA_THRESHOLD_PCT`, etc.) so tests pin the literal §13.2.1 numbers. `CheckResult` dataclass holds `should_trigger_deep`, `reasons`, `snapshot`, `previous`, plus `to_dict()`. **`agent.py`** ships `MacroRegimeManager` — the LLM-powered deep / emergency assessment class. Constructor takes `llm_provider`, `output_path` (default `macro_regime.json`), and an injectable `clock`. `run_deep(snapshot, urgency, triggering_symbols, reasons, dry_run)` is the single async entry point. Workflow: (1) build the assessment prompt via `build_assessment_prompt(snapshot, urgency, triggering_symbols, reasons)` which formats every snapshot field with `(unavailable)` placeholders for missing data, lists the next 8 calendar events, and tags the urgency level + triggering context; (2) call `llm.generate_text(agent_name="macro_regime_manager")` with `temperature=0.2` and `max_tokens=1024`; (3) parse the LLM JSON via `_parse_llm_json` which tolerates ```json fences AND prose-prefixed responses (`_BARE_JSON_RE` finds the first `{...}` block); (4) validate via `_payload_to_regime`: regime ∈ {RISK_ON, RISK_OFF, NEUTRAL}, confidence ∈ [0,1], and clamp `position_size_multiplier` to [0.1, 2.0] and `conviction_threshold_boost` to [0.0, 0.5] so a hallucinated 99x can't propagate into the live system; (5) call `_finalise` which stamps `generated_at = now`, `expires = now + 24h`, builds `blackout_windows` deterministically from the calendar via `build_blackout_windows()`, and atomically writes via tmp+rename. **The LLM is explicitly told (in the system prompt) to NEVER suggest blackout_windows in its JSON** — the system picks the dates, the LLM picks the regime. Every error path (LLM call failure, JSON parse failure, payload validation failure, write failure) returns a `MacroRegime` with `error` set, never crashes. `build_blackout_windows(events, reference, pre_buffer_minutes=60, post_buffer_minutes=30, lookahead_hours=48)` walks the calendar, filters to HIGH-impact events only (per §13.2.4 — FOMC/CPI/NFP — MEDIUM events get NO window), excludes events outside the lookahead horizon AND events more than `post_buffer_minutes` in the past, and emits one `BlackoutWindow{start, end, reason, action="execution_block"}` per qualifying event. The pre/post buffers match §13.2.4: 1h before, 30min after by default. Dataclasses: `MacroRegime` (regime, confidence, reasoning, adjustments, blackout_windows, generated_at, expires, error, output_path), `MacroAdjustments` (conviction_threshold_boost, max_concurrent_positions_override, position_size_multiplier, avoid_assets, prefer_assets — with `from_dict` defaults), `BlackoutWindow` (with a `contains(when)` helper for ConvictionAgent in Task 6). `load_macro_regime(path)` is a module-level helper that ConvictionAgent + Sentinel will call in Task 6 to read the persisted file — tolerates missing/corrupt files by returning None. **`runner.py`** is the cron entry point: `python -m mcp.macro_regime.runner --mode [check|deep|emergency] [--trigger-symbols BTC-USDC,ETH-USDC] [--output PATH] [--snapshot-path PATH] [--dry-run] [--verbose]`. `check` mode is the hourly tier: builds a fetcher, fetches a snapshot, runs the LightweightCheck. If no trigger fires → exit 0 with `Triggered: no` summary. If a trigger fires → escalates inline to the deep tier using the SAME snapshot (no double fetch) with `urgency="triggered"` and the trigger reasons threaded into the prompt. `deep` mode runs the full LLM assessment with `urgency="normal"`. `emergency` mode accepts `--trigger-symbols` and runs with `urgency="emergency"` plus the symbols + reasons in the prompt body — designed for the Task 6 swarm-triggered MacroReassessmentRequired handler. Lazy `_build_fetcher()` and `_build_llm_provider()` so `--help` doesn't pull in httpx/anthropic; tests monkeypatch both. Deep/emergency modes refuse to run without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (exit 2). The summary printers produce 72-char-wide blocks matching the spec example: `Regime: RISK_OFF (confidence: 0.82). 2 blackout window(s). Written to macro_regime.json`. Returns exit 1 when the deep run carries an error, 0 otherwise. Suitable for cron with the example lines from §13.2.1. **`__init__.py`** exports the public API (`MacroDataFetcher`, `MacroSnapshot`, `EconomicEvent`, `LightweightCheck`, `CheckResult`, `MacroRegimeManager`, `MacroRegime`, `MacroAdjustments`, `BlackoutWindow`). **Spec deviations to flag**: (1) The hardcoded calendar is small by design — only FOMC/CPI/NFP for known 2026 dates within a 30-day lookahead. We'd rather miss a low-impact event than fabricate timestamps for releases we can't reliably look up. A future task can layer a real calendar API (Forex Factory / Alpha Vantage) on top via the same `economic_calendar` field; the existing `MacroSnapshot` shape supports it without code changes. (2) The Hyperliquid funding aggregation is a simple arithmetic mean across markets — the spec says "aggregate" without specifying weighting. Volume-weighted would be more accurate but requires fetching candles per market, which would blow the 1s rate budget. Documented inline. (3) The LLM is told (in `SYSTEM_PROMPT`) to NEVER suggest blackout_windows in its JSON — windows are derived deterministically from the calendar. This is the §13.2 safety contract: the LLM picks the regime, the system picks the dates. Even if the LLM ignores the instruction and dumps a blackout list, it gets ignored — `_payload_to_regime` only reads `regime`, `confidence`, `reasoning`, and `adjustments`. (4) `position_size_multiplier` is clamped to [0.1, 2.0] post-LLM and `conviction_threshold_boost` is clamped to [0.0, 0.5]. The clamps are intentionally permissive on the safe side (small multiplier / large boost) and tight on the dangerous side. (5) Lightweight check returns trigger reasons as human-readable strings (e.g. `"VIX moved +7.50% (threshold ±5.0%)"`) rather than structured records — they're consumed by the prompt as urgency context, so the natural-language form is more useful than a parsed dict. (6) `macro_regime_manager` registered in `PROMPT_VERSIONS` at v1.0 (`quantagent/version.py`); engine version bumped to `2026.04.2.11.0-alpha.1`. (7) Drive-by fix: `tests/integration/test_migrations.py::TestSQLiteSchemaParity::test_trades_table_columns` was failing before this task started (Task 3 added the `forward_max_r` column to the trades table without updating this test's expected set). Added `"forward_max_r"` to the expected set as a one-line fix. **74 new tests** across 4 files. **`test_data_fetcher.py`** (14 tests): a `_FakeClient` shared infrastructure (URL-substring routes, get_calls/post_calls capture), happy-path fetch populates all 6 sources + calendar, partial failure (Yahoo VIX + CoinGecko down) keeps the rest with `errors` dict populated, total failure (every API down) returns calendar-only with all 6 errors, rate-limit `sleep_func` called exactly 5 times for 6 fetchers, zero rate limit skips sleep entirely, MacroSnapshot to_dict/from_dict round-trip preserves
